Sunnah Ghusl for Jumu'ah, 'Eid, Ihram, and 'Arafah
Ruling with proof: ghusl is sunnah for specific occasions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for Jumu'ah and similar occasions, cite the hadith evidence, and explain why it indicates sunnah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Ghusl for Jumu'ah is sunnah muakkadah—the Prophet's statement 'ghusl is better' proves recommendation, not obligation.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling on ghusl for specific occasions. While some may consider it obligatory, the Hanafi school holds it as a strongly recommended sunnah. The key evidence is a hadith that explicitly distinguishes between wudu (good) and ghusl (better). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the sunnah in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the text rules ghusl as sunnah for Friday, the two 'Eids, entering ihram, and standing at 'Arafah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
The Arabic verb 'sunn' indicates the legal category.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: from Samura (ra) narrated by multiple scholars, including al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
The hadith is classified hasan sahih.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze the wording: 'Whoever performs wudu... it is good; whoever performs ghusl, ghusl is better.' The explicit comparison shows ghusl is superior but not required.
The word 'afdal' (better) indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars considered ghusl for Jumu'ah wajib, but the Hanafi school and the majority hold it as sunnah based on this hadith.
The Hanafi position is confirmed by the practice of the salaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The hadith is sound (hasan sahih) and its clear wording supports the sunnah ruling. No contradictory evidence overrides it.
The tarjih authority is the mainstream Hanafi reliance on this transmitted proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رواية عبد الله قوله : (وسن للجمعة والعيدين والإحرام وعرفة أي وسن الغسل لأجل هذه الأشياء. وأما الجمعة فلما روى الترمذي وأبو داود النسائي وأحمد في مسنده والبيهقي في سننه وابن أبي شيبة في مصنفة وابن عبد البر في الاستذكار عن قتادة عن الحسن عن سمرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من توضأ يوم الجمعة فبها ونعمت ومن اغتسل فالغسل أفضل»(۱) قال الترمذي حديث حسن صحيح أي فبالسنة أخذ ونعمت هذه الخصلة، وقيل فبالرخصة أخذ
Narration of 'Abdullah. His saying: 'And it is sunnah for Friday, the two 'Eids, ihram, and 'Arafah' meaning ghusl is sunnah for these things. As for Friday, because al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ahmad in his Musnad, al-Bayhaqi in his Sunan, Ibn Abi Shaybah in his Musannaf, and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr in al-Istidhkar narrated from Qatada from al-Hasan from Samura who said: The Messenger of Allah (s) said: 'Whoever performs wudu on Friday, it is good and fine; and whoever performs ghusl, ghusl is better.' Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih hadith. Meaning he took the sunnah and fine is this characteristic; and it was said he took the concession.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling statement with proof that ghusl is sunnah for Friday, the two 'Eids, entering ihram, and standing at 'Arafah. The evidence for Friday is a hadith from Samura (ra) that wudu on Friday is good, but ghusl is better, indicating that ghusl is not obligatory but recommended (sunnah). The author also notes that al-Tirmidhi classified the hadith as hasan sahih. The phrase 'fahia wa ni'mat' is interpreted as indicating that wudu is a valid sunnah, while ghusl is superior.

Key Terms
سن (sunnah): A recommended act; performing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
أفضل (afdal): Better, superior. Indicates preference but not necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is ghusl for Jumu'ah considered sunnah and not wajib?
A) Because the hadith does not mention ghusl.
B) Because the hadith says 'ghusl is better' (afdal), which indicates recommendation.
C) Because only wudu is recommended for Friday.
D) Because the Hanafi school rejects all hadith on this topic.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl for Friday, Eid, ihram, and Arafah is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, based on the Prophet's words 'ghusl is better.'

Friday Ghusl: Sunnah or Wajib? The Hanafi Position
Defending the sunnah status of Friday ghusl and refuting the Zahiri claim of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Friday ghusl is sunnah mu'akkadah and evaluate the Zahiri counter-argument using the three responses.

Core Idea
Friday ghusl is sunnah, not wajib—the imperative is overridden by contextual evidence from the Prophet's own practice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends the Hanafi position that Friday ghusl is an emphasized sunnah, not an obligation. The author refutes the Zahiri school's claim of obligation by citing the Hadith of Samurah and providing three detailed responses to the opposing proofs. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in interpreting legal imperatives (amr) in the presence of contextualizing evidence (qarinah).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules Friday ghusl as sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended), not wajib.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that the Zahiri school (and some mistakenly attribute it to Malik) holds Friday ghusl is wajib.
The author denies it was ever the Maliki position.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyze the Hadith of Samurah: 'Whoever performs wudu on Friday, it is good; whoever performs ghusl, ghusl is better.' The comparative 'better' indicates recommendation, not obligation.
This hadith is the primary dalil for sunnah.
4
Analyze the opposing proof
Review the hadiths of Umar and al-Khudri that use imperatives and explicit 'wajib', which the Zahiris use to claim obligation.
Understand why these appear to indicate obligation at first glance.
5
Work through the three Hanafi responses
Study each response: (1) abrogation rejected due to lack of date; (2) context-specific command for a time of hardship; (3) the imperative is interpreted as nadb because it is associated with non-obligatory acts (siwak, perfume).
Each response undermines the claim of obligation.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Conclude that the practical difference is whether omitting ghusl incurs sin. Hanafi: no sin; Zahiri: sin.
This clarifies the real-world impact of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وسن للجمعة والعيدين والإحرام وعرفة أي وسن الغسل لأجل هذه الأشياء. وأما الجمعة فلما روى الترمذي وأبو داود النسائي وأحمد في مسنده والبيهقي في سننه وابن أبي شيبة في مصنفة وابن عبد البر في الاستذكار عن قتادة عن الحسن عن سمرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من توضأ يوم الجمعة فبها ونعمت ومن اغتسل فالغسل أفضل قال الترمذي حديث حسن صحيح أي فبالسنة أخذ ونعمت هذه الخصلة، وقيل فبالرخصة أخذ مخالف له بل راجع إلى القول الأول وحاصله أن كل ناقض موجب لحكمه إلا أنه اكتفى بوضوء واحد. ولا يلزم منه أن يقال به في كل موضع تعددت فيه العلل لحكم واحد لأنه يلزم عليه رفع وقوعها كذلك مع أن الأصوليين أثبتوه، ولا يخفى أن ما ذكره عن الفتح من أن الحدث واحد لا تعدد في أسبابه ينفي ما ذكره وكان الذي حمله على ذلك ما قدمه من مسألة الحنث فإنها تقتضي تعدد الحكم لكن المحقق في فتح القدير قد أجاب عن ذلك فقال : والحق أن لا تنافي بين كون الحدث بالسبب الأول فقط وبين الحنث لأنه لا يلزم بناؤه على تعدد الحدث بل على العرف، والعرف أن يقال ونعمت الخصلة هذه والأول أولى فإنه قال وإذا اغتسل فالغسل أفضل فتبين أن الوضوء سنة لا رخصة كذا في الطلبة والضمير في فبها يعود إلى غير المذكور وهو جائز إذا كان مشهوراً وهذا مذهب جمهور العلماء وفقهاء الأمصار وهو المعروف من مذهب مالك وأصحابه، وما وقع في الهداية من أنه واجب عند مالك فقال بعض الشارحين : إنه غير صحيح فإنه لم يقل أحد بالوجوب إلا أهل الظاهر وتمسكوا بما رواه البخاري ومسلم من حديث عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من جاء منكم الجمعة فليغتسل والأمر للوجوب. وروى البخاري ومسلم من حديث الخدري أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم وقد أجاب الجمهور عنه بثلاثة أجوبة : أحدها أن الوجوب قد كان ونسخ ودفع بأن الناسخ وإن صححه الترمذي لا يقوي قوة حديث الوجوب ما ليس فيه تاريخ أيضاً فعند التعارض يقدّم الموجب. ثانيها أنه من قبيل انتهاء الحكم بانتهاء علته كما يفيده ما أخرجه أبو داود عن عكرمة أن ناساً من أهل العراق جاءوا فقالوا يا ابن عباس أترى الغسل يوم الجمعة واجباً؟ فقال : لا ولكنه طهور وخير لمن اغتسل ومن لم يغتسل فلا شيء عليه بواجب، وسأخبركم كيف بدأ الغسل كان الناس مجهودين يلبسون الصوف ويعملون على ظهورهم وكان مسجدهم ضيقاً مقارب السقف إنما هو عريش، فخرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في يوم حار وعرق الناس في الصوف حتى ثارت منه رياح حتى أذى بعضهم بعضاً، فلما وجد عليه السلام تلك الرياح قال : يا أيها الناس، إذا كان هذا اليوم فاغتسلوا وليمس أحدكماً مثل ما يجد من دهنه وطيبه . قال ابن عباس : ثم جاء الله بالخير ولبسوا غير الصوف وكفوا العمل ووسع مسجدهم وذهب بعض الذي كان يؤذي بعضهم بعضاً من العرق وثالثها أن المراد بالأمر النسب وبالوجوب الثبوت شرعاً على وجه الندب كأنه قال واجب في الأخلاق الكريمة وحسن السنة بقرينة متصلة ومنفصلة. أما المتصلة فهي أنه قرنه بما لا يجب اتفاقاً كما رواه مسلم في حديث الخدري إنه عليه السلام قال غسل الجمعة على كل محتلم والسواك والطيب ما يقدر عليه ومعلوم أن الطيب والسواك ليسا بواجبين فكذلك الغسل، وأما قول أبي هريرة كغسل الجنابة فإنما أراد التشبيه في الهيئة والكيفية لا في كونه فرضاً يدل عليه ما رواه الترمذي عن أحمد ذلك
He said: (And it is sunnah for Friday, the two Eids, Ihram, and Arafah) i.e., ghusl is sunnah for these things. As for Friday, because of what al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ahmad in his Musnad, al-Bayhaqi in his Sunan, Ibn Abi Shaybah in his Musannaf, and Ibn Abd al-Barr in al-Istidhkar narrated from Qatadah from al-Hasan from Samurah, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Whoever performs wudu on Friday, it is good and excellent, and whoever performs ghusl, ghusl is better.' Al-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is hasan sahih. That is, he adopted the sunnah, and how excellent is this characteristic. And it is said: he adopted a concession (rukhsah) contrary to that, but it returns to the first saying. The gist of it is that every nullifier of wudu necessitates its renewal, but he was content with a single wudu. This does not necessitate that it be said in every instance where multiple causes for a single ruling exist, because that would necessitate removing their occurrence similarly, while the scholars of usul have affirmed it. It is not hidden that what he mentioned from al-Fath, that the hadath (ritual impurity) is one, there is no multiplicity in its causes, negates what he mentioned. What prompted him to that is what he previously presented regarding the issue of oath-breaking, for it requires multiplicity of rulings. But the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir answered that, saying: The truth is that there is no contradiction between the hadath being only from the first cause and the oath-breaking, because it is not necessary to build it upon multiplicity of hadath, but rather upon custom. And custom is that it is said: 'how excellent is this characteristic.' The first is better, for he said, 'And if he performs ghusl, ghusl is better.' Thus it becomes clear that wudu is sunnah, not a concession. So it is in al-Talibah. The pronoun in 'fiha' refers to something unmentioned, which is permissible if it is well-known. This is the madhhab of the majority of scholars and the jurists of the regions, and it is the known madhhab of Malik and his companions. What occurred in al-Hidayah that it is wajib according to Malik, some commentators said: it is not correct, for no one said it is wajib except the Zahiris. They clung to what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from the hadith of Umar, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Whoever among you comes to Friday, let him perform ghusl.' The imperative form indicates obligation. And al-Bukhari and Muslim also narrated from the hadith of al-Khudri that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Ghusl on Friday is obligated upon every person who has reached puberty.' The majority of scholars answered these with three answers: First: That obligation existed but was abrogated. This is refuted because the abrogator, even if authenticated by al-Tirmidhi, does not match the strength of the hadith of obligation, especially since there is no date; in case of conflict, the obligating hadith is given precedence. Second: That it is of the type where the ruling ends with the end of its cause, as indicated by what Abu Dawud narrated from Ikrimah that some people from Iraq came and said: O Ibn Abbas, do you consider ghusl on Friday obligatory? He said: No, but it is purification and good for whoever performs ghusl, and whoever does not perform ghusl, nothing is obligatory upon him. I will inform you how ghusl began: The people were struggling, wearing wool and working on their backs, their mosque was narrow and low-ceilinged, merely a canopy. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out on a hot day, and the people sweated in the wool until an odor arose, bothering each other. When he (peace be upon him) perceived that odor, he said: O people, when this day comes, perform ghusl, and let each one apply whatever he finds of his perfume and oil. Ibn Abbas said: Then Allah brought prosperity, and they wore other than wool, were relieved of labor, their mosque was expanded, and the sweat that had bothered them disappeared. Third: That the imperative (amr) is meant for recommended emphasis (nadb), and the word 'wajib' means established (thabit) in the Shari'ah in the sense of being recommended. It is as if he said: It is obligatory in noble character and good sunnah, indicated by connected and disconnected evidence. The connected evidence is that he (peace be upon him) associated it with what is undisputedly not obligatory, as Muslim narrated in the hadith of al-Khudri that he (peace be upon him) said, 'Ghusl on Friday is upon every pubescent person, and using siwak and perfume to the extent possible.' It is known that perfume and siwak are not obligatory, so likewise ghusl. As for the saying of Abu Hurayrah, 'like ghusl from janabah,' he only meant comparison in form and manner, not in being obligatory. This is indicated by what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ahmad that.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement that ghusl is sunnah for Friday, the two Eids, Ihram, and Arafah. The author focuses primarily on Friday, presenting the Hanafi position that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended) and not wajib. The discussion includes a detailed refutation of the claim that Friday ghusl is obligatory, attributed to the Zahiri school (the author denies it was the Maliki position). The author provides three arguments: (1) The hadith of Samurah clearly states that wudu suffices and that ghusl is better, indicating preference not obligation. (2) The apparent imperative in other hadiths is either abrogated (though the author rejects this due to lack of date) or was context-specific, as explained by Ibn Abbas—the command was given because people were sweating in wool, but after conditions improved, the obligation ceased. (3) The imperative in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) due to the accompanying evidence: in the same hadith, the Prophet mentioned siwak and perfume, which are unanimously non-obligatory; thus ghusl is also non-obligatory. The author also addresses a subtle point about the pronoun 'fiha' and the meaning of 'wajib' as 'thabit' (established) rather than 'obligatory'. Overall, the Hanafi position is that Friday ghusl is a stressed sunnah, not an obligation, and this is the view of the majority of scholars.

Key Terms
سن (sunnah): A recommended act established by the Prophet’s practice; omitting it is not sinful but is regarded as a loss of reward.
الغسل (al-ghusl): The ritual washing of the entire body; here specifically for Friday and other occasions.
واجب (wajib): In this context, some interpret it as 'established' (thabit) rather than obligatory; the Hanafi school distinguishes between fard (absolute obligation) and wajib (lesser obligation based on speculative evidence).
أمر (amr): An imperative verb form; in principles of jurisprudence, amr indicates obligation unless there is a counter-indication making it recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the ruling on performing ghusl before Friday prayer?
A) Fard (obligatory).
B) Wajib (necessary).
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended).
D) Mubah (permissible but not recommended).

Key Takeaway
Friday ghusl is an emphasized sunnah in the Hanafi school, not an obligation, because the imperative in the hadith is overridden by contextual evidence and the explicit wording of the Samurah hadith.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Friday Ghusl: Sunnah, Not Wajib
Establishes Hanafi ruling as sunnah and refutes opposing evidences for wujub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Friday ghusl and evaluate the three proofs used to refute its obligation.

Core Idea
Friday ghusl is sunnah, not wajib — the command was for a specific cause that ceased.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author establishes the Hanafi position that performing ghusl for Friday is a highly recommended sunnah, not an obligation. He then engages with the Zahiri argument for wujub, providing three detailed responses. Understanding this dispute teaches you how Hanafi scholars handle apparently authoritative commands that conflict with other evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the ruling and note its basis: 'sunnah muakkadah' from the majority of scholars.
The author attributes this to 'the majority of scholars and the jurists of the provinces'.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The Zahiris hold it wajib; their main proof is the hadith 'Ghusl on Friday is wajib upon every pubescent person' (Bukhari, Muslim).
The command 'فليغتسل' is taken as literal obligation.
3
Examine the first Hanafi response (abrogation)
The obligation might have existed but was abrogated. However, the abrogator is weak and undated, so this response is not preferred.
The author notes that the Zahiris give precedence to the obligating hadith due to lack of abrogation proof.
4
Examine the second Hanafi response (cause cessation)
The command was tied to a specific cause (body odor from wool and work) which later disappeared. Hence the ruling ended with its cause.
Ibn Abbas narrates the historical context: when conditions improved, the obligation lifted.
5
Examine the third Hanafi response (qarina for recommendation)
The word 'wajib' is interpreted as 'recommended' because the hadith couples ghusl with siwak and perfume, which are not wajib by consensus. This connected qarina shows the command is for recommendation.
An separate qarina: the hadith 'Whoever performs ghusl, then ghusl is better' indicates that wudu suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونعمت الخصلة هذه والأول أولى فإنه قال وإذا اغتسل فالغسل أفضل فتبين أن الوضوء سنة لا رخصة كذا في الطلبة والضمير في فبها» يعود إلى غير المذكور وهو جائز إذا كان مشهوراً وهذا مذهب جمهور العلماء وفقهاء الأمصار وهو المعروف من مذهب مالك وأصحابه، وما وقع في الهداية من أ أنه واجب عند مالك فقال بعض الشارحين : إنه غير صحيح فإنه لم يقل أحد بالوجوب إلا أهل الظاهر وتمسكوا بما رواه البخاري ومسلم من حديث عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من جاء منكم الجمعة فليغتسل) (۱) والأمر للوجوب. وروى البخاري ومسلم من حديث الخدري أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم»(۲) وقد أجاب الجمهور عنه بثلاثة أجوبة : أحدها أن الوجوب قد كان ونسخ ودفع بأن الناسخ وإن صححه الترمذي لا يقوي قوة حديث الوجوب ما ليس فيه تاريخ أيضاً فعند التعارض يقدّم الموجب. ثانيها أنه من قبيل انتهاء الحكم بانتهاء علته كما يفيده ما أخرجه أبو داود عن عكرمة أن ناساً من أهل العراق جاءوا فقالوا يا ابن عباس أترى الغسل يوم الجمعة واجباً؟ فقال : لا ولكنه طهور وخير لمن اغتسل ومن لم يغتسل فلا شيء عليه بواجب، وسأخبركم كيف بدأ الغسل كان الناس مجهودين يلبسون الصوف ويعملون على ظهورهم وكان مسجدهم ضيقاً مقارب السقف إنما هو عريش، فخرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في يوم حار وعرق الناس في الصوف حتى ثارت منه رياح حتى أذى بعضهم بعضاً، فلما وجد عليه السلام تلك الرياح قال : يا أيها الناس، إذا كان هذا اليوم فاغتسلوا وليمس أحدكماً مثل ما يجد من دهنه وطيبه . قال ابن عباس : ثم جاء الله بالخير ولبسوا غير الصوف وكفوا العمل ووسع مسجدهم وذهب بعض الذي كان يؤذي بعضهم بعضاً من العرق وثالثها أن المراد بالأمر النسب وبالوجوب الثبوت شرعاً على وجه الندب كأنه قال واجب في الأخلاق الكريمة وحسن السنة بقرينة متصلة ومنفصلة. أما المتصلة فهي أنه قرنه بما لا يجب اتفاقاً كما رواه مسلم في حديث الخدري إنه عليه السلام قال غسل الجمعة على كل محتلم والسواك والطيب ما يقدر عليه» ومعلوم أن الطيب والسواك ليسا بواجبين فكذلك الغسل، وأما قول أبي هريرة «كغسل الجنابة» فإنما أراد التشبيه في الهيئة والكيفية لا في كونه فرضاً يدل عليه ما رواه الترمذي عن أبي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من توضأ فأحسن الوضوء ثم أتى الجمعة فدنا واستمع وأنصت غفر له ما بينه وبين الجمعة وزيادة ثلاثة أيام، ومن مس الحصى فقد لغا»(۱) وهذا نص في الاكتفاء بالوضوء. وأما القرينة المنفصلة فهي قوله ومن اغتسل فالغسل أفضل».
And this is a good characteristic, and the first is more appropriate, for he said: 'And if he performs ghusl, then ghusl is better.' So it becomes clear that wudu is sunnah, not a concession. Likewise in al-Tulbah. And the pronoun in 'fiha' refers to something not mentioned, and that is permissible if it is well-known. This is the madhhab of the majority of scholars and the jurists of the provinces, and it is the well-known madhhab of Malik and his companions. And what occurred in al-Hidayah that it is obligatory according to Malik, some commentators said: it is not correct, for no one said obligation except the Zahiris, and they clung to what Bukhari and Muslim narrated from the hadith of Umar that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'Whoever among you comes to Friday, let him perform ghusl' – and the command is for obligation. And Bukhari and Muslim narrated from the hadith of al-Khudri that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person.' And the majority answered it with three answers: First, that obligation was and then abrogated, and it is countered that the abrogator, even if al-Tirmidhi authenticated it, does not have the strength of the hadith of obligation, and it also lacks a date, so when they conflict, the obligator is given precedence. Second, that it is of the type of termination of a ruling by termination of its cause, as indicated by what Abu Dawud narrated from Ikrimah that some people from Iraq came and said: O Ibn Abbas, do you consider ghusl on Friday obligatory? He said: No, but it is purification and good for the one who performs ghusl, and the one who does not perform ghusl has no sin that is obligatory. And I will inform you how ghusl began. The people were struggling, wearing wool and working on their backs, and their mosque was narrow, low-ceilinged, only a shelter. So the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) went out on a hot day, and the people sweated in the wool until a smell arose from it, bothering one another. When he (PBUH) sensed that smell, he said: O people, when this day comes, perform ghusl, and let each one of you apply whatever he finds of his oil and perfume. Ibn Abbas said: Then Allah brought good, and they wore other than wool, ceased work, their mosque was expanded, and some of the harm that one caused another from sweat disappeared. Third, that what is meant by 'command' is recommendation, and by 'obligatory' is established legally in a recommended manner, as if he said: obligatory in noble character and good sunnah, with a connected and separate qarina. As for the connected, it is that he associated it with what is not obligatory by agreement, as Muslim narrated in the hadith of al-Khudri that he (PBUH) said: 'Ghusl on Friday is upon every pubescent person, and siwak and perfume as much as he can' – and it is known that perfume and siwak are not obligatory, so likewise ghusl. And as for the saying of Abu Hurairah 'like ghusl from janabah,' he only intended similarity in form and manner, not in it being fard. This is indicated by what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Whoever performs wudu and does it well, then comes to Friday, draws near, listens, and remains silent, will have his sins between that Friday and the next forgiven, plus three days, and whoever touches pebbles has engaged in idle talk.' This is explicit text regarding sufficiency of wudu. As for the separate qarina, it is his saying: 'And whoever performs ghusl, then ghusl is better.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that ghusl for Friday is sunnah, not wajib. The author begins by affirming that the preferred position is that wudu suffices and ghusl is better. He attributes this to the majority of scholars and jurists, including the well-known position of Imam Malik. He then refutes the apparent view of the Zahiris who hold it wajib based on hadiths of command. Three responses are given: (1) the obligation was abrogated, (2) the command was for a specific cause that later ceased [the smell of sweat], and (3) the command is interpreted as recommendation due to accompanying qarinas (like mentioning siwak and perfume which are not wajib). The passage uses both textual evidence and reasoned argument.

Key Terms
غسل الجمعة (ghusl al-jumu'ah): The ritual bath taken specifically for Friday prayer
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation, a ruling that requires performance and renders one sinful for omission

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ghusl for Friday?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Friday ghusl as sunnah due to contextual evidence, refuting the Zahiri claim of obligation with three responses.

Ghusl for Eid and Ihram is Sunnah
Cites hadith evidence and analogy to establish sunnah for ghusl on Eid, Arafah, and ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for Eid, Arafah, and ihram, and cite the hadith evidence and analogy that establish it as sunnah.

Core Idea
Ghusl for Eid, Arafah, and ihram is sunnah, established by Prophetic practice and analogy from Friday ghusl.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the evidence for ghusl on the two Eids, the day of Arafah, and before entering ihram. The author cites multiple hadiths, discusses their authenticity, and concludes that the ruling is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory. The discussion also includes an analogy to Friday ghusl and addresses the methodological principle that consistent practice (muwazabah) is required for establishing sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts under discussion
List the occasions for which ghusl is being considered: Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, day of Arafah, and before ihram.
2
Find the primary hadith evidence
Locate the hadith from Ibn Majah that describes the Prophet's practice of ghusl on these days.
The hadith is also narrated by Tabarani and Bazzar with an addition for Friday.
3
Assess the authenticity of narrations
The author notes that some narrations about Eid and Arafah are weak, but the ruling is supported by stronger evidence.
4
Understand the analogy (qiyas) from Friday ghusl
The author uses an analogy: just as Friday ghusl is sunnah (after abrogation of its obligation), so too are the ghusls for Eid, Arafah, and ihram.
The illa is the shared characteristic of being a recommended purification for a significant occasion.
5
Conclude the ruling
The evidence, including the hadith of Aishah on the four ghusls, establishes that consistent practice (muwazabah) is present, so the ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
Some Hanafi scholars considered it mustahabb, but the relied-upon position is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما كون الغسل سنة للعيدين وعرفة فبما رواه ابن ماجه في سننه عن أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يغتسل يوم الفطر ويوم النحر ويوم عرفة، ورواه الطبراني في معجمه والبزار في مسنده وزاد فيه يوم الجمعة، ورواه أحمد في مسنده أيضاً وروى ابن ماجه عن ابن عباس قال: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يغتسل يوم العيدين. وأما كونه سنة للإحرام فيما أخرجه الترمذي في الحج وحسنه عن خارجة بن زيد بن ثابت عن أبيه زيد بن ثابت أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم تجرد لإهلاله واغتسل وذهب بعض مشايخنا إلى أن هذه الأغسال الأربعة مستحبة من قول محمد في الأصل إن غسل الجمعة حسن. قال في فتح القدير : وهو النظر لأنا إن قلنا بأن الوجوب انتسخ لا يبقى حكم آخر بخصوصه إلا بدليل والدليل المذكور يفيد الاستحباب، وكذا إن قلنا بأنه من قبيل انتهاء الحكم بانتهاء علته وإن حملنا الأمر على الندب فدليل الندب يفيد الاستحباب إذ لا سنة دون مواظبته وليس ذلك لازم الندب ثم يقاس عليه باقي الأغسال، وإنما يتعدى إلى الفرع حكم الأصل وهو الاستحباب. وأما ما رواه ابن ماجه في العيدين وعرفة من حديثي الفاكه وابن عباس المتقدم ذكرهما فضعيفان قاله النووي وغيره. وأما ما رواه الترمذي في الإهلال فواقعة حال لا تستلزم المواظبة فاللازم الاستحباب إلا أن يقال : إهلاله اسم جنس فيعم لفظاً كل إهلال صدر منه فثبتت سنية هذا الغسل ا هـ. لكن قال تلميذه ابن أمير حاج والذي يظهر استنان غسل الجمعة لما روي عن الله عائشة رضي عنها أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يغتسل من أربع من الجنابة ويوم الجمعة وغسل الميت ومن الحجامة . رواه أبو داود وصححه ابن خزيمة والحاكم وقال على شرط الشيخين. وقال البيهقي : رواته كلهم ثقاة. مع ما تقدم فإن هذا الحديث ظاهره يفيد المواظبة وما تقدم يفيد جواز الترك من غير لوم، وبهذا القدر تثبت السنة .
As for ghusl being sunnah for the two Eids and Arafah, it is based on what Ibn Majah narrated in his Sunan from... that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) used to perform ghusl on the day of Fitr, the day of Adha, and the day of Arafah. At-Tabarani and al-Bazzar also narrated it, adding Friday. Ahmad also narrated it. Ibn Majah also narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) used to perform ghusl on the two Eids. As for it being sunnah for ihram, based on what at-Tirmidhi narrated in Hajj and classified as hasan from Kharjah ibn Zayd ibn Thabit from his father Zayd ibn Thabit that he saw the Prophet (PBUH) remove his clothes for his ihram and perform ghusl. Some of our shaykhs held that these four ghusls are mustahabb based on Muhammad's statement in al-Asl that ghusl on Friday is good. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This is the correct view, because if we say obligation was abrogated, no other specific ruling remains except by evidence, and the mentioned evidence indicates istihbab. Similarly, if we say it is of the type of termination of ruling by termination of its cause, and we interpret the command as recommendation, then evidence of recommendation indicates istihbab, for there is no sunnah without consistent practice, and that is not necessary for recommendation. Then the remaining ghusls are analogized to it, so the subsidiary takes the ruling of the original, which is istihbab. As for what Ibn Majah narrated about the two Eids and Arafah from the hadiths of al-Fakah and Ibn Abbas mentioned earlier, they are weak, according to al-Nawawi and others. As for what at-Tirmidhi narrated about ihram, it is a specific incident that does not imply consistent practice, so the necessary ruling is istihbab, unless it is said: 'Ihram' is a generic noun, so the wording includes every ihram that occurred from him, thus establishing sunnah for this ghusl. However, his student Ibn Amir Hajj said: What appears is the establishment of sunnah for Friday ghusl due to what was narrated from Aishah that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) used to perform ghusl from four: janabah, Friday, washing the deceased, and cupping. Abu Dawud narrated it, and Ibn Khuzaymah and al-Hakim authenticated it, saying it meets the conditions of the two shaykhs. Al-Bayhaqi said: All its narrators are trustworthy. Combined with what preceded, this hadith apparently indicates consistent practice, and what preceded indicates permissibility of leaving without blame, and to this extent sunnah is established.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage establishes that ghusl for Eid, Arafah, and ihram is sunnah. The author cites hadith evidence, noting that some narrations are weak but the ruling is supported by the practice of the Prophet and analogy from Friday ghusl. The discussion includes a methodological point from Fath al-Qadir that if the obligation of Friday ghusl was abrogated, the remaining evidence points to istihbab, and other ghusls are analogized to it. The ahadith about Aishah strongly support sunnah for Friday ghusl, and by extension for the others.

Key Terms
الغسل للعيدين (al-ghusl lil-'idayn): The ritual bath performed on the mornings of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, which begins with the intention and talbiyah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for Eid and Arafah?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Ghusl for Eid, Arafah, and ihram is sunnah in the Hanafi school, supported by Prophetic practice, hadith, and analogy from Friday ghusl.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Ghusl for the Day or the Prayer?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of sunnah ghusl for Friday and Eids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether ghusl for Friday and Eids is sunnah for the prayer or for the day, identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf), and apply the relied-upon position (Abu Yusuf) to real scenarios.

Core Idea
Ghusl on Friday and Eids is sunnah for the prayer, not for the day, per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Within the Hanafi school, a subtle but consequential dispute arises: is the sunnah ghusl for Friday and the two Eids attached to the prayer itself or to the day? Abu Yusuf ties it to the prayer, arguing the prayer is more virtuous than the time, while Hasan ibn Ziyad attaches it to the day to honour the day's virtue. This difference leads to several practical divergences.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core question: Is ghusl for Friday and Eids sunnah for the prayer or for the day?
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Hasan (or Muhammad in some rivayat).
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds it is sunnah for the prayer because the prayer is more virtuous than the time.
His reliance on the virtue of the prayer shapes the timing and conditions.
3
State Hasan's position and proof
Hasan holds it is sunnah for the day to manifest the virtue of the day itself.
This allows more flexibility in timing.
4
List the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
Three scenarios: (a) those not obligated for Friday, (b) ghusl followed by wudu, (c) ghusl after prayer before sunset.
Each scenario yields a different ruling under each opinion.
5
Determine the tarjih (relied-upon position)
Many Hanafi books state the correct position is that of Abu Yusuf, making ghusl sunnah for the prayer.
This is the mufta bihi for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلفوا فعند أبي يوسف الغسل في الجمعة والعيدين سنة للصلاة لا لليوم لأنها أفضل من الوقت، وعند الحس لليوم اظهاراً لفضيلته. وهكذا في كثير من الكتب وفي بعض الكتب كما نقله في المعراج ذكر محمد مكان الحسن وقالوا : الصحيح قول أبي يوسف. وتظهر ثمرة الاختلاف فيمن لا جمعة عليه هل يسن له الغسل أو لا، وفيمن اغتسل ثم أحدث وتوضأ وصلى به الجمعة لا يكون له فضل غسل الجمعة عند أبي يوسف خلافاً للحسن، وفيمن اغتسل بعد الصلاة قبل الغروب فعند أبي يوسف ،لا، وعند الحسن نعم. كذا
Then they differed: According to Abu Yusuf, ghusl on Friday and the two Eids is sunnah for the prayer, not for the day, because the prayer is more virtuous than the time. According to Hasan, it is for the day, to manifest its virtue. This is found in many books. In some books, as quoted in al-Mi'raj, Muhammad is mentioned in place of Hasan, and they said: The correct position is that of Abu Yusuf. The fruit of the difference appears: For the one upon whom Friday is not obligatory, is it sunnah for him to perform ghusl or not? And for the one who performed ghusl, then had an event, performed wudu, and prayed Friday with it, he does not attain the virtue of Friday ghusl according to Abu Yusuf, unlike Hasan. And for the one who performed ghusl after the prayer before sunset, according to Abu Yusuf no, but according to Hasan yes.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad (or Muhammad al-Shaybani according to some reports) regarding the nature of the sunnah of ghusl on Friday and Eids. Abu Yusuf considers it sunnah for the prayer specifically, meaning it is tied to the prayer and must be performed before the prayer. Hasan considers it sunnah for the day, so it can be done at any point during the day, and even after the prayer before sunset. The practical consequences are clearly outlined: (1) whether those not obligated for Friday (women, travelers) should still perform ghusl, (2) whether ghusl followed by wudu suffices for the virtue, and (3) timing after prayer. The correct position according to many is that of Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
سنة للصلاة (sunnat lil-salat): The sunnah is attached to the prayer, meaning it should be performed before the prayer
سنة لليوم (sunnat lil-yawm): The sunnah is attached to the day, meaning it can be performed anytime during the day

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, if someone performs ghusl for Friday, then has an event and performs wudu, then prays Friday with that wudu, do they attain the virtue of ghusl?
A) Yes
B) No

Key Takeaway
For ghusl on Friday and Eids, the relied-upon Hanafi view is that it is sunnah for the prayer, so it must be performed before the prayer to achieve its virtue.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ghusl for Jumu'ah: Timing and Hadath
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions for sunnah ghusl for Jumu'ah, 'Eid, and Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan regarding the conditions for attaining the sunnah of ghusl for Jumu'ah, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each view.

Core Idea
The sunnah of ghusl for Jumu'ah is lost if hadath intervenes according to Abu Yusuf, but not according to al-Hasan—the dispute hinges on whether the ghusl is for the prayer or the day.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a subtle but important intra-Hanafi dispute: what are the precise conditions for attaining the reward (thawab) of the sunnah ghusl for Jumu'ah? The two views, attributed to Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, disagree on two key points: the timing of the ghusl (before dawn or after dawn) and the effect of minor ritual impurity (hadath) occurring after the ghusl. Understanding this dispute not only clarifies the ruling for Friday prayer but also extends to ghusl for 'Eid and Arafah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Hukm
Determine the act being discussed: ghusl for Jumu'ah. Its hukm is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah). The dispute is not over obligation but over the conditions to earn its reward.
2
State Abu Yusuf's Position
Abu Yusuf holds that the ghusl is specifically for the prayer. It must be performed after dawn on Friday, and no hadath (minor impurity) may intervene between the ghusl and the prayer. If hadath occurs, the sunnah reward is lost.
3
State al-Hasan's Position
Al-Hasan holds that the ghusl is for the entire day of Jumu'ah, not solely the prayer. It must precede the prayer, but it can be performed even before dawn. Intervening hadath does not nullify the reward.
There are two narrations from al-Hasan: one allowing ghusl before dawn and one requiring it after dawn. The primary text follows the stricter view that before dawn does not earn the reward.
4
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Difference)
Consider the concrete scenario: if one performs ghusl before dawn and then prays Jumu'ah, Abu Yusuf grants the reward (since the ghusl is before the prayer), while al-Hasan does not (since the ghusl is not on the day itself after dawn). Similarly, if hadath occurs after ghusl, Abu Yusuf says the sunnah is lost, al-Hasan says it is not.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
The commentator (Ibn al-Humam) leans towards Abu Yusuf's view, citing the purpose of removing odor and the consensus that ghusl after prayer is invalid. Al-Zayla'i objects to al-Hasan's analogy, but the author rebuts that the object of ghusl (the day) can accommodate the ghusl, while the prayer cannot. Later authorities prefer Abu Yusuf's view as the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر الشارحون والمنقول في فتاوى قاضيخان في باب صلاة الجمعة أنه لو اغتسل بعد الصلاة لا يعتبر بالإجماع وهو الأولى فيما يظهر لي لأن سبب مشروعية هذا الغسل لأجل إزالة الأوساخ في بدن الإنسان اللازم منها حصول الأذى عند الاجتماع، وهذا المعنى لا يحصل بالغسل بعد الصلاة، والحسن رحمه الله وإن كان يقول هو لليوم لا للصلاة لكن بشرط أن يتقدم على الصلاة. ولا يضر تخلل الحدث بين الغسل والصلاة عنده وعند أبي يوسف يضر. وفي الكافي للمصنف وخلاصة الفتاوى تظهر فائدة الخلاف فيما لو اغتسل قبل الصبح وصلى به الجمعة نال فضل الغسل عند أبي يوسف، وعند الحسن لا. وتعقب الزيلعي الحسن بأنه مشكل جداً لأنه لا يشترط وجود الاغتسال بما سن الاغتسال لأجله وإنما يشترط أن يكون متطهراً بطهارة الاغتسال، ألا ترى أن أبا يوسف لا يشترط الاغتسال في الصلاة وإنما يشترط أن يصليها بطهارة الاغتسال، فكذا ينبغي أن يكون هنا متطهراً بطهارته في ساعة من اليوم عند الحسن لا أن ينشيء الغسل فيه ا هـ . وأقره عليه في فتح القدير . سن وقد يقال : إن ما استشهد به بقوله ألا ترى إلى آخره لا يصلح للاستشهاد لأن ما الاغتسال لأجله عند الحسن وهو اليوم يمكن إنشاء الغسل فيه، فلو قيل باشتراطه أمكن بخلاف ما سن الاغتسال لأجله عند أبي يوسف وهو الصلاة لا يمكن إنشاء الغسل فيها فافترقا، لكن المنقول في فتاوى قاضيخان من باب صلاة الجمعة أنه إن اغتسل قبل الصبح وصلى بذلك الغسل كانت صلاة بغسل عند الحسن. وفي معراج الدراية : لو اغتسل يوم الخميس أو ليلة الجمعة استن بالسنة لحصول المقصود وهو قطع الرائحة ا هـ . هـ. ولم ينقل خلافاً . وينبغي أن لا تحصل السنة عند أبي يوسف لاشتراطه أن لا يتخلل بين الغسل والصلاة حدث والغالب في مثل هذا القدر من الزمان حصول حدث بينهما، ولا تحصل السنة أيضاً عند الحسن على ما في الكافي وغيره. أما على ما في الكافي فظاهر، وأما على ما في غيره فلأنه يشترط أن يكون متطهراً بطهارة الاغتسال في اليوم لا قبله. ولو اتفق يوم الجمعة ويوم العيد أو عرفة وجامع ثم اغتسل ينوب عن الكل كذا في معراج الدراية . ثم في البدائع : يجوز أن يكون غسل عرفة على هذا الاختلاف أيضاً يعني أن يكون للوقوف أو لليوم كما في الجمعة. قال ابن أمير حاج والظاهر أنه للوقوف وما أظن أحداً ذهب إلى استنانه ليوم عرفة من غير حضور عرفات . وفي المنبع شرح المجمع : فإن قلت هل يتأتى هذا الاختلاف في غسل العيد أيضاً؟ قلت : يحتمل ذلك ولكني ما ظفرت به ا هـ . قلت : والظاهر أنه للصلاة أيضاً ويشهد له ما موطأ مالك عن نافع أن عبد الله بن عمر كان يغتسل يوم الفطر قبل أن يغدو ا هـ . وعبارة المجمع أولى من عبارة المصنف حيث قال : وفى عرفة ليبين أنه لا ينال السنة إلا إذا اغتسل في نفس الجبل بخلاف عبارة المصنف فإنها صادقة بما إذا اغتسل خارجه لأجله ثم دخله .
The commentators and what is transmitted in the Fatawa of Qadi Khan in the chapter of Friday prayer stated: If one performs ghusl after the prayer, it is not considered by consensus, and that is the preferable view in my opinion because the reason for the legislation of this ghusl is to remove dirt from the body of a person, which necessarily causes harm during gathering, and this meaning is not achieved by ghusl after the prayer. Al-Hasan (may Allah have mercy on him) says it is for the day, not for the prayer, but on condition that it precedes the prayer. Intervening hadath between ghusl and prayer does not harm according to him, while Abu Yusuf says it harms. In al-Kafi by the author and Khulasat al-Fatawa, the benefit of the dispute appears: if one performs ghusl before dawn and prays Friday with it, he attains the virtue of ghusl according to Abu Yusuf, but not according to al-Hasan. Al-Zayla'i objected to al-Hasan, saying it is very problematic because the presence of the ghusl for that for which ghusl is prescribed is not required; rather what is required is to be in a state of purity by the purity of ghusl. Do you not see that Abu Yusuf does not require the ghusl during the prayer but rather requires that he pray it with the purity of ghusl? Thus, it should be similar here: one should be pure by that purity at some hour of the day according to al-Hasan, not that he initiates the ghusl within it. End quote. And he approved it in Fath al-Qadir. 'Sin' and it may be said: The evidence he cited by his saying 'do you not see' etc. is not suitable as evidence because that for which ghusl is prescribed according to al-Hasan is the day, and it is possible to initiate the ghusl within it. If it were said that it is required, it is possible, unlike that for which ghusl is prescribed according to Abu Yusuf, which is the prayer, and it is impossible to initiate the ghusl within it, so they differ. But what is transmitted in the Fatawa of Qadi Khan from the chapter of Friday prayer is that if he performs ghusl before dawn and prays with that ghusl, it is considered prayer with ghusl according to al-Hasan. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: If one performs ghusl on Thursday or Thursday night, he follows the sunnah because the purpose is achieved, which is removing odor. End quote. And no disagreement is transmitted. It should be that the sunnah is not attained according to Abu Yusuf because he requires that no hadath intervene between the ghusl and the prayer, and generally in such a period of time hadath occurs between them. Nor is the sunnah attained according to al-Hasan based on what is in al-Kafi and others. As for what is in al-Kafi, it is apparent; as for what is in others, because he requires that one be pure by the purity of ghusl on the day, not before. If Friday coincides with 'Eid or Arafah, and one performs the ghusl once, it suffices for all. This is in Mi'raj al-Diraya. Then in al-Bada'i: It is permissible that ghusl for Arafah is subject to this same difference, meaning whether it is for the standing or for the day, as in Friday. Ibn Amir Hajj said: The apparent view is that it is for the standing, and I do not think anyone holds that it is sunnah for the day of Arafah without being present at Arafat. In al-Manba' Sharh al-Majma': If you say: Does this difference apply to ghusl for 'Eid as well? I say: It is possible, but I have not come across it. End quote. I say: The apparent view is that it is also for the prayer, as supported by what is in Muwatta' Malik from Nafi' that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar used to perform ghusl on the day of Fitr before going out. End quote. The expression of al-Majma' is better than the expression of the author where he said: 'And for Arafah' to indicate that one does not attain the sunnah unless he performs ghusl on the mountain itself, unlike the expression of the author, which applies even if he performs ghusl outside it for its sake and then enters it.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for attaining the reward (thawab) of the sunnah ghusl for Jumu'ah, 'Eid, and Arafah. The author, Ibn al-Humam, first cites from Fatawa Qadi Khan that if one performs ghusl after Jumu'ah prayer, it is not considered valid by consensus. The reasoning is that the purpose of this ghusl is to remove dirt and odor before gathering, which is not achieved after prayer. Al-Hasan (ibn Ziyad) holds that the ghusl is for the day, not specifically for the prayer, but it must precede the prayer. He also holds that intervening hadath (e.g., passing wind) between the ghusl and prayer does not nullify the virtue. Abu Yusuf, however, stipulates that no hadath should intervene, and he considers the ghusl to be for the prayer itself, not just the day. The practical difference emerges: if one performs ghusl before dawn (i.e., after Fajr?) and then prays Jumu'ah with it, Abu Yusuf grants the reward, while al-Hasan does not because the ghusl was not performed on the day of Jumu'ah? Actually, the text says 'before dawn' which is still Friday? This is clarified later: al-Zayla'i objects to al-Hasan's view, arguing that the requirement is not to perform ghusl at the moment of prayer but to be in a state of purity derived from that ghusl. He analogizes to Abu Yusuf's own view that one does not need to perform ghusl during the prayer but must pray with the purity attained from ghusl. The commentator then offers a rebuttal: the analogy fails because al-Hasan's object (the day) can accommodate the ghusl within it, whereas Abu Yusuf's object (the prayer) cannot. Then from Qadi Khan, there is a transmission that if one performs ghusl before dawn and prays with it, it is considered prayer with ghusl according to al-Hasan, implying two views from al-Hasan. The discussion continues with ghusl on Thursday night or Friday night, and the condition of no hadath intervening. The passage also covers the case when Jumu'ah, 'Eid, and Arafah coincide, where one ghusl suffices for all. For 'Eid and Arafah, the same difference applies: is the ghusl for the day or the specific act? Ibn Amir Hajj opines that ghusl for Arafah is for the standing (wuquf), not just the day, and he doubts anyone considers it sunnah for the day without being present. The author then cites Muwatta' Malik as evidence that ghusl for 'Eid is for the prayer, since Ibn 'Umar performed it before going to the prayer.

Key Terms
غسل الجمعة (ghusl al-jumu'ah): The ritual bath prescribed for Friday prayer, considered a sunnah mu'akkadah.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity (minor or major) that nullifies wudu or ghusl.
طهارة الاغتسال (taharat al-ightisal): The state of purity achieved by performing ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for attaining the sunnah of ghusl for Jumu'ah according to Abu Yusuf?
A) The ghusl must be performed on Thursday night.
B) The ghusl must be performed after dawn on Friday with no intervening hadath.
C) The ghusl is only for removing odor, so any time is fine.
D) The ghusl must be performed in the mosque before the khutbah.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of ghusl for Jumu'ah is attained only if performed before the prayer with no hadath intervening, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view (Abu Yusuf).

Ghusl of the Deceased: Communal Obligation and Intention
Expansion on obligation and intention for ghusl of deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of ghusl for the deceased as fard kifayah and explain why intention is required for the one performing the ghusl to discharge the obligation.

Core Idea
Washing the deceased is a communal obligation; intention is required to discharge the duty, not to purify the dead.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the legal status of washing the deceased. The commentator explains that the author's term 'obligated' means fard kifayah, supported by consensus. He also addresses two important sub-issues: the exceptional case of a hermaphrodite and the requirement of intention for the washer. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghusl al-mayyit (washing the deceased). The ruling is fard kifayah (communal obligation) – if some Muslims perform it, all are absolved; if none do, all sin.
The commentator emphasizes that the author's 'wajaba' means fard kifayah.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites consensus (ijma) as the proof, referencing Fath al-Qadir.
Ijma is a strong evidence (qat'i thubut).
3
Trace the role of intention
Intention is required for the person performing the ghusl to discharge the communal obligation, not to achieve purity of the deceased. It is also a condition for the validity of the funeral prayer over the deceased.
This distinguishes the ruling from simply cleaning the body.
4
Note the exception
For a deceased hermaphrodite with ambiguous genitalia, there is a dispute: some say tayammum, others say wash in clothes. The preferred view (al-awla) is tayammum.
Details will be discussed later in the funeral chapter.
5
Evaluate the weak opinion
The claim that ghusl of the deceased is a confirmed sunnah is dismissed after the transmission of consensus. Such a view is not considered and does not affect the consensus.
The author refutes this by asserting the strength of ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ووجب للميت) أي الغسل فرض على المسلمين على الكفاية لأجل الميت وهذا هو مراد المصنف من الوجوب كما صرح به في الوافي في الجنائز. وفي فتح القدير إنه بالإجماع إلا أن يكون الميت خنثى مشكلاً فإنه مختلف فيه قيل ييمم، وقيل يغسل في ثيابه والأول أولى وسيأتي في الجنائز إن شاء الله تعالى دليله وهل يشترط لهذا الغسل النية؟ الظاهر أنه يشترط لإسقاط وجوبه عن المكلف لا لتحصيل طهارته هو وشرط صحة الصلاة عليه كذا في فتح القدير ولنافيه نظر نذكره إن شاء الله في الجنائز . وما نقله مسكين من قوله وقيل غسل الميت سنة مؤكدة ففيه نظر بعد نقل الإجماع اللهم إلا أن يكون قولاً غير معتد به فلا يقدح في انعقاد الإجماع
His saying: 'And obligated for the deceased' means that ghusl is fard upon the Muslims as a communal obligation for the sake of the deceased. This is what the author means by obligation, as he stated in al-Wafi in the chapter of funerals. In Fath al-Qadir, it is by consensus except if the deceased is a hermaphrodite with ambiguity, then it is disputed: some say he should be given tayammum, others say he should be washed in his clothes, and the first is better. Its proof will come in funerals, Allah willing. And is intention required for this ghusl? The apparent view is that it is required to discharge the obligation from the responsible person, not to achieve the purity of the deceased himself, and it is a condition for the validity of prayer upon him. This is in Fath al-Qadir. Its negator has a view we will mention, Allah willing, in funerals. What Maskeen transmitted from his statement 'and it is said that ghusl of the deceased is a confirmed sunnah' is questionable after the transmission of consensus, unless it is a view not considered, which does not harm the formation of consensus.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the obligation of ghusl for the deceased. The commentator clarifies that the author's phrase 'obligated' means fard kifayah (communal obligation). He cites Fath al-Qadir that this is established by consensus (ijma). An exception is made for a hermaphrodite with ambiguous genitalia: there is a dispute whether to perform tayammum or wash in clothes; the preferred view is tayammum. The passage then addresses the requirement of intention (niyyah) for this ghusl. According to the relied-upon view, intention is necessary for the person performing the ghusl to discharge the communal obligation, not to purify the deceased. It is also a condition for the validity of the funeral prayer over the deceased. The commentator notes that there is a view (attributed to 'Maskeen') that it is a confirmed sunnah, but this is weak after the consensus. The text promises further discussion in the funeral section.

Key Terms
غسل الميت (ghusl al-mayyit): The ritual washing of a deceased Muslim's body before burial.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform the ghusl for the sake of discharging the obligation.
الخنثى المشكل (al-khuntha al-mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose sex is ambiguous, leading to a special ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal status of washing the deceased according to the majority of Hanafi scholars as stated in this passage?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib on every individual (fard 'ayn)
C) Fard kifayah (communal obligation)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Ghusl of the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), and intention is required for the washer to discharge the duty, not to purify the deceased.

Ghusl for a Disbeliever Who Becomes Muslim While Junub
Ruling that ghusl is obligatory for a disbeliever who becomes Muslim while in a state of janabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of ghusl for a new Muslim who was junub and explain the proof and the distinction with menstruation.

Core Idea
Janabah persists after Islam, making ghusl obligatory.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the obligation of ghusl for a disbeliever who accepts Islam while in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah). The commentator explains the linguistic shift that indicates obligation and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute by preferring the view that the continued state of janabah demands purification. Additionally, a distinction is made with menstruation, where the impurity ceases naturally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a disbeliever becoming Muslim while junub. The ruling is that ghusl is fard (obligatory), indicated by the lam being interpreted as 'upon'.
The phrase 'wa illa nudiba' confirms the obligation by contrast.
2
Understand the linguistic evidence
The lam in 'liman aslama junuban' is not literal, because the two cases (junub vs. not junub) are treated differently. It must mean 'upon' (='ala), indicating obligation.
This is a standard Hanafi interpretive technique for prepositions.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars said it is not obligatory because disbelievers are not addressed by subsidiary rulings and no new janabah occurs after Islam. This is a weak transmission.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school, not cross-madhhab.
4
Evaluate the stronger proof
The correct view (al-ashah) holds it is obligatory because the previous state of janabah persists after Islam. Since acts conditioned on purity (like prayer) cannot be performed without removing it, ghusl becomes fard.
This is supported by qiyas.
5
Distinguish the case of menstruation
A disbelieving woman who becomes Muslim after her period ends does not require ghusl, because menstruation ceases naturally and does not persist like janabah.
Shams al-A'immah is cited for this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولمن أسلم جنباً وإلا ندب أي افترض الغسل على من أسلم حال كونه جنباً فاللام بمعنى «على بقرينة قوله وإلا ندب إذ لو كانت اللام على حقيقتها لاستوت الحالتان كما لا يخفى وعبارة أصله الوافي أحسن ولفظه وندب لمن أسلم ولم يكن جنباً وإلا لزم» وقد اختلف المشايخ في الكافر إذا أسلم وهو جنب؛ فقيل لا يجب لأنهم غير مخاطبين بالفروع ولم يوجد بعد الإسلام جنابة وهو رواية وفي رواية يجب وهو الأصح لبقاء صفة الجنابة السابقة بعد الإسلام فلا يمكنه أداء المشروط بزوالها إلا به فيفترض ولو حاضت الكافرة فطهرت ثم أسلمت قال شمس الأئمة : لا غسل عليها بخلاف الجنب والفرق أن صفة الجنابة باقية بعد الإسلام
His saying: 'And for one who becomes Muslim while junub, otherwise it is recommended' means that ghusl is fard for one who becomes Muslim while in the state of janabah. So the lam is in the sense of 'upon' by the context of his saying 'otherwise it is recommended'; if the lam were in its literal sense, the two cases would be equal, as is obvious. The expression of his original al-Wafi is better, and its wording: 'It is recommended for one who becomes Muslim if he was not junub, and if he was, it is required.' The scholars differed regarding a disbeliever who becomes Muslim while junub: some said it is not obligatory because disbelievers are not addressed by subsidiary rulings and no janabah occurs after Islam – this is one transmission. In another transmission, it is obligatory, which is the more correct view, because the previous description of janabah persists after Islam, so he cannot perform what is conditioned upon it except by its removal, so it becomes fard. If a disbelieving woman menstruates, then becomes pure, then becomes Muslim, Shams al-A'immah said: no ghusl is required for her, unlike the junub. The difference is that the description of janabah persists after Islam.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the obligation of ghusl for a disbeliever who accepts Islam while in a state of janabah (major impurity). The commentator interprets the author's phrase 'and for one who becomes Muslim while junub' with the lam meaning 'upon' (i.e., it is obligatory). The alternate case ('otherwise it is recommended') confirms this: if the person becomes Muslim without janabah, ghusl is only recommended (mustahabb). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: a weak view says it is not obligatory because the disbeliever was not addressed by the obligation of ghusl and after Islam, he is not in a state of janabah. However, the correct view (as preferred by the later scholars) is that it is obligatory because the state of janabah continues after embracing Islam. The obligation arises because ritual acts that require purity (like prayer) are conditioned upon removing janabah. The passage distinguishes the case of a menstruating woman: if she becomes Muslim after her period ends, she does not need ghusl because the state of menstruation (hayd) ends with its cessation, unlike janabah which remains until ghusl. This ruling is attributed to Shams al-A'immah (al-Sarakhsi).

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl.
الحائض (al-ha'id): A menstruating woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a disbeliever who becomes Muslim while in a state of janabah?
A) Ghusl is recommended but not obligatory.
B) Ghusl is obligatory because the state of janabah persists.
C) Ghusl is not required because disbelievers are not addressed.
D) Only tayammum is required.

Key Takeaway
For a new Muslim who was junub, ghusl is obligatory because the state of janabah continues after Islam.

Ghusl for Eid and Arafah: For the Day or the Prayer?
Explains different views on whether ghusl on Eid and Arafah is for the day or the prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the occasion of ghusl on Eid and Arafah and distinguish between the view that it is for the day and the view that it is for the prayer.

Core Idea
Ghusl on Eid and Arafah is for the day itself, not just the prayer.

This lesson addresses a subtle but practically important intra-Hanafi dispute: is the recommended ghusl on the days of Arafah and the two Eids specifically for the standing at Arafat or the Eid prayer, or is it for the entire day due to its virtue? The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq contrasts the wordings of different Hanafi authorities and clarifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghusl on the day of Arafah and the two Eids. Its ruling is sunnah (recommended). The dispute is about the occasion: is it for the standing/prayer or for the day?
The hukm level is sunnah, not wajib.
2
State the two positions
Position 1 (preferred): it is for the day itself. Position 2 (some scholars and a narration from Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan): it is for the prayer only.
The wording of al-Majma‘ supports position 1, whereas the wording of Kanz al-Daqa’iq is ambiguous.
3
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The primary evidence for the day view is the practice of Ibn Umar (ghusl before going to the prayer) and the general joy of Eid. The passage also cites the testimony of Ibn Malik that the best day is Arafah.
The dalil is a hadith from Muwatta Malik.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a person takes ghusl outside Arafat intending the day, then enters Arafat, does he fulfill the sunnah? According to Kanz (ambiguous wording), yes; according to al-Majma‘, only if he takes ghusl on the mountain itself.
This affects the proper timing and place of ghusl.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that it is for the day itself, as stated explicitly by the author of al-Durar and supported by the majority. The narration from Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan is considered weak in this context.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the evidence and the clarity of the wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صح في حاج والظاهر أنه للوقوف وما أظن أحداً ذهب إلى استنانه ليوم عرفة من غير حضور عرفات . وفي المنبع شرح المجمع : فإن قلت هل يتأتى هذا الاختلاف في غسل العيد أيضاً؟ قلت : يحتمل ذلك ولكني ما ظفرت به ا هـ . قلت : والظاهر أنه للصلاة أيضاً ويشهد له ما موطأ مالك عن نافع أن عبد الله بن عمر كان يغتسل يوم الفطر قبل أن يغدو ا هـ . وعبارة المجمع أولى من عبارة المصنف حيث قال : وفى عرفة ليبين أنه لا ينال السنة إلا إذا اغتسل في نفس الجبل بخلاف عبارة المصنف فإنها صادقة بما إذا اغتسل خارجه لأجله ثم دخله . قال ابن أمير (حاج أي في الحلية على المنية. قال العلامة المقدسي في شرحه على نظم الكنز أقول : ولا يستبعد أن يقول أحد بسنتيه لليوم لفضيلته حتى لو حلف بطلاق امرأته في أفضل أيام العام تطلق يوم عرفة. ذكره ابن ملك في شرح المشارق. وقد وقع السؤال عن في هذه الأيام ودار بين الأقوام وكتب بعضهم بأفضلية يوم الجمعة والعقل بخلافه اهـ. قوله : قلت والظاهر أنه للصلاة أيضاً قال في النهر أقول في الدرر لمنلاخسر وما لفظه : ويسن ولعيد. فإن المصنف في شرحه : أعاد اللام لئلا يفهم كونه سنة لصلاة العيد، وهذا صريح في أنه لليوم فقط وذلك لأن السرور فيه عام فيندب فيه التنظيف لكل قادر عليه، صلى أم لا. اهـ. أقول: نقل القهستاني عن التحفة أن غسل العيدين فيه خلاف أبي يوسف والحسن .
It is correct in Hajj, and the apparent is that it is for the standing (wuquf). I do not think anyone went to it being sunnah for the day of Arafah without being present at Arafat. In al-Manba‘ Sharh al-Majma‘: If you say, does this difference occur in ghusl for Eid also? I say: it is possible, but I have not come across it. End quote. I say: the apparent is that it is for the prayer as well, as evidenced by what is in Muwatta Malik from Nafi‘ that Abdullah ibn Umar used to take a ghusl on the day of Fitr before going out. End quote. And the wording of al-Majma‘ is better than the wording of the author, because he said: 'and on Arafah' to indicate that the sunnah is only attained if he takes his ghusl on the mountain itself, unlike the author's wording which applies even if he takes ghusl outside for its sake then enters. Ibn Amir (Hajj) said in al-Hilya 'ala al-Munya: al-‘Allama al-Maqdisi said in his commentary on Nazm al-Kanz: I say: it is not far-fetched that one say it is sunnah for the day because of its virtue, so much so that if a man swore by divorce that he would divorce his wife on the best day of the year, she would be divorced on the day of Arafah. Ibn Malik mentioned it in Sharh al-Mashariq. There has been inquiry about these days and discussion among people, and some wrote that Friday is better, but the mind is contrary. End quote. He said: I say: the apparent is that it is for the prayer as well. In al-Nahr he said: I say in al-Durar li al-Munla Khisraw: it is sunnah for both Eids. The author in his commentary repeated the lam to avoid understanding it as sunnah for the Eid prayer, and this is explicit that it is for the day only, because joy is general on that day, so it is recommended for the capable person, whether he prays or not. End quote. I say: al-Qahistani narrated from al-Tuhfah that ghusl for the two Eids has a difference between Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq discusses the ruling of ghusl on the days of Arafah and the two Eids. The author initially states that the apparent view is that ghusl on Arafah is specifically for the standing (wuquf) at Arafat, not merely for the day itself. However, he then quotes a possibility that the same ikhtilaf could apply to Eid as well. He argues that the apparent view is that it is for the prayer, citing the practice of Ibn Umar (radiyallahu ‘anhu) from Muwatta Malik. The author prefers the wording of al-Majma‘ over that of the author of Kanz al-Daqa’iq, because it restricts the sunnah to those who perform ghusl on the mountain itself. Later, he clarifies that the difference between the two Eids is known: some scholars like Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan held different positions. The commentary clarifies that the sunnah is for the day itself due to general joy, not specifically for the prayer.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, a pillar of Hajj.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that is not obligatory but consistently practiced by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred Hanafi view regarding ghusl on the day of Eid?
A) It is only for those who pray the Eid prayer.
B) It is for the day itself, recommended for all capable persons.
C) It is obligatory.
D) It is prohibited for those not going to the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the sunnah ghusl on Eid and Arafah is for the day itself, not specifically for the prayer, based on the practice of Ibn Umar and the general joy of these days.

Ghusl for a Convert Who Was Junub
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghusl for a convert junub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on ghusl for a convert who was junub and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with its dalil.

Core Idea
A convert who was junub must perform ghusl because janabah is a persisting physical state.

What happens when a disbeliever embraces Islam while in a state of major impurity (janabah)? Does conversion wipe away the need for ghusl, or is it still obligatory? The Hanafi school has an internal difference on this, and the answer hinges on whether pre-Islamic acts are addressed and whether the state of janabah continues after Islam. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the stronger position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the exact fiqh question: Is ghusl obligatory for a disbeliever who becomes Muslim while junub? Note that the condition of janabah exists at the moment of conversion.
2
State the two Hanafi narrations
One narration says ghusl is not obligatory (because the kafir is not addressed by furu' before Islam, and after Islam no new janabah occurred). The other (more correct) says it is obligatory (because janabah is a physical state that persists).
The debate is within the school, not between madhahib.
3
Analyze the dalil for each side
For non-obligation: pre-Islamic acts are not legally binding (ghayr mukhatabin). For obligation: the attribute of janabah remains after Islam; it is a continuous state, not a new hadath. The convert cannot perform acts like prayer without removing it.
The argument for wujub is based on 'baqa' al-wasf' (persistence of the description).
4
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is obligation, as stated by Qadikhan and others. The asahh (more correct) narration supports wujub. The thamarah al-khilaf: if ghusl is not performed, are subsequent acts valid? According to the stronger view, they are invalid until ghusl is done.
Precaution (ihtiyat) also dictates obligation in all related cases.
5
Extend to analogous cases
Apply the principle to related scenarios: a disbelieving woman who menstruates before conversion, a boy who reaches puberty by wet dream, etc. The same reasoning – persistence of the state – governs.
Qadikhan extends obligation to all four cases for caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولمن أسلم جنباً وإلا ندب أي افترض الغسل على من أسلم حال كونه جنباً فاللام بمعنى «على بقرينة قوله وإلا ندب إذ لو كانت اللام على حقيقتها لاستوت الحالتان كما لا يخفى وعبارة أصله الوافي أحسن ولفظه وندب لمن أسلم ولم يكن جنباً وإلا لزم» وقد اختلف المشايخ في الكافر إذا أسلم وهو جنب؛ فقيل لا يجب لأنهم غير مخاطبين بالفروع ولم يوجد بعد الإسلام جنابة وهو رواية وفي رواية يجب وهو الأصح لبقاء صفة الجنابة السابقة بعد الإسلام فلا يمكنه أداء المشروط بزوالها إلا به فيفترض ولو حاضت الكافرة فطهرت ثم أسلمت قال شمس الأئمة : لا غسل عليها بخلاف الجنب والفرق أن صفة الجنابة باقية بعد الإسلام فكأنه أجنب بعده والانقطاع في الحيض هو السبب ولم يتحقق بعد فلذلك لو أسلمت حائضاً ثم طهرت وجب عليها الغسل. ولو بلغ الصبي بالاحتلام أو هي بالحيض قيل يجب عليها لا عليه فهذه أربعة فصول . قال قاضيخان والأحوط وجوب الغسل في الفصول كلها وفي فتح القدير : ولا نعلم خلافاً في وجوب الوضوء للصلاة إذا أسلم محدثاً، ولا معنى للفرق بين هاتين فإنه إن اعتبر حال البلوغ أوان انعقاد أهلية التكليف فهو كحال انعقاد العلة لا يجب عليهما وإن اعتبر أوان توجه الخطاب حتى ا اتحد زمانهما وجب عليهما، والحيض إما حدث أو يوجب حدثاً في رتبة حدث الجنابة كما سنحققه في بابه فوجب أن يتحد حكمه بالذي أسلم جنباً. وجوابه أن السبب في الحيض الانقطاع وثبوته بعد البلوغ لتحقق البلوغ بابتداء الحيض كيلا يثبت الانقطاع إلا وهي بالغة ا هـ . وهذا الجواب بعد تسليمه يصلح جواباً عما يرد على الفرق بين المرأة إذا بلغت بالحيض والصبي إذا بلغ بالاحتلام ولقائل أن يمنعه لما تقدم أن المختار أن السبب في وجوب الغسل على الحائض ليس الحيض ولا انقطاعه وإنما هو وجوب الصلاة، فحينئذ لا فرق بينهما والجواب الصحيح أن الصحيح وجوب الاغتسال على الصبي إذا بلغ بالاحتلام ذكره في معراج الدراية معزياً إلى أمالي قاضيخان وأما ما يرد على الفرق بين المرأة الحائض إذا أسلمت بعد الانقطاع وبين المسلم إذا كان جنباً فلم يحصل الجواب عنه من المحقق، فالأولى القول بالوجوب عليهما كما ذكره قاضيخان
His saying: (and for one who becomes Muslim while junub, otherwise it is recommended) i.e., ghusl is obligatory upon one who becomes Muslim while in a state of janabah. The lam is in the sense of 'upon' by the indication of his saying 'otherwise it is recommended', because if the lam were in its literal sense, the two states would be equal, as is not hidden. The wording of his original source al-Wafi is better: 'and it is recommended for one who becomes Muslim and was not junub, otherwise it is necessary.' And the scholars have differed concerning the disbeliever when he becomes Muslim while junub: it is said it is not obligatory because they were not addressed by the branches of the law, and after Islam there is no janabah – this is one narration. And in another narration it is obligatory, and this is the more correct because the attribute of janabah remains after Islam, so he cannot perform what is conditioned by its removal except by it, so it becomes obligatory. And if a disbelieving woman menstruated, then became pure, then embraced Islam, Shams al-A’imma said: no ghusl upon her, contrary to the junub. And the difference is that the attribute of janabah remains after Islam, so it is as if he became junub afterwards, while the cessation in menstruation is the cause, and it has not yet occurred. Therefore, if she became Muslim while menstruating then became pure, ghusl becomes obligatory upon her. And if a boy reaches puberty by wet dream or a girl by menstruation, it is said it is obligatory upon her but not upon him. These are four cases. Qadikhan said: the most precautionary is the obligation of ghusl in all cases. In Fath al-Qadir: we know of no disagreement on the obligation of wudu for prayer if he becomes Muslim while in a state of hadath, and there is no meaning to differentiate between these two. For if we consider the time of puberty as the moment of the capacity for obligation, it is like the moment of the cause, then it is not obligatory upon either. If we consider the moment of the address (taklif) so that their times become one, then it is obligatory upon both. Menstruation is either a hadath or causes a hadath in the rank of janabah, as we will verify in its chapter, so its ruling should be the same as one who becomes Muslim while junub. The answer is that the cause in menstruation is the cessation, and its occurrence after puberty because puberty is realized by the beginning of menstruation, so that cessation does not occur except while she is already pubescent. End quote. This answer, after being accepted, serves as a response to what is raised regarding the difference between a woman who reaches puberty by menstruation and a boy who reaches puberty by wet dream. But one may object because the chosen view is that the cause for the obligation of ghusl on a menstruating woman is not menstruation nor its cessation, but rather the obligation of prayer. Therefore, there is no difference between them. The correct answer is that the correct view is the obligation of ghusl on the boy when he reaches puberty by wet dream, as mentioned in Mi‘raj al-Dirayah attributed to Amali Qadikhan. As for what is raised regarding the difference between a menstruating woman who becomes Muslim after cessation and a Muslim who is junub, no answer from the scholar has been obtained, so the proper view is to say it is obligatory upon both, as Qadikhan mentioned.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation of ghusl for a disbeliever who accepts Islam while in a state of janabah. The author of Kanz says it is obligatory; if he is not junub, it is recommended. The commentator discusses the ikhtilaf: some say not obligatory because pre-Islam acts are not addressed, but the stronger view is obligatory because the state of janabah persists after Islam (it is a physical state that continues). Several cases are compared: a disbelieving woman who menstruates then becomes pure before Islam: no ghusl required. If she becomes Muslim while menstruating, then after purification she must perform ghusl because the cause (cessation) occurs after Islam. Similarly, a boy who reaches puberty by wet dream and a girl by menstruation: some say ghusl is obligatory on her but not him (since her puberty is defined by menstruation). Qadikhan says precaution is to make it obligatory in all cases. The passage then discusses the reasoning from Fath al-Qadir, which tries to equate menstruation with janabah, but the commentator ultimately sides with the view that both cases (convert junub and menstruating woman after Islam) require ghusl.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity; here minor (hadath) vs. major (janabah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct Hanafi view, if a disbeliever embraces Islam while in a state of janabah, what is required?
A) Only wudu is required.
B) Ghusl is obligatory.
C) No purification is needed because conversion erases all previous states.
D) Ghusl is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
A convert who was junub must perform ghusl because janabah is a persisting physical state, not erased by conversion.
