قوله : (وإن غير طاهر أحد أوصافه أي يجوز الوضوء بالماء ولو خالطه شيء طاهر فغير أحد أوصافه التي هي الطعم واللون والريح وهذا عندنا وقال الشافعي: إن كان المخالط الطاهر مما لا يمكن حفظ الماء عنه كالطحلب وما يجري عليه الماء من الملح والنورة جاز الوضوء به، وإن كان تراباً طرح فيه قصداً لم يؤثر، وإن كان شيئاً سوء ذلك كالزعفران والدقيق والملح الجبلي والطحلب المدقوق بما يستغني الماء عنه لم يجز الوضوء به. المهذب. وأصل الخلاف أن هذا الماء الذي اختلط به طاهر هل صار به مقيداً أم لا؟ فقال الشافعي ومن وافقه : يقيد لأنه يقال ماء الزعفران ونحن لا ننكر أنه يقال ذلك ولكن لا ما يمتنع دام المخالط مغلوباً أن يقول القائل فيه هذا ماء من غير زيادة، وقد رأيناه يقال في ماء المد والنيل حال غلبة لون الطين عليهما وتقع الأوراق في الحياض زمن الخريف فيمر الرفيقان ويقول أحدهما للآخر هنا ماء تعالى نشرب نتوضأ فيطلقه مع تغير أوصافه، فظهر لنا من اللسان أن المخالط المغلوب لا يسلب الإطلاق فوجب ترتيب حكم المطلق على الماء الذي كذلك. ويدل عليه من السنة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «اغسلوه بماء وسدر قاله المحرم وقصته ناقته فمات. رواه البخاري ومسلم في حديث ابن عباس. وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم حين توفيت ابنته «اغسلنها بماء وسدر» رواه مالك في الموطأ من حديث أم عطية. والميت لا يغسل إلا بماء يجوز للحي أن يتطهر به . والغسل بالماء والسدر لا يتصور إلا بخلط السدر بماء أو بوضعه على الجسد الماء عليه، وكيفما كان فلا بد من الاختلاط والتغيير وقد اغتسل يوم الفتح في قصعة فيها أثر العجين. رواه النسائي والماء بذلك يتغير ولم يعتبر للمغلوبية وأمر عليه السلام قيس بن عاصم حين أسلم أن يغتسل بماء وسدر، فلولا أنه طهور لما أمر أن يغتسل به. فإن قيل : المطلق يتناول الكامل دون الناقص وفي الماء المختلط بطاهر غيره قصور، فالجواب أن المطلق يتناول الكامل ذاتاً لا وصفاً والماء المتغير بطاهر كامل ذاتاً فيتناوله مطلق الاسم. فإن قيل : لو حلف لا يشرب ماء فشرب هذا الماء المتغير لم يحنث ولو استعمل المحرم الماء، والمختلط بالزعفران لزمته الفدية. ولو وكل وكيلاً بأن يشتري له ماء فاشترى هذا الماء لا يجوز فعلم بهذا أن الماء المتغير ليس بماء مطلق قلنا لا نسلم ذلك هكذا ذكر السراج الهندي أقول : ولئن سلمنا فالجواب؛ أما في مسألة اليمين والوكالة فالعبرة فيهما للعرف وفي العرف أن هذا الماء لا يشرب وأما في مسألة المحرم فإنما لزمته الفدية لكونه استعمل عين الطيب وإن كان مغلوباً.
His statement: 'And if a pure substance changes one of its attributes means that it is permissible to perform wudu with water even if a pure substance has mixed with it and changed one of its attributes which are taste, color, and smell. This is our (Hanafi) view. Al-Shafi'i said: If the pure substance mixed is such that water cannot be preserved from it, like algae and what water flows over of salt and lime, then wudu with it is permissible. If it is dirt thrown into it intentionally, it has no effect. If it is something other than that, like saffron, flour, rock salt, and ground algae that water can do without, then wudu with it is not permissible. [Al-Muhadhdhab]. The basis of the disagreement is: Has this water which has been mixed with a pure substance become restricted (muqayyad) or not? Al-Shafi'i and those who agree with him said: It becomes restricted because it is called 'saffron water'. We do not deny that it is called that, but as long as the mixed substance is subdued, it does not prevent a person from saying about it 'this is water' without addition. We have seen it said about the water of the tide and the Nile when the color of mud overcomes them, and leaves fall into ponds in autumn; two companions pass by and one says to the other 'here is water, come let us drink and perform wudu' and he says it despite the change of its attributes. So it has become clear to us from language that a subdued mixed substance does not negate absoluteness, so it is necessary to apply the ruling of absolute water to water that is like this. It is supported from the Sunnah by his statement, peace be upon him: 'Wash him with water and lotus leaves' said about the pilgrim whose riding camel broke his neck and he died—narrated by Bukhari and Muslim in the hadith of Ibn Abbas. And he said, peace be upon him, when his daughter died: 'Wash her with water and lotus leaves'—narrated by Malik in the Muwatta from the hadith of Umm Atiyyah. A deceased person is not washed except with water that is permissible for a living person to purify with. Washing with water and lotus leaves is inconceivable except by mixing lotus leaves with water or placing them on the body and pouring water over them. However it is done, mixing and change are inevitable. The Prophet performed ghusl on the day of conquest from a bowl that had traces of dough—narrated by al-Nasa'i—and the water changed due to that, and he did not consider the subdued nature (of the dough). And he commanded Qays ibn 'Asim when he embraced Islam to perform ghusl with water and lotus leaves; if it were not purifying, he would not have commanded him to perform ghusl with it. If it is said: The absolute (al-mutlaq) is used for the perfect, not the deficient, and water mixed with another pure substance has deficiency; then the answer: The absolute is used for the perfect in essence, not in description, and water changed by a pure substance is perfect in essence, so the absolute name applies to it. If it is said: If someone swore not to drink water and then drank this changed water, he would not break his oath; and if a pilgrim in ihram used water mixed with saffron, he would owe a fidyah; and if a person appointed an agent to buy water for him and the agent bought this water, it would not be valid; from this it is known that changed water is not absolute water. We say: We do not accept that. This is what al-Siraj al-Hindi mentioned. I say: Even if we accept, the answer is: In the matter of oath and agency, the criterion is custom, and in custom, this water is not drunk. In the matter of the pilgrim, he incurs the fidyah because he used the actual perfume, even if it is subdued (by the water).
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute about water that has been mixed with a pure (tahir) substance such that one of its attributes (taste, color, smell) changes. The Hanafi position (this is our view) is that such water remains valid for wudu regardless of the substance, as long as the substance is subdued (maghlub) and the water is still commonly called 'water'. The Shafi'i position, as summarized from Al-Muhadhdhab, differentiates: if the substance cannot normally be avoided (like algae in flowing water, or dirt that is unavoidable), then it is permissible; but if it is something intentional like saffron, flour, or ground algae, then it is not permissible. The basis of the dispute is whether such water becomes 'restricted' (muqayyad) or remains 'absolute' (mutlaq). The Hanafis argue that language and custom support that the absolute name still applies as long as the mixture is subdued. They provide evidence from the Sunnah: the Prophet ordered washing the deceased with water and sidr (lotus leaves), which necessarily involves mixing and change; the Prophet performed ghusl from a bowl with traces of dough; and he ordered Qays ibn 'Asim to perform ghusl with water and sidr after embracing Islam. All these indicate that water mixed with pure substances remains purifying. To objections about oaths, ihram, and agency, the Hanafis respond that those are based on custom (in oaths and agency) or on using the perfume itself (in ihram).

Key Terms
ماء مطلق (māʾ muṭlaq): Absolute water, which is naturally pure and purifying without any added description.
المخالط المغلوب (al-mukhāliṭ al-maghlūb): The mixed substance that is subdued and does not dominate the water.
فسلخة (falsakhah (not in text but from 'idgham'? Actually text uses 'غسل' but the term 'سدورة'? The text uses 'السدر' for lotus leaves.): سدر: lotus leaves used in washing the deceased in the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary criterion for water mixed with a pure substance to remain valid for wudu?
A) The substance must be something that can be avoided
B) The water must not change color at all
C) The mixture must be subdued (maghlub) so the water is still commonly called 'water'
D) The substance must be from the earth like mud

Key Takeaway
Water mixed with a pure substance remains valid for wudu as long as the mixture is subdued and the water is still commonly called 'water'.

Taharah — Purification

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ghalabah: Parts vs. Color
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the criterion for ghalabah in mixed water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on determining predominance (ghalabah) when water mixes with a pure liquid, and identify which view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
For liquid admixtures similar to water, predominance is judged by quantity, not color – the view of Abu Yusuf preferred in Al-Hidayah.

When water mixes with a pure substance like saffron or rose water, does it remain valid for wudu? The answer depends on whether the water is still 'absolute' or has become 'restricted'. The Hanafi school teaches that water remains absolute unless the admixture predominates. But how is 'predominance' measured? This question sparked a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks their difference, the supporting authorities, and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The two Imams differ on the criterion for ghalabah when a liquid admixture changes water's color. State each position: Abu Yusuf by parts (quantity), Muhammad by color.
2
Locate the supporting statements
Which Hanafi authorities support each view? The text cites Al-Majma', Al-Khaniyah, Al-Muhit, and others. Note that Al-Muhit reverses the attribution.
Al-Muhit says Abu Yusuf by color, Muhammad by parts – but the more correct view is the first (Abu Yusuf by parts).
3
Determine the tarjih
Al-Hidayah prefers Abu Yusuf's view (by parts). Also note the view of Al-Asbijabi: color first, then taste, then parts.
The mufta bihi is predominance by parts for liquid admixtures similar to water.
4
Apply to a real case
Take the example of saffron: if it changes water's color but is less in volume, is wudu permissible? According to Abu Yusuf, yes (by quantity); according to Muhammad, no (by color). The mufta bihi view permits.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – practical consequence.
5
Understand the limitations
This criterion applies to liquid admixtures similar to water; other cases (solids, differing qualities) have different rules, covered in the next lesson.

Source Text

في الفتاوى وصاحب المحيط ، وصدر به في الكافي وذكر الجواز بصيغة «قبل». وفي شرح منية المصلي : الأوجه عدم الجواز فكان هو الأولى لما أنه كمل امتزاجه كما صرح به في الكافي. فما وقع في شرح الزيلعي من أنه لم يكمل امتزاجه ففيه نظر، وقد علمت أن العلماء اتفقوا على جواز الوضوء بالماء المطلق وعلى عدم جوازه بالماء المقيد . ثم الماء إذا اختلط به شيء طاهر لا يخرج عن صفة الإطلاق إلا إذا غلب عليه غيره . بقي الكلام هنا في تحقيق الغلبة بماذا تكون؟ فعبارة القدوري وهي قوله وتجوز الطهارة بماء خالطه شيء طاهر فغير أحد أوصافه» كعبارة الكنز والمختار تفيد أن المتغير لو كان وصفين لا يجوز به الوضوء، وعبارة المجمع وهي قوله ونجيزه بغالب على طاهر کزعفران تغیر به بعض أوصافه تفيد أن المتغير لو كان وصفين يجوز أو كلها لا يجوز. وفي تتمة الفتاوى الماء المتغير أحد أوصافه لا يجوز به الوضوء» وفي الهداية والغلبة بالإجزاء لا بتغير اللون هو الصحيح وقد حكي خلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد ففي المجمع والخانية وغيرهما أن أبا يوسف يعتبر الغلبة بالإجزاء، ومحمداً باللون، وفي المحيط عكسه، والأصح من الخلاف الأول كما صرحوا به. وذكر القاضي الاسبيجابي أن الغلبة تعتبر أولاً من حيث اللون ثم من حيث الطعم ثم من حيث الإجزاء. وفي الينابيع : لو نقع الحمص والباقلاء وتغير لونه وطعمه وريحه يجوز الوضوء به. وعن أبي يوسف: ماء الصابون إذا كان ثخيناً قد غلب على الماء لا يتوضأ به، وإن كان رقيقاً يجوز وكذا ماء الأشنان. ذكره في الغاية وفيه إذا كان الطين غالباً عليه لا يجوز الوضوء به، وإن كان رقيقاً يجوز الوضوء به. وصرح في التجنيس بأن من التفريع على اعتبار الغلبة بالإجزاء قول الجرجاني إذا طرح الزاج أو العفص في الماء جاز الوضوء به إن كان لا ينقش إذا كتب به، فإن نقش لا يجوز والماء هو المغلوب وهكذا جاء الاختلاف ظاهراً في عباراتهم فلا بد من التوفيق فنقول : إن التقييد المخرج عن الاطلاق بأحد أمرين : الأول كمال الامتزاج وهو بالطبخ طاهر لا يقصد به المبالغة في التنظيف أو بتشرب النبات سواء خرج بعلاج أو لا. الثاني غلبة المخالط فإن كان جامداً فبانتفاء رقة الماء وجريانه على الأعضاء، وعليه يحمل ما عن أبي يوسف وما في الينابيع، ويوافقه ما في الفتاوى الظهيرية : إذا طرح الزاج في الماء حتى اسود جاز الوضوء به وإن كان مائعاً موافقاً للماء في الأوصاف الثلاثة كالماء الذي يؤخذ بالتقطير من لسان الثور، وماء الورد الذي انقطعت رائحته والماء المستعمل على القول المفتى به من طهارته إذا اختلط بالمطلق فالعبرة للاجزاء فإن كان الماء المطلق أكثر جاز الوضوء بالكل، وإن كان مغلوباً لا يجوز، وإن استويا لم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية. وفي البدائع قالوا : حكمة حكم الماء المغلوب احتياطاً وعليه وعلى الأول يحمل قول من قال العبرة بالإجزاء وهو قول أبي يوسف الذي اختاره في الهداية. فإن كان المخالط جامداً فغلبة الإجزاء فيه بثخونته، فإن كان مائعاً موافقاً للماء فغلبة الإجزاء فيه بالقدر، وذكر الحدادي أن غلبة الإجزاء في الجامد تكون بالثلث وفي المائع بالنصف، فإن كان مخالفاً للماء في الأوصاف كلها فإن غيرها أو أكثرها لا يجوز الوضوء به وإلا جاز، وعليه يحمل قول من قال إن غير أحد أوصافه جاز الوضوء به وإن خالفه في وصف واحد أو وصفين فالعبرة لغلبة ما به الخلاف كاللبن يخالفه في اللون والطعم. فإن كان لون اللبن أو طعمه هو الغالب فيه لم يجز الوضوء به وإلا جاز، وكذا ماء البطيخ يخالفه في الطعم فتعتبر الغلبة فيه بالطعم وعليه يحمل قول من قال إذا غير أحد أوصافه لا يجوز، وقول من قال العبرة للون. وأما قول من قال العبرة للون ثم الطعم ثم الإجزاء فمراده إن المخالط المائع للماء إن كان لونه مخالفاً للون الماء فالغلبة تعتبر من حيث اللون، وإن كان لونه لون الماء فالعبرة للطعم إن غلب طعمه على الماء لا يجوز، وإن كان لا يخالفه في اللون والطعم والريح فالعبرة للإجزاء. وأما ما يفهم من عبارة المجمع فلا يمكن حمله على شيء كما لا يخفى والذي يظهر أن مراده من البعض البعض الأقل وهو الواحد حققه في البحر والنهر والمنح. قلت: لكن الشرنبلالي في شرحه للوهبانية فرق بينهما فراجعه متأملاً اهـ. وكأنه يشير إلى ضعف ما في الشرنبلالية من الفرق، وستطلع إن شاء الله تعالى على حقيقة الحال بعون الملك المتعال هذا وفي فتح القدير والوجه أن يخرج من الأقسام ما خالط جامداً فسلب رقته وجريانه لأن هذا ليس بماء مقيد والكلام فيه، بل ليس بماء أصلاً كما يشير إليه قول المصنف فيما يأتي قريباً في المختلط بالأشنان إلا أن يغلب فيصير كالسويق لزوال اسم الماء عنه اهـ.
In the Fatawa and the author of Al-Muhit, and it was introduced in Al-Kafi, and he mentioned permissibility with the form 'qabla'. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: the most likely is impermissibility, so it was the first because it completed its mixture as stated in Al-Kafi. What occurred in Sharh al-Zayla'i that it did not complete its mixture is debatable. And you have known that the scholars agreed on the permissibility of wudu with absolute water and on its impermissibility with restricted water. Then water, when a pure thing mixes with it, does not leave the description of absoluteness unless something else overcomes it. The remaining discussion here is on realizing predominance: with what does it occur? The statement of Al-Quduri, which is his saying 'and purification is permissible with water mixed with a pure substance that changed one of its descriptions', like the statement of Al-Kanz and Al-Mukhtar, indicates that if two descriptions changed, wudu is not permissible with it. And the statement of Al-Majma', which is his saying 'and we permit it with a predominant over a pure substance like saffron that changed some of its descriptions', indicates that if two descriptions changed, it is permissible, or if all changed, it is not permissible. In Tatimmat al-Fatawa: 'water that changed one of its descriptions is not permissible for wudu.' In Al-Hidayah: 'and predominance by parts, not by change of color, is the correct view.' And a difference has been narrated between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In Al-Majma', Al-Khaniyah, and others, that Abu Yusuf considers predominance by parts, and Muhammad by color. In Al-Muhit the opposite. The more correct of the two differences is the first, as they stated. Al-Qadi al-Asbijabi mentioned that predominance is considered first by color, then by taste, then by parts. In Al-Yanabi': 'if chickpeas and broad beans are soaked and their color, taste, and smell change, wudu is permissible with it.' And from Abu Yusuf: 'soap water, if it is thick and has overcome the water, wudu is not performed with it; if it is thin, it is permissible, and likewise water of ushnan.' It was mentioned in Al-Ghayah: 'if mud is predominant over it, wudu is not permissible; if it is thin, wudu is permissible.' And he stated in Al-Tajniss that among the branches on considering predominance by parts is the saying of Al-Jurjani: 'if alum or gallnut is thrown into water, wudu is permissible if it does not leave a mark when written with; if it leaves a mark, it is not permissible, and the water is the overcome.' Thus the difference is apparent in their statements, so reconciliation is necessary. We say: restriction removing from absoluteness occurs by one of two matters: first, complete mixture, which is by cooking a pure substance not intended for extreme cleaning, or by plant absorption whether it comes out by treatment or not. Second, predominance of the admixture: if it is solid, then by the loss of the water's thinness and its flow over the limbs. Upon this are carried what is from Abu Yusuf and what is in Al-Yanabi', and it is supported by what is in Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: 'if alum is thrown into water until it turns black, wudu is permissible with it.' And if it is liquid that agrees with water in all three descriptions, like water taken by distillation from ox-tongue, and rose water that has lost its scent, and used water according to the mufta bihi opinion of its purity, when it mixes with absolute water, the criterion is by parts. If the absolute water is more, wudu is permissible with all; if it is overcome, it is not permissible; if they are equal, it is not mentioned in the apparent riwayah. In Al-Bada'i' they said: 'the wisdom of ruling on overcome water is as a precaution.' Upon this and the first is carried the saying of those who said the criterion is by parts, which is the saying of Abu Yusuf, which he chose in Al-Hidayah. If the admixture is solid, then predominance by parts is by its thickness; if it is liquid that agrees with water, then predominance by parts is by quantity. Al-Haddadi mentioned that predominance by parts in solid is by one-third, and in liquid by half. If it differs from water in all descriptions, then if it changes them or most of them, wudu is not permissible; otherwise it is permissible. Upon this is carried the saying of those who said that if it changes one of its descriptions, wudu is permissible. If it differs in one description or two, the criterion is the predominance of that in which there is difference, like milk differing in color and taste. If the color or taste of milk is predominant, wudu is not permissible; otherwise it is permissible. Likewise, watermelon juice differs in taste, so predominance is considered by taste. Upon this is carried the saying of those who said if it changes one of its descriptions, it is not permissible, and the saying of those who said the criterion is by color. As for the saying of those who said the criterion is by color, then taste, then parts, his meaning is: if the liquid admixture's color differs from water's color, then predominance is considered by color; if its color is the same as water, then the criterion is by taste; if its taste overcomes the water, it is not permissible; if it does not differ in color, taste, and smell, then the criterion is by parts. As for what is understood from the statement of Al-Majma', it cannot be interpreted in any way, as is not hidden. And it appears that his meaning of 'some' is the lesser part, which is one. This was verified in Al-Bahr, Al-Nahr, and Al-Manh. I say: but Al-Shirnablali in his commentary on Al-Wahbaniyyah differentiated between the two, so refer to it with reflection. It seems he is pointing to the weakness of the differentiation. You will see the reality with the help of Allah. In Fath al-Qadir, the correct view is to exclude from the categories what is mixed with a solid that removes its thinness and flow, because this is not restricted water under discussion, rather it is not water at all, as indicated by the author's statement shortly in the chapter on mixing with ushnan: 'unless it overcomes and becomes like sawiq, due to the removal of the name water.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition by Ibn Nujaym (author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) on the issue of water mixed with a pure (tahir) substance and when it loses its status as absolute water (maa' mutlaq) for the purpose of wudu. The central question is: how do we determine 'ghalabah' (predominance)? The author begins by noting that scholars agree that wudu with absolute water is permissible and with restricted water (muqayyad) is not. When water mixes with a pure substance, it remains absolute unless the substance 'overcomes' it. The discussion then focuses on the definition of 'ghalabah'. 

The author presents various statements from earlier Hanafi works. The text of Al-Quduri (similar to Kanz al-Daqa'iq) says: 'water changed in one of its descriptions' still permits wudu, implying that change in two or more descriptions would prevent it. The text of Al-Majma' says: 'we permit it with a predominant on a pure substance... changed some of its descriptions' — this implies that change in some descriptions (i.e., one or two) is permissible, but change in all is not. Tatimmat al-Fatawa states that change in even one description is impermissible. 

Al-Hidayah declares that the correct view is predominance by 'ajza' (parts/quantity), not by change of color. A difference is narrated between Abu Yusuf (predominance by quantity) and Muhammad (by color). The more correct view is the first. Al-Qadi al-Asbijabi prioritizes color, then taste, then parts. 

The author then reconciles the conflicting statements. He identifies two factors that take water out of absoluteness: (1) complete mixture (kamal al-imitizaj) — achieved by cooking a pure substance not intended for cleaning, or by plant absorption; (2) predominance by the admixture. If the admixture is solid, predominance is determined by the loss of water's thinness and flow. If liquid and similar to water in qualities, predominance is by quantity. If different in qualities, predominance is by the specific changed quality. 

He then details sub-rules: for solid admixtures, thickness is the criterion; for liquid similar admixtures, quantity; if the admixture differs in all qualities, change of most or all disqualifies. For milk (differs in color and taste), the predominant quality determines. For watermelon juice (differs in taste), taste is the criterion. 

Finally, he notes that Al-Shirnablali attempted a different reconciliation but was considered weak. The author concludes with Fath al-Qadir's view that a solid admixture that completely removes the water's fluidity removes it from being water at all, not just being restricted.

Key Terms
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Predominance of the admixture over the water such that the water loses its attribute of absoluteness. The criterion differs based on the nature of the admixture.
المطلق (al-mutlaq): Absolute water (maa' mutlaq) — water in its original state, not mixed with any substance that alters its nature. Used for purification.
المقيد (al-muqayyad): Restricted water — water that has been mixed with a pure substance to the extent that it is no longer called absolute water (e.g., rose water, soap water if thick). Not valid for wudu.
الإجزاء (al-ajza'): The parts or quantity of the mixture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in Al-Hidayah, how is predominance (ghalabah) determined when a liquid admixture similar to water (e.g., rose water) is mixed with water?
A) By color
B) By taste
C) By quantity
D) By the most obvious change

Key Takeaway
For liquid admixtures similar to water, the Hanafi mufta bihi view determines predominance by quantity, not by change in color or taste.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Reconciling the Views: Ibn Nujaym's Comprehensive Criteria for Ghalabah
Reconciliation of intra-Hanafi differences on ghalabah criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Ibn Nujaym's reconciled framework for determining predominance (ghalabah) in water mixed with pure substances, distinguishing between solid admixtures, liquid similar, and liquid different admixtures.

Core Idea
Ibn Nujaym reconciles all Hanafi views: for solids, predominance by thickness; for similar liquids, by quantity; for different liquids, by the specific changed quality.

The seemingly contradictory statements from early Hanafi authorities on ghalabah can be harmonised. Ibn Nujaym, in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, provides a comprehensive framework that categorises admixtures into three types: solid, liquid similar to water, and liquid different in qualities. Each has its own criterion for predominance. This lesson teaches you how to apply this framework to any real-world case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two factors that remove water from absoluteness
Complete mixture (kamal al-imitizaj) by cooking or plant absorption, and predominance (ghalabah) of the admixture.
Complete mixture does not require predominance; it is a separate category.
2
Classify the admixture
Is it solid, liquid similar to water in all three qualities, or liquid different in some qualities?
Similar liquids: same color, taste, and smell as water. Different liquids: differ in one or more qualities.
3
Apply the appropriate criterion
Solid: predominance by loss of thinness and flow (thickness). Liquid similar: predominance by quantity. Liquid different: predominance by the specific quality that differs (e.g., taste for watermelon juice).
For differing liquids, if only one quality differs, that quality is decisive. If multiple differ, the one that is predominant determines the ruling.
4
Check for extreme cases
If a solid admixture completely removes the water's fluidity (like thick mud), the mixture is no longer water at all, not even restricted water.
Refer to Fath al-Qadir's view: such mixtures are not water and cannot be used for wudu.
5
Practice with examples
Apply to soap water, alum, milk, watermelon juice, and confirm the ruling per the reconciled framework.
Use the table from the reconciliation.

في الفتاوى وصاحب المحيط ، وصدر به في الكافي وذكر الجواز بصيغة «قبل». وفي شرح منية المصلي : الأوجه عدم الجواز فكان هو الأولى لما أنه كمل امتزاجه كما صرح به في الكافي. فما وقع في شرح الزيلعي من أنه لم يكمل امتزاجه ففيه نظر، وقد علمت أن العلماء اتفقوا على جواز الوضوء بالماء المطلق وعلى عدم جوازه بالماء المقيد . ثم الماء إذا اختلط به شيء طاهر لا يخرج عن صفة الإطلاق إلا إذا غلب عليه غيره . بقي الكلام هنا في تحقيق الغلبة بماذا تكون؟ فعبارة القدوري وهي قوله وتجوز الطهارة بماء خالطه شيء طاهر فغير أحد أوصافه» كعبارة الكنز والمختار تفيد أن المتغير لو كان وصفين لا يجوز به الوضوء، وعبارة المجمع وهي قوله ونجيزه بغالب على طاهر کزعفران تغیر به بعض أوصافه تفيد أن المتغير لو كان وصفين يجوز أو كلها لا يجوز. وفي تتمة الفتاوى الماء المتغير أحد أوصافه لا يجوز به الوضوء» وفي الهداية والغلبة بالإجزاء لا بتغير اللون هو الصحيح وقد حكي خلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد ففي المجمع والخانية وغيرهما أن أبا يوسف يعتبر الغلبة بالإجزاء، ومحمداً باللون، وفي المحيط عكسه، والأصح من الخلاف الأول كما صرحوا به. وذكر القاضي الاسبيجابي أن الغلبة تعتبر أولاً من حيث اللون ثم من حيث الطعم ثم من حيث الإجزاء. وفي الينابيع : لو نقع الحمص والباقلاء وتغير لونه وطعمه وريحه يجوز الوضوء به. وعن أبي يوسف: ماء الصابون إذا كان ثخيناً قد غلب على الماء لا يتوضأ به، وإن كان رقيقاً يجوز وكذا ماء الأشنان. ذكره في الغاية وفيه إذا كان الطين غالباً عليه لا يجوز الوضوء به، وإن كان رقيقاً يجوز الوضوء به. وصرح في التجنيس بأن من التفريع على اعتبار الغلبة بالإجزاء قول الجرجاني إذا طرح الزاج أو العفص في الماء جاز الوضوء به إن كان لا ينقش إذا كتب به، فإن نقش لا يجوز والماء هو المغلوب وهكذا جاء الاختلاف ظاهراً في عباراتهم فلا بد من التوفيق فنقول : إن التقييد المخرج عن الاطلاق بأحد أمرين : الأول كمال الامتزاج وهو بالطبخ طاهر لا يقصد به المبالغة في التنظيف أو بتشرب النبات سواء خرج بعلاج أو لا. الثاني غلبة المخالط فإن كان جامداً فبانتفاء رقة الماء وجريانه على الأعضاء، وعليه يحمل ما عن أبي يوسف وما في الينابيع، ويوافقه ما في الفتاوى الظهيرية : إذا طرح الزاج في الماء حتى اسود جاز الوضوء به وإن كان مائعاً موافقاً للماء في الأوصاف الثلاثة كالماء الذي يؤخذ بالتقطير من لسان الثور، وماء الورد الذي انقطعت رائحته والماء المستعمل على القول المفتى به من طهارته إذا اختلط بالمطلق فالعبرة للاجزاء فإن كان الماء المطلق أكثر جاز الوضوء بالكل، وإن فإن كان المخالط جامداً فغلبة الإجزاء فيه بثخونته، فإن كان مائعاً موافقاً للماء فغلبة الإجزاء فيه بالقدر، وذكر الحدادي أن غلبة الإجزاء في الجامد تكون بالثلث وفي المائع بالنصف، فإن كان مخالفاً للماء في فيصير كالسويق لزوال اسم الماء عنه اهـ.
In the Fatawa and the author of Al-Muhit, and it was introduced in Al-Kafi, and he mentioned permissibility with the form 'qabla'. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: the most likely is impermissibility, so it was the first because it completed its mixture as stated in Al-Kafi. What occurred in Sharh al-Zayla'i that it did not complete its mixture is debatable. And the statement of Al-Majma', which is his saying 'and we permit it with a predominant over a pure substance like saffron that changed some of its descriptions', indicates that if two descriptions changed, it is permissible, or if all changed, it is not permissible. In Tatimmat al-Fatawa: 'water that changed one of its descriptions is not permissible for wudu.' In Al-Hidayah: 'and predominance by parts, not by change of color, is the correct view.' And a difference has been narrated between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In Al-Majma', Al-Khaniyah, and others, that Abu Yusuf considers predominance by parts, and Muhammad by color. In Al-Muhit the opposite. The more correct of the two differences is the first, as they stated. Al-Qadi al-Asbijabi mentioned that predominance is considered first by color, then by taste, then by parts. In Al-Yanabi': 'if chickpeas and broad beans are soaked and their color, taste, and smell change, wudu is permissible with it.' And from Abu Yusuf: 'soap water, if it is thick and has overcome the water, wudu is not performed with it; if it is thin, it is permissible, and likewise water of ushnan.' It was mentioned in Al-Ghayah: 'if mud is predominant over it, wudu is not permissible; if it is thin, wudu is permissible.' And he stated in Al-Tajniss that among the branches on considering predominance by parts is the saying of Al-Jurjani: 'if alum or gallnut is thrown into water, wudu is permissible if it does not leave a mark when written with; if it leaves a mark, it is not permissible, and the water is the overcome.' Thus the difference is apparent in their statements, so reconciliation is necessary. We say: restriction removing from absoluteness occurs by one of two matters: first, complete mixture, which is by cooking a pure substance not intended for extreme cleaning, or by plant absorption whether it comes out by treatment or not. Second, predominance of the admixture: if it is solid, then by the loss of the water's thinness and its flow over the limbs. Upon this are carried what is from Abu Yusuf and what is in Al-Yanabi', and it is supported by what is in Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: 'if alum is thrown into water until it turns black, wudu is permissible with it.' And if it is liquid that agrees with water in all three descriptions, like water taken by distillation from ox-tongue, and rose water that has lost its scent, and used water according to the mufta bihi opinion of its purity, when it mixes with absolute water, the criterion is by parts. If the absolute water is more, wudu is permissible with all; if it is overcome, it is not permissible; if they are equal, it is not mentioned in the apparent riwayah. In Al-Bada'i' they said: 'the wisdom of ruling on overcome water is as a precaution.' Upon this and the first is carried the saying of those who said the criterion is by parts, which is the saying of Abu Yusuf, which he chose in Al-Hidayah. If the admixture is solid, then predominance by parts is by its thickness; if it is liquid that agrees with water, then predominance by parts is by quantity. Al-Haddadi mentioned that predominance by parts in solid is by one-third, and in liquid by half. If it differs from water in all descriptions, then if it changes them or most of them, wudu is not permissible; otherwise it is permissible. Upon this is carried the saying of those who said that if it changes one of its descriptions, wudu is permissible. If it differs in one description or two, the criterion is the predominance of that in which there is difference, like milk differing in color and taste. If the color or taste of milk is predominant, wudu is not permissible; otherwise it is permissible. Likewise, watermelon juice differs in taste, so predominance is considered by taste. Upon this is carried the saying of those who said if it changes one of its descriptions, it is not permissible, and the saying of those who said the criterion is by color. As for the saying of those who said the criterion is by color, then taste, then parts, his meaning is: if the liquid admixture's color differs from water's color, then predominance is considered by color; if its color is the same as water, then the criterion is by taste; if its taste overcomes the water, it is not permissible; if it does not differ in color, taste, and smell, then the criterion is by parts. As for what is understood from the statement of Al-Majma', it cannot be interpreted in any way, as is not hidden. And it appears that his meaning of 'some' is the lesser part, which is one. This was verified in Al-Bahr, Al-Nahr, and Al-Manh. I say: but Al-Shirnablali in his commentary on Al-Wahbaniyyah differentiated between the two, so refer to it with reflection. It seems he is pointing to the weakness of the differentiation. You will see the reality with the help of Allah. In Fath al-Qadir, the correct view is to exclude from the categories what is mixed with a solid that removes its thinness and flow, because this is not restricted water under discussion, rather it is not water at all, as indicated by the author's statement shortly in the chapter on mixing with ushnan: 'unless it overcomes and becomes like sawiq, due to the removal of the name water.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition by Ibn Nujaym (author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) on the issue of water mixed with a pure (tahir) substance and when it loses its status as absolute water (maa' mutlaq) for the purpose of wudu. The central question is: how do we determine 'ghalabah' (predominance)? The author begins by noting that scholars agree that wudu with absolute water is permissible and with restricted water (muqayyad) is not. When water mixes with a pure substance, it remains absolute unless the substance 'overcomes' it. The discussion then focuses on the definition of 'ghalabah'. 

The author presents various statements from earlier Hanafi works. The text of Al-Quduri (similar to Kanz al-Daqa'iq) says: 'water changed in one of its descriptions' still permits wudu, implying that change in two or more descriptions would prevent it. The text of Al-Majma' says: 'we permit it with a predominant on a pure substance... changed some of its descriptions' — this implies that change in some descriptions (i.e., one or two) is permissible, but change in all is not. Tatimmat al-Fatawa states that change in even one description is impermissible. 

Al-Hidayah declares that the correct view is predominance by 'ajza' (parts/quantity), not by change of color. A difference is narrated between Abu Yusuf (predominance by quantity) and Muhammad (by color). The more correct view is the first. Al-Qadi al-Asbijabi prioritizes color, then taste, then parts. 

The author then reconciles the conflicting statements. He identifies two factors that take water out of absoluteness: (1) complete mixture (kamal al-imitizaj) — achieved by cooking a pure substance not intended for cleaning, or by plant absorption; (2) predominance by the admixture. If the admixture is solid, predominance is determined by the loss of water's thinness and flow. If liquid and similar to water in qualities, predominance is by quantity. If different in qualities, predominance is by the specific changed quality. 

He then details sub-rules: for solid admixtures, thickness is the criterion; for liquid similar admixtures, quantity; if the admixture differs in all qualities, change of most or all disqualifies. For milk (differs in color and taste), the predominant quality determines. For watermelon juice (differs in taste), taste is the criterion. 

Finally, he notes that Al-Shirnablali attempted a different reconciliation but was considered weak. The author concludes with Fath al-Qadir's view that a solid admixture that completely removes the water's fluidity removes it from being water at all, not just being restricted.

Key Terms
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Predominance of the admixture over the water such that the water loses its attribute of absoluteness. The criterion differs based on the nature of the admixture.
المطلق (al-mutlaq): Absolute water (maa' mutlaq) — water in its original state, not mixed with any substance that alters its nature. Used for purification.
المقيد (al-muqayyad): Restricted water — water that has been mixed with a pure substance to the extent that it is no longer called absolute water (e.g., rose water, soap water if thick). Not valid for wudu.
الجامد (al-jamid): Solid admixture.
المائع الموافق (al-ma'i' al-muwafiq): Liquid admixture that agrees with water in all three qualities (color, taste, smell).
المائع المخالف (al-ma'i' al-mukhalif): Liquid admixture that differs from water in one or more qualities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Nujaym's reconciliation, how is predominance determined when water is mixed with a solid pure substance like clay that makes the water thick?
A) By quantity
B) By color
C) By thickness and loss of flow
D) By taste

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles apparent contradictions on ghalabah by applying different criteria for solids, similar liquids, and different liquids.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
Criterion for Mixed Water in Wudu: Preponderance vs. Parts
Intra-Hanafi dispute over criteria for mixed water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for validity of wudu with water mixed with pure substances and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and al-Hadadi.

Core Idea
A mixture of water with a pure substance remains valid for wudu unless the additive overcomes the water by quantity or by removing fluidity.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi debate on when mixed water retains its purifying quality. The central question: does the mixture become invalid when the additive's properties predominate, or is it a matter of parts? Understanding this dispute is key to applying the principle that the name 'water' must remain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Start with the zahir al-riwayah: if absolute water is more, wudu is permissible; if overcome, not; if equal, not mentioned. Then note Abu Yusuf's view that the criterion is parts (al-ijza').
This sets the baseline for the dispute.
2
Classify the mixture
Distinguish between solid and liquid additives. For solids, preponderance is determined by removal of fluidity (al-riqqa); for liquids matching water, by quantity.
Al-Hadadi specifies fractions: 1/3 for solids, 1/2 for liquids.
3
Analyze property changes
If the additive changes all or most of water's three descriptions (color, taste, smell), wudu is invalid. If it changes only one or two, the criterion is preponderance of the changed property.
Examples: milk (color and taste), watermelon (taste).
4
Reconcile conflicting statements
Study how the commentator resolves apparent contradictions by applying the principle that the name 'water' must remain. For solids like saffron, if fluidity is lost, water is no longer mutlaq.
The hadith about not urinating in stagnant water is the proof (dalil).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that preponderance is by quantity for liquids and by fluidity for solids, with the condition that the water remains called 'water'.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah adopts Abu Yusuf's view on parts.

كتاب الطهارة
اسود جاز الوضوء به وإن كان مائعاً موافقاً للماء في الأوصاف الثلاثة كالماء الذي يؤخذ بالتقطير من لسان الثور، وماء الورد الذي انقطعت رائحته والماء المستعمل على القول المفتى به من طهارته إذا اختلط بالمطلق فالعبرة للاجزاء فإن كان الماء المطلق أكثر جاز الوضوء بالكل، وإن كان مغلوباً لا يجوز، وإن استويا لم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية. وفي البدائع قالوا : حكمة حكم الماء المغلوب احتياطاً وعليه وعلى الأول يحمل قول من قال العبرة بالإجزاء وهو قول أبي يوسف الذي اختاره في الهداية. فإن كان المخالط جامداً فغلبة الإجزاء فيه بثخونته، فإن كان مائعاً موافقاً للماء فغلبة الإجزاء فيه بالقدر، وذكر الحدادي أن غلبة الإجزاء في الجامد تكون بالثلث وفي المائع بالنصف، فإن كان مخالفاً للماء في الأوصاف كلها فإن غيرها أو أكثرها لا يجوز الوضوء به وإلا جاز، وعليه يحمل قول من قال إن غير أحد أوصافه جاز الوضوء به وإن خالفه في وصف واحد أو وصفين فالعبرة لغلبة ما به الخلاف كاللبن يخالفه في اللون والطعم. فإن كان لون اللبن أو طعمه هو الغالب فيه لم يجز الوضوء به وإلا جاز، وكذا ماء البطيخ يخالفه في الطعم فتعتبر الغلبة فيه بالطعم وعليه يحمل قول من قال إذا غير أحد أوصافه لا يجوز، وقول من قال العبرة للون. وأما قول من قال العبرة للون ثم الطعم ثم الإجزاء فمراده إن المخالط المائع للماء إن كان لونه مخالفاً للون الماء فالغلبة تعتبر من حيث اللون، وإن كان لونه لون الماء فالعبرة للطعم إن غلب طعمه على الماء لا يجوز، وإن كان لا يخالفه في اللون والطعم والريح فالعبرة للإجزاء. وأما ما يفهم من عبارة المجمع فلا يمكن حمله على شيء كما لا يخفى والذي يظهر أن مراده من البعض البعض الأقل وهو الواحد. حققه في البحر والنهر والمنح. قلت: لكن الشرنبلالي في شرحه للوهبانية فرق بينهما فراجعه متأملاً اهـ. وكأنه يشير إلى ضعف ما في الشرنبلالية من الفرق، وستطلع إن شاء الله تعالى على حقيقة الحال بعون الملك المتعال هذا وفي فتح القدير والوجه أن يخرج من الأقسام ما خالط جامداً فسلب رقته وجريانه لأن هذا ليس بماء مقيد والكلام فيه، بل ليس بماء أصلاً كما يشير إليه قول المصنف فيما يأتي قريباً في المختلط بالأشنان إلا أن يغلب فيصير كالسويق لزوال اسم الماء عنه اهـ. قوله: (وعليه يحمل ما عن أبي يوسف وما في الينابيع الذي قدمه عن أبي يوسف لا يخالف هذا ظاهراً حتى يحمل عليه بخلاف ما في الينابيع تأمل قوله : وعليه وعلى (الأول) أي على أن العبرة للإجزاء أي القدر والوزن إن كان لا يخالف في الأوصاف، وعلى أن العبرة بانتفاء الرقة إن كان جامداً، فقوله «فإن كان المخالط جامداً وقوله وإن كان مائعاً» تفريع عليه وتفصيل لما علم إجمالاً. قوله: (كاللبن يخالفه في اللون والطعم الخ) قال الرملي أقول : المشاهد في اللبن مخالفته للماء في الرائحة أيضاً وكذلك المشاهد في البطيخ مخالفته للماء في الرائحة فجعل الأول مما يخالفه في وصفين فقط، والثاني في وصف فقط فيه نظر وأيضاً في البطيخ ما لونه أحمر وفيه ما لونه أصفر فتأمل قوله : (والذي يظهر أن مراده من البعض الأقل الخ) أقول : قول المجمع ونجيزه بغالب على طاهر لا يخلو إما أن يحمل على الأعم من

كما الثاني هي عبارة القدوري تصحيحاً لكلامه، ويدل عليه قوله في شرحه «فغير بعض أوصافه من طعم أو ريح أو لون» ذكره بـ«أو» التي هي لأحد الأشياء بعد «من» التي أوقعها بياناً للبعض، ولا يظهر لتغيير عبارة القدوري فائدة وههنا تنبيهات مهمة لا بأس بإيرادها : الأول أن مقتضى ما قالوه هنا أن المخالط الجامد لا يقيد الماء إلا إذا سلبه وصف الرقة من والسيلان جواز التوضؤ بنبيذ التمر والزبيب ولو غير الأوصاف الثلاثة، وقد صرحوا قبيل باب التيمم بأن الصحيح خلافه، وأن تلك رواية مرجوع عنها. وقد يقال إن ذلك مشروط بما إذا لم يزل عنه اسم الماء، وفي مسألة نبيذ التمر زال عنه اسم الماء فلا مخالفة كما لا يخفى. أنه يقتضي أيضاً أن الزعفران إذا اختلط بالماء يجوز الوضوء به ما دام رقيقاً سيالاً ولو غير الأوصاف كلها لأنه من قبيل الجامدات والمصرح به في معراج الدراية معزياً إلى القنية أن الزعفران إذا وقع في الماء أمكن الصبغ فيه فليس بماء مطلق من غير نظر إلى الثخونة . ويجاب عنه بما تقدم من أنه زال عنه اسم الماء. الثالث أنهم قد صرحوا بأن الماء المستعمل على القول بطهارته إذا اختلط بالماء الطهور لا يخرجه عن الطهورية إلا إذا غلبه أو ساواه، أما إذا كان مغلوباً فلا يخرجه عن الطهورية فيجوز الوضوء بالكل، وهو بإطلاقه يشمل ما إذا استعمل الماء خارجاً ثم ألقي الماء المستعمل واختلط بالطهور أو الغمس في الماء الطهور لا فرق بينهما يدل عليه ما في البدائع في الكلام على حديث «لا يبولن أحدكم في الماء الدائم» لما فيه من إخراج من أن يكون مطهراً من غير ضرورة وذلك لا يقال إنه نهى عن ذلك الماء الجامد والمائع أو على الجامد فقط، ولا سبيل إلى حمله على المائع فقط لقوله كزعفران» فإن حمل على الأعم لا يصح حمل البعض على الواحد لأن غلبة المخالط الجامد تعتبر بانتفاء الرقة لا بالأوصاف عن وصف واحد. وأيضاً بالنظر إلى المخالط المائع لا تثبت الغلبة فيه بوصف واحد مطلقاً فإنه فضلاً إذا كان مخالفاً للماء في كل الأوصاف يعتبر ظهورها كلها أو أكثرها وإن حمل على الجامد فقط فقد علمت مما قررناه ما يرد عليه من أنه يعتبر فيه انتفاء الرقة والسيلان وإن تغيرت الأوصاف كلها ما لم يزل عنه اسم الماء كما يأتي التقييد به فلا فرق بين الزعفران وبين ماء الباقلاء والجاز الذي في الينابيع والظهيرية، فكما اعتبر فيه انتفاء الرقة فليعتبر في الزعفران. نعم في عبارة المجمع تأمل من حيث إفهامها أنه لو تغير الأوصاف كلها لا يجوز الوضوء به فإنه ليس على إطلاقه فيقيد بانتفاء الرقة، أو يقال : إذا تغيرت الأوصاف كلها بنحو الزعفران يزول اسم الماء عنه غالباً فقد ظهر لك إمكان حملها على ما قرره وإن حملها على أن المراد بالبعض الواحد كما هو ظاهر عبارة شرحه يقوي الإشكال (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الوضوء باب ٦٨ مسلم في كتاب الطهارة حديث ٩٤ ٩٦. أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ٣٦ الترمذي في كتاب الطهارة باب ٥١ ابن ماجه في كتاب الطهارة باب ٢٥.
On the left of the book: Book of Purification. [Text] And... it is permissible to perform ablution with it even if it is a liquid matching water in the three descriptions, like water extracted by distillation from ox-tongue (plant), and rose water whose smell has disappeared, and used water according to the fatwa of its purity when it mixes with absolute water; the consideration is for the parts. So if the absolute water is more, it is permissible to perform ablution with all, and if it is overcome, it is not permissible, and if equal, it is not mentioned in the apparent narration. And in al-Bada'i' they said: The wisdom of ruling the overcome water is precautionary, and upon it and the first is based the statement of one who said the consideration is for the parts, and it is the statement of Abu Yusuf which he chose in al-Hidayah. So if the mixture is solid, then overbalancing in parts is by its thickness; if it is a liquid matching water, then overbalancing in parts is by quantity. Al-Hadadi mentioned that overbalancing in parts in solids is by one-third, and in liquids by half. If it is contrary to water in all descriptions, then if it changes them or most of them, it is not permissible to perform ablution with it; otherwise it is permissible. And upon it is based the statement of one who said that if it changes one of its descriptions, it is permissible to perform ablution with it. And if it contradicts it in one or two descriptions, the consideration is for the overbalancing of what is in contradiction, like milk contradicts it in color and taste. So if the color or taste of milk is predominant in it, it is not permissible to perform ablution with it; otherwise it is permissible. Likewise watermelon water contradicts it in taste, so overbalancing in it is considered by taste. And upon it is based the statement of one who said: if it changes one of its descriptions, it is not permissible; and the statement of one who said the consideration is for color. As for the statement of one who said the consideration is for color, then taste, then parts, his meaning is that if the mixing liquid contradicts water in color, overbalancing is considered from the aspect of color; if its color is the color of water, the consideration is for taste; if its taste overcomes water, it is not permissible; and if it does not contradict it in color, taste, and smell, the consideration is for parts. As for what is understood from the expression of al-Mujma', it cannot be interpreted in any way, as is not hidden, and what is apparent is that his meaning by 'some' is the least part, which is one. Verified in al-Bahr, al-Nahr, and al-Minh. I say: But al-Shurnbulali in his commentary on al-Wahbaniyyah distinguished between them, so consult him carefully. And it seems he indicates the weakness of the distinction in al-Shurnbulaliyyah, and you will see, Allah willing, the reality of the matter with the help of the Exalted King. And in Fath al-Qadir: The correct view is to exclude from the categories what mixes with a solid and removes its fluidity and flow, because this is not restricted water and the discussion is about it, rather it is not water at all, as indicated by the author's statement later in the section on mixing with ashnan, unless it overcomes and becomes like sawiq due to the removal of the name of water. His statement: (And upon it is based what is from Abu Yusuf and what is in al-Yanabi') which he presented from Abu Yusuf does not contradict this apparently so that it is based on it, unlike what is in al-Yanabi'; contemplate. His statement: 'And upon it and upon (the first)' meaning upon that the consideration is for parts, i.e., quantity and weight if it does not contradict in descriptions, and upon that the consideration is for the removal of fluidity if it is solid. So his statement 'if the mixture is solid' and his statement 'and if it is liquid' is a branching from it and a detail of what was known in summary. His statement: (like milk contradicts it in color and taste etc.) al-Ramli said: I say: observed in milk is its contradiction of water in smell as well, and similarly observed in watermelon is its contradiction of water in smell, so making the first as contradicting in only two descriptions, and the second in only one description is questionable. Also in watermelon there is what is red and what is yellow, so contemplate. His statement: (and what is apparent is that his meaning by 'some' is the least etc.) I say: The statement of al-Mujma' 'and we permit what is predominant over pure' is not free from either being carried on the general, as the second is the expression of al-Quduri correcting his speech, and it is indicated by his statement in his commentary 'so he changed some of its descriptions from taste or smell or color' mentioned with 'or' which is for one of the things after 'from' which he placed as a clarification of 'some', and there is no apparent benefit in changing the expression of al-Quduri. And here are important notices that it is good to mention: The first: that the implication of what they said here is that a solid mixture does not restrict water unless it removes the description of fluidity and flow; [example] the permissibility of performing ablution with date and raisin nabidh even if it changes the three descriptions, and they stated before the chapter of tayammum that the correct view is otherwise, and that narration is abandoned. And it may be said that this is conditioned on the name of water not being removed, and in the issue of date nabidh, the name of water is removed, so there is no contradiction, as is not hidden. That it also implies that saffron, if mixed with water, is permissible to perform ablution with it as long as it is thin and flowing, even if it changes all descriptions, because it is from the category of solids; and what is stated in Mi'raj al-Dirayah attributed to al-Qunyah is that saffron, when it falls in water, can be dyed in it, so it is not absolute water without consideration of thickness. And it is answered by what preceded: that the name of water is removed from it. The third: that they have stated that used water, according to the view of its purity, when it mixes with pure water, does not remove it from being purifying unless it overcomes or equals it; but if it is overcome, it does not remove it from being purifying, so it is permissible to perform ablution with all, and its absolute includes whether water is used externally and then the used water is thrown and mixed with pure water, or dipping in pure water; there is no difference between them, as indicated by what is in al-Bada'i' in the discussion of the hadith 'None of you should urinate in stagnant water' because of the removal of it from being purifying without necessity, and that does not imply that he forbade that water; the solid and liquid or only the solid, and it is not possible to carry it only on liquid because of his saying 'like saffron'. So if it is carried on the general, it is not correct to carry 'some' on one because the overbalancing of a solid mixture is considered by the removal of fluidity, not by descriptions regarding one description. Also, regarding the liquid mixture, overbalancing is not established by one description absolutely; rather, if it contradicts water in all descriptions, the appearance of all or most of them is considered. And if it is carried only on solid, you have known from what we established what refutes it: that it is considered in it the removal of fluidity and flow even if all descriptions change as long as the name of water is not removed, as the restriction will come, so there is no difference between saffron and broad bean water and the like in al-Yanabi' and al-Zuhayriyyah. So just as removal of fluidity is considered in it, let it be considered in saffron. Yes, in the expression of al-Mujma' there is contemplation regarding its indication that if all descriptions change, performing ablution with it is not permissible, for it is not absolute; so it is restricted by the removal of fluidity, or it is said: if all descriptions change by something like saffron, the name of water is usually removed from it; so it has become clear to you the possibility of carrying it on what he established, and if it is carried that the meaning of 'some' is one, as is apparent from the expression of his commentary, it strengthens the problem. (1) Narrated by al-Bukhari in Kitab al-Wudu, Bab 68; Muslim in Kitab al-Taharah, Hadith 94-96; Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Taharah, Bab 36; al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Taharah, Bab 51; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Taharah, Bab 25.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the ruling on performing wudu (ablution) with water that has been mixed with another pure substance. The passage is a detailed legal analysis of the criteria for such mixed water to remain valid for wudu. It opens by stating the basic ruling: if a liquid that matches water in all three descriptions (color, taste, smell) is mixed with absolute (mutlaq) water, then the consideration is based on the quantity (ajza'). If the absolute water is more, wudu is permissible with the entire mixture; if the mixture is more, it is not permissible; if equal, the ruling is not mentioned in the zahir al-riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to al-Bada'i', the ruling for overcome water is precautionary. The passage then notes that the view that the criterion is the parts (al-ijza') is the one chosen by Abu Yusuf in al-Hidayah. For solid mixtures, the criterion is thickness (thakhana); for liquid mixtures that match water, it is quantity. Al-Hadadi is cited as specifying that for solids, preponderance by parts is determined by one-third, and for liquids, by half. If the mixture changes all or most of water's descriptions, wudu is invalid; otherwise, it is valid. Examples are given: milk (changes color and taste) and watermelon water (changes taste). In each case, the preponderance of the changed properties determines the ruling. The passage then discusses the interpretation of statements from earlier scholars, particularly the phrase 'some of its descriptions' in al-Mujma', and debates whether 'some' means one or more. The commentator al-Ramli objects to the simplification of properties in milk and watermelon, noting that they also affect smell. The passage also addresses three important points (tanbihat): (1) solids do not restrict water unless they remove its fluidity and flow; an exception is nabidh (date or raisin infusion) where the name 'water' is removed, so the ruling differs. (2) Saffron, though a solid, if mixed with water and remains fluid, wudu is permissible, but if it dyes the water, it is no longer absolute water. (3) Used water (al-ma' al-musta'mal), according to the view that it is pure, when mixed with pure water does not render it non-purifying unless it exceeds or equals it in quantity. The passage concludes by reconciling various statements and emphasizing the importance of whether the mixture retains the name 'water'. The hadith cited (about not urinating in stagnant water) is used as a proof for the principle that water remains purifying unless changed. Overall, the passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing textual evidence (naql) and rational consideration (aql) to derive detailed rulings.

Key Terms
الماء المطلق (al-ma' al-mutlaq): Absolute water that is pure and purifying in its original state, not mixed with any impurity or pure substance that changes its properties.
الغلبة (al-ghalaba): Preponderance or predominance of one component over another in a mixture, either by quantity (for liquids) or by thickness (for solids).
الرقة (al-riqqa): Fluidity or thinness; when a solid mixture removes the water's fluidity, the mixture is no longer considered water for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if watermelon water (changes taste) is mixed with absolute water and the taste of watermelon is predominant, what is the ruling?
A) Permissible, because only one property changed.
B) Not permissible, because the taste overcomes.
C) Permissible, because the quantity of water is more.
D) Not permissible, because watermelon water is impure.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi criterion for mixed water: preponderance (ghalaba) determines validity, with quantity for liquids and fluidity for solids, provided the name 'water' remains.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
The Ruling on Used Water Mixing with Pure Water: Dominance Criterion and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on rulings of water mixing with used water and solid substances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on the mixture of used water (musta'mal) with pure water (tahur) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the dominance criterion (ghalabah).

Core Idea
Used water is pure but not purifying; it spoils pure water only if dominant or equal.

This lesson examines a key issue in Hanafi taharah: what happens when used water (musta'mal) mixes with pure water. The relied-upon position is that the mixture remains valid for wudu unless the used water dominates or equals the pure water. We will explore the textual basis, the intra-Hanafi differences among Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and the practical application for wudu in shared water sources like school fountains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: when used water (musta'mal, which is pure but not purifying) mixes with pure purifying water (tahur), does the mixture remain purifying for wudu? The answer hinges on the proportion of used water.
2
State the relied-upon Hanafi ruling
The mufta bihi position: the mixture remains tahur (purifying) unless the used water dominates (ghalabah) or equals the pure water. If the used water is overcome (maghlub), wudu with the mixture is valid.
This is the view favored by the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) and consistent with Muhammad al-Shaybani's position.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa held strict: pouring any used water into a well requires removing all water. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differentiate: if the water was used for istinja', same as Abu Hanifa; otherwise, according to Muhammad, it remains pure but twenty buckets are drawn. Muhammad's criterion is explicit dominance.
The disagreement is over the threshold for spoilage, not the purity of used water itself.
4
Analyze the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith 'لا يبولن أحدكم في الماء الدائم' to argue that only a dominant impurity (like urine) removes purifying property. Used water is pure, so it is analogous to milk or rose water: a pure substance that does not spoil water unless it dominates.
The hadith is ahad, but its implication (dalalah) is used to support the dominance criterion.
5
Apply to a real scenario
School fountains (فساقي المدارس): unless there is a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that used water dominates, wudu from them is valid. This is a practical application of the dominance criterion.
The commentator explicitly rules this way, cautioning against assuming invalidity without evidence.

As the second is the phrase of al-Quduri as a correction of his speech, and it is indicated by his statement in his commentary: 'so it changed some of its descriptions, of taste, or odor, or color' — he mentioned it with 'or' which is for one of the things after 'min' which he made as a clarification of 'some'. And no benefit appears in changing the phrase of al-Quduri. And here are important notices, there is no harm in mentioning them: The first: that what they said here necessitates that a solid admixture does not restrict water unless it strips it of the attribute of fluidity and flow, and the permissibility of performing wudu with date and raisin wine even if it changed all three descriptions. And they explicitly stated before the chapter of tayammum that the correct opinion is the opposite, and that that narration is retracted. And it may be said that that is conditioned by if the name of water has not been removed from it, and in the issue of date wine the name of water has been removed from it, so there is no contradiction as is not hidden. It also necessitates that if saffron mixes with water, it is permissible to perform wudu with it as long as it is thin and flowing, even if it changed all descriptions, because it is of the category of solids. And what is explicitly stated in Mi'raj al-Dirayah attributed to al-Qunyah is that if saffron falls into water and dyeing is possible in it, then it is not absolute water without consideration of thickness. And it is answered by what has preceded: that the name of water has been removed from it. The third: that they have explicitly stated that used water, according to the opinion of its purity, if it mixes with purifying water, it does not remove it from being purifying except if it overcomes it or equals it. As for if it is overcome, then it does not remove it from being purifying, so it is permissible to perform wudu with all of it. And its absoluteness includes whether the water was used outside then the used water was thrown and mixed with the purifying water, or immersion in purifying water — no difference between them. This is indicated by what is in al-Bada'i' in the discussion of the hadith: 'Let none of you urinate in still water...' because it takes it out of being a purifier without necessity. It cannot be said that it is a prohibition of the water... solid and liquid or only solid, and there is no way to restrict it to liquid only because of his statement 'like saffron'. For if it is interpreted as general, it is not valid to apply 'some' to 'one' because the overpowering of a solid admixture is considered by the absence of fluidity, not by descriptions of one attribute. And also, with regard to a liquid admixture, overpowering is not established by a single attribute at all, for if it is contrary to water in all descriptions, all or most of their manifestation is considered. And if it is restricted to solid only, then you have known from what we established what is objected to it: that it is considered in it the absence of fluidity and flow even if all descriptions changed as long as the name of water has not been removed from it, as the restriction will come. So there is no difference between saffron and bean water and the like in springs and al-Zahiriyyah. So just as the absence of fluidity is considered in it, let it be considered in saffron. Yes, in the phrase of al-Majma' there is contemplation in that it implies that if all descriptions changed, wudu with it is not permissible, for it is not absolute, so it is restricted by the absence of fluidity, or it is said: if all descriptions changed by something like saffron, the name of water is usually removed from it. So it has become clear to you the possibility of interpreting it according to what he established, and if it is interpreted that what is meant by 'some' is 'one' as is apparent from the phrase of his commentary, it strengthens the problem. (1) Narrated by al-Bukhari in Kitab al-Wudu' Bab 68, Muslim in Kitab al-Taharah Hadith 94-96, Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Taharah Bab 36, al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Taharah Bab 51, Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Taharah Bab 25. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Vol. 1, Page 9. The Book of Taharah. For we say: Little water only leaves being purifying by mixing with a non-purifier if the non-purifier is dominant, like rose water and milk. As for if it is overcome, then no. And here the used water that contacts the body, and there is no doubt that it is less than the unused, so how can it take it out of being purifier? End quote. And he said in another place regarding one who falls into a well: if there is on his body a legal impurity, i.e., he is in a state of minor impurity or major impurity or menstruating or postpartum, then according to the opinion of those who do not consider this water used, nothing is drawn out. Likewise according to the opinion of those who consider it used and consider used water pure, because the unused water is more, so it does not remove it from being purifying as long as the used is not dominant over it, just as if milk is poured into the well by consensus, or if a sheep urinates in it according to Muhammad. And he said in another place: If used water mixes with little water, some said: it is not permissible to perform wudu with it even if little, and this is false. As for according to Muhammad, because it is pure and did not overcome the absolute water, so it does not change it from the attribute of purifying like milk. And as for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?), because little water cannot be avoided. Then 'much' according to Muhammad is what overcomes the absolute water, and according to them is that the places of the drop in the vessel are distinguishable. End quote. And in al-Khulasa: A junub bathed and something from his washing splashed into his vessel — it does not spoil his water. But if it flows into it in a flowing manner, it spoils it. And likewise the basin of the bathhouse is on this. And according to Muhammad's opinion, it does not spoil it as long as it does not overcome it — meaning not by its wording. So if you understand this, do not delay in ruling the validity of wudu from the fountains placed in schools when there is no dominant assumption of the dominance of used water or the occurrence of impurity in the small ones. If you say: Qadi Khan explicitly stated in his Fatawa that if wudu water is poured into a well, according to Abu Hanifa all water is drawn out, and according to his two companions if he cleaned himself with that water then likewise, and if he did not clean himself with it, according to Muhammad it is not impure but twenty buckets are drawn out to make the water pure! So this is apparent in the use of water by falling a little used water into it according to Muhammad. Likewise they explicitly stated that if a junub descends into a well intending to bathe, it spoils the water according to all, as stated by al-Akmal and the author of Mi'raj al-Dirayah and others. And in some books, twenty buckets are drawn out according to Muhammad. And were it not that all became used, nothing would be drawn out. And in Qadi Khan's Fatawa: if one inserts his hand or foot into a vessel to cool down, the water becomes used due to the absence of necessity. Likewise they explicitly stated that water is spoiled if the palm is inserted into it. And among those who stated it is the author of al-Mubtagha with the dotted ghayn. And it necessitates the use of all. And the Qadi said: it is necessary to interpret what is in his commentary as that what is meant is not a single change only, or that 'or' is in the meaning of 'and' so the speech becomes coherent. And Allah, the Exalted, is the Guide to inspiration. His statement: 'This is indicated by what is in al-Bada'i'...' — apparently the pronoun refers to the absence of difference between them. Thus I used to imagine and wrote some statements on the commentator's phrase based on that. Then it became apparent that his intent was to use it as evidence that used water does not spoil the purifier unless it overcomes it or equals it, not on the absence of difference, as might be imagined. His statement: (If you say: Qadi Khan explicitly stated...) the answer to the condition will come after a page, and the origin of the question is... end.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It is an expansion probe by the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) discussing the rulings on water purity when mixed with other substances, particularly used water (musta'mal). The passage opens with a correction of al-Quduri's phrasing regarding change of water's attributes. Then it presents three important notes (tanbihat). The first note discusses solid admixtures (jamid) that do not restrict water unless they remove its fluidity. The second note addresses saffron: if it mixes with water but the water remains thin and fluid, wudu is permissible; however, if the saffron overcomes and removes the name of water, it is no longer absolute water. The third and longest note addresses used water mixing with pure water: according to the relied-upon opinion that used water is pure (tahir), it does not render pure water impure unless it dominates or equals it. The commentator then cites al-Bada'i' and discusses a hadith about urinating in still water, explaining that the prohibition is because it removes the purifying property. He contrasts the cases of solid and liquid admixtures. He then examines intra-Hanafi disputes regarding water in a well when a junub or a person with ritual impurity falls in. According to Abu Hanifa, such water becomes used and the entire well must be emptied; according to Muhammad, if the used water does not dominate, it remains pure but precautionary measures (twenty buckets) are taken. The commentator concludes by applying these principles to wudu from school fountains: as long as there is no strong presumption that used water dominates, wudu is valid. The passage ends with a discussion of Qadi Khan's fatwa and the resolution that the commentator's earlier understanding was mistaken.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (mā' musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl (i.e., has contacted a body in an act of worship).
ماء طهور (mā' tahūr): Pure water that is itself purifying and can be used for wudu.
غلبة (ghalabah): The condition where the admixture (e.g., used water) is quantitatively or qualitatively dominant over the pure water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, when does used water (musta'mal) mixed with pure water (tahur) prevent wudu with the mixture?
A) Whenever any amount of used water is present
B) Only if the used water is dominant or equal in quantity/effect
C) Only if the used water changes the color of the pure water
D) Only if the used water is from a minor impurity (hadath)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that used water is pure, and its mixture with pure water remains purifying for wudu unless the used water dominates or equals the pure water.

Principle of Small Water Losing Purifying Status by Dominant Impurity
States the rule that small water loses purifying effect only by dominant non-purifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which small water loses its purifying property according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof by qiyas with rose water and milk.

Core Idea
Small water remains purifying unless a dominant non-purifier mixes with it – used water does not dominate.

The Hanafi school maintains that water used for wudu (ma' musta'mal) does not automatically lose its purifying quality when mixed back into a larger body of pure water. The author defends this position by drawing an analogy with rose water or milk: just as these non-purifiers only affect water when they are dominant, used water, being less in quantity, cannot dominate. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and clarifies the crucial principle of dominance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using small water for purification. The ruling is that it remains purifying unless mixed with a dominant non-purifier.
The passage focuses on the property of water, not a specific act of worship.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) with milk and rose water. These are clear non-purifiers, but they don't spoil water unless they dominate.
The analogy is based on a jali (clear) illa.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is dominance: a non-purifier only affects water's purifying status if it is physically dominant. Used water is less in quantity than the original water, so it cannot dominate.
This is a zanni dalalah but accepted in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'is hold that used water is non-purifying even if not dominant, based on the idea that contact with the body makes it impure.
The Hanafi response relies on the dominance criterion.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi due to the strength of the qiyas and the lack of explicit contrary evidence.
The authority_weight is unknown; but it is the relied-upon view in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرام لأنا نقول : الماء القليل إنما يخرج عن كونه مطهراً باختلاط غير المطهر به إذا كان غير المطهر غالباً كماء الورد واللبن فأما إذا كان مغلوباً فلا، وههنا الماء المستعمل ما يلاقي البدن ولا شك أن ذلك أقل من غير المستعمل فكيف يخرج به من أن يكون مطهراً؟ ا هـ.
It is forbidden because we say: The small water only leaves its purifying status by mixing with a non-purifier if the non-purifier is dominant, like rose water and milk. But if it is overpowered, then no. Here, used water is that which contacts the body, and there is no doubt that it is less than unused water. So how can it cause it to cease being purifying? End quote.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a rational proof. The author argues that small water (ma' qalil) loses its purifying property only when mixed with a dominant non-purifier. The example given is rose water and milk. Here, used water (musta'mal) that has contacted the body is less in quantity than the unused water, so it cannot dominate. Therefore, used water does not render the water non-purifying. This is based on qiyas jali: just as milk does not spoil water when it is not dominant, used water also does not spoil it. The Hanafi position is that used water is tahir but not mutahhir in itself, but when mixed with pure water, it does not affect the purifying quality unless it becomes dominant.

Key Terms
الماء القليل (al-ma' al-qalil): Water that is less than two qullas or a small quantity that becomes impure by contact with impurity, according to Hanafi fiqh.
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification (wudu or ghusl) and has contacted a limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does small water lose its purifying property according to the Hanafi school?
A) When any non-purifier is mixed with it
B) When the non-purifier is dominant
C) When it touches a human body
D) When it is used for wudu

Key Takeaway
Small water loses its purifying property only when a dominant non-purifier is mixed with it; used water does not automatically affect it.
