Falling into a Well with Ritual Impurity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on water used by a person with hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person with hadath falls into a well and explain why no draining is required.

Core Idea
Hadath in a well does not spoil the water; the majority unused water keeps it purifying.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a person in a state of ritual impurity (hadath) falls into a well. Does the well water become used (musta'mal) or impure? The Hanafi school discusses two positions, but both agree that no draining is needed. Understanding the criterion of dominance helps clarify why the water remains purifying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the impurity
The scenario is a person with hadath (minor impurity, janabah, menstruation, post-natal bleeding) falling into a well. Note that this is legal impurity (najasah hukmiyyah), not physical impurity.
Hanafi distinguishes clearly between legal and physical impurity; only physical impurity can directly affect water.
2
Recognize the two Hanafi positions
First position: water is not considered used at all. Second position: water is used but pure (tahir). Both conclude no draining needed.
The disagreement is only about the definition of musta'mal, not the practical outcome.
3
Understand the criterion of dominance
The water retains its purifying quality as long as the used (or impure) portion is not dominant. Since only a small amount contacts the person, the unused water is more.
This principle applies to other substances like milk or goat urine, as mentioned in the text.
4
Apply the analogy to consolidate
The text uses qiyas: just as pouring milk into a well (by consensus) or a goat urinating in it (according to Muhammad) does not spoil the water, so too with a person with hadath.
This shows that dominance is the criterion, not mere contact or the type of impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في موضع آخر فيمن وقع في البئر فإن كان على بدنه نجاسة حكمية بأن كان محدثاً أو جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء، فعلى قول من لم يجعل هذا الماء مستعملاً لا ينزح شيء، وكذا على قول من جعله مستعملاً وجعل المستعمل طاهراً لأن غير المستعمل أكثر فلا يخرج عن كونه طهوراً ما لم يكن المستعمل غالباً عليه كما لو صب اللبن في البئر بالإجماع أو بالت شاة فيها عند محمد
And he said in another place: Regarding someone who falls into a well: if there is a legal impurity (hadath) on his body, whether he is in a state of minor impurity, janabah, menstruation, or postnatal bleeding, according to the opinion of those who do not consider this water used, nothing needs to be drained. Similarly, according to the opinion of those who consider it used but consider used water pure, because the unused water is more, so it does not cease to be purifying as long as the used water is not dominant, like if milk is poured into the well by consensus, or if a goat urinates in it according to Muhammad.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person with hadath falling into a well. Two positions are mentioned: 1) Those who do not consider the water used (musta'mal) say no water needs to be drained. 2) Those who consider it used but hold used water to be pure (tahir) also say no draining is needed because the unused water is dominant, so the water remains purifying. This is based on the same principle as the previous lesson: the water remains purifying unless the used water dominates. The example of milk or goat urine is given as analogous. The mention of 'according to Muhammad' refers to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's view that goat urine in a well does not make it impure (since the urine of animals whose meat is eaten is not najis in Hanafi).

Key Terms
النجاسة الحكمية (al-najasah al-hukmiyyah): Legal impurity, i.e., the state of hadath (minor or major) which prevents one from performing prayer, as opposed to physical impurity (najasah 'ayniyyah).
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used water: water that has been used for removing hadath (wudu or ghusl). In Hanafi, musta'mal water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (tahur) according to one view, but the text here says it is considered tahir and still purifying if not dominant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The water becomes used (musta'mal) and non-purifying, so the well must be emptied
C) No water needs to be drained because the used water is not dominant
D) The person becomes pure automatically

Key Takeaway
The dominant portion of water determines its purity; a small amount of legal impurity from hadath does not necessitate draining.

The Ruling on Mixing Used Water with Small Water: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of used water mixing with small pure water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn on whether used water spoils a small quantity of pure water, and state the operative ruling for fatwa.

Core Idea
Used water is pure and does not spoil pure water unless it dominates or is detectable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of mixing used water (musta'mal) with a small quantity of pure water. While some scholars categorically prohibit wudu with such water, the Hanafis differentiate based on quantity and detectability. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rulings of taharah in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is performing wudu with water that has been mixed with used water. The issue is whether the presence of used water invalidates the water's purifying quality (tahuriyyah).
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Muhammad holds that used water does not spoil pure water unless it dominates (ghalaba) the pure water. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that if the used water is so little that its traces are not clear, it does not spoil; but if its traces are clear in the vessel, it spoils.
These positions are based on different definitions of 'kathir' (large quantity) in this context.
3
Examine the proof for each view
Muhammad uses analogy (qiyas) to milk: milk is pure and does not change water's purifying quality unless it dominates. The Sahibayn rely on the principle that small water cannot be guarded against (la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu), so the ruling is based on difficulty.
The proofs are talil (reasoning by cause).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Muhammad, wudu is valid as long as used water is not dominant; according to the Sahibayn, wudu is invalid if traces of used water are visible, but valid if not visible.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text rejects the view that any amount of used water spoils (calling it fasid). The relied-upon position is that used water does not spoil pure water unless it is dominant (Muhammad's view) or its traces are clearly detectable (Sahibayn's view). In practice, the stricter view (Sahibayn) is often adopted for caution.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq does not explicitly choose, but the rejection of the absolute prohibition indicates the middle ground.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في موضع آخر : ولو اختلط الماء المستعمل بالماء القليل قال بعضهم : لا يجوز التوضؤ به وإن قل وهذا فاسد. أما عند محمد فلأنه طاهر لم يغلب على الماء المطلق فلا يغيره عن صفة الطهور كاللبن، وأما عندهما فلأن القليل لا يمكن التحرز عنه. ثم الكثير عند محمد ما يغلب على الماء المطلق، وعندهما أن يستبين مواضع القطرة في الإناء ا هـ.
And he said in another place: If used water mixes with small water, some said: It is not permissible to perform wudu with it even if it is little, and this is invalid. As for according to Muhammad, because it is pure and has not overcome the absolute water, so it does not change its purifying quality, like milk. As for according to them (the two), because small water cannot be guarded against. Then, 'much' according to Muhammad is that which overcomes the absolute water, and according to them, that which makes the traces of drops clear in the vessel. End quote.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific ruling: if used water (musta'mal) mixes with small water (ma' qalil). Some scholars said wudu is invalid even if the used water is little, but the author rejects this as fasid (invalid). Then it explains the views of Muhammad (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually 'cindahuma' refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? But it says 'عند محمد' then 'عندهما', which might refer to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad as a pair? In Hanafi, 'Sahibayn' usually means Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. But here it says 'عند محمد' separately, and then 'عندهما' could mean Abu Yusuf and some other? Possibly it means 'according to the two' i.e., Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? Actually in the passage, 'عند محمد' is stated first, then 'عندهما' which likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? This is a common tripartite split: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad. But the text says 'عند محمد' then 'عندهما' so 'the two' may be Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. However, in the next sentence, 'ثم الكثير عند محمد... وعندهما أن يستبين مواضع القطرة في الإناء' - this defines the definition of 'much' (kathir) water. For Muhammad, kathir is water that overcomes the absolute water; for the two, it is that which makes the spots of a drop appear in the vessel (i.e., if a drop of used water spreads and cannot be located, it is considered kathir). So the dispute is about the definition of kathir when mixing used water. The practical outcome: according to Muhammad, used water only spoils pure water if it dominates; according to the two, if the used water is detectable (spots visible), it is considered dominant and spoils it; if not detectable, it does not spoil.

Key Terms
الكثير (al-kathir): A large quantity of water; for Muhammad, it is water that overcomes (yaghlibu) the absolute water; for the Sahibayn, it is water in which the traces of a drop can be distinguished.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what analogy does he use to support his view that used water does not spoil pure water unless it dominates?
A) Milk
B) Wine
C) Oil
D) Honey

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, used water is pure and does not ruin purifying water unless it dominates (Muhammad) or its traces are clearly visible (Sahibayn).

Junub's Wash Splash: Flow vs. Splash
Quotes a branch from al-Khulasa about a junub's splash affecting his vessel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a junub's washing water splashing into a vessel and distinguish between a splash (intidah) and continuous flow (sailan).

Core Idea
Splash does not spoil; only flowing used water invalidates.

A person in a state of janabah washes himself. Some water splashes into a nearby vessel. Does this spoil the water for purification? The Hanafi school makes a precise distinction: a mere splash does not make the water musta'mal (used), but if the water flows in continuously, it does. This ruling, cited from al-Khulasa, also applies to the basin of a bathhouse. Imam Muhammad adds a further condition: the flowing water must dominate the pure water to spoil it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The passage describes a junub (one in major impurity) washing himself. Some of that washing water splashes into a separate vessel. Determine whether this contact affects the purity of the water in the vessel.
2
State the general ruling
The general ruling is that the water in the vessel remains pure and purifying. The splash (intidah) does not make it musta'mal because the water does not flow continuously from the body into the vessel.
Hanafi principle: used water (musta'mal) is defined by flow (sailan), not mere splashing.
3
Identify the exception
The ruling changes if the used water flows (sailan) into the vessel. In that case, the water in the vessel becomes musta'mal and invalid for purification.
The condition for spoiling is continuous flow, not just any transfer.
4
Consider Imam Muhammad's opinion
Imam Muhammad holds that even flowing water does not spoil the vessel water unless the flowing water dominates (ghalaba) over the pure water in quantity.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view that flow alone suffices.
5
Apply to analogous cases
The passage analogizes to the basin of a bathhouse (howd al-hammam): if used water flows into it, it spoils the water for purification. The same rule applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : جنب اغتسل فانتضح من غسله شيء في إنائه لم يفسد عليه الماء، أما إذا كان يسيل فيه سيلاناً أفسده، وكذا حوض الحمام على هذا. وعلى قول محمد لا يفسده ما لم يغلب عليه يعني لا بلفظه .
And in al-Khulasa: A junub washed, and something splashed from his washing into his vessel; it does not spoil the water for him. But if it flows into it, it spoils it. Similarly, the basin of the bathhouse is upon this. And according to Muhammad, it does not spoil it unless it dominates over it, meaning not by his wording.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This is a branch ruling from the Khulasa. A person in a state of janabah washes himself, and some water splashes into a separate vessel. The ruling: if it is just a splash (no continuous flow), the water in the vessel remains pure and usable. If the water flows continuously (running like a stream) into the vessel, then it becomes used water (musta'mal) and spoils the water for purification. The same rule applies to the basin of a bathhouse (howd al-hammam). Additionally, according to Imam Muhammad, even if it flows, it does not spoil the water unless it dominates (ghalaba) over the pure water. The phrase 'meaning not by his wording' likely refers to an earlier definition: the condition of dominance is not based on wording but on actual quantity.

Key Terms
الانتفاض (al-intidah): Splashing of water without continuous flow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Only if the water splashes in large quantity

Key Takeaway

Wudu from School Water Basins (Fasaqi)
Applies the ruling of school water basins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu from shared water basins and identify the condition regarding ghalabat al-zann that affects validity.

Core Idea
Wudu from a school basin is valid unless you strongly suspect used water or impurity dominates.

You have learned the general rules about pure and used water. This passage applies those rules to a concrete situation: the communal water basins found in schools and mosques. The Hanafi school provides a practical guideline based on overwhelming presumption (ghalabat al-zann) rather than mere doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu from a communal water basin (faskiyyah) in a school. The ruling is that the wudu is valid (sahih) under certain conditions.
2
Pinpoint the key condition
The condition for validity is that there is no overwhelming presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the water in the basin is predominantly used water (musta'mal) or that impurity (najasa) has fallen into it, especially in smaller basins.
Ghalabat al-zann is a strong probability, not mere doubt.
3
Understand the legal basis
The default rule is that water remains pure and purifying (istishab al-hal). So without strong evidence to the contrary, the water is considered pure and wudu is valid.
This follows the Hanafi principle: al-asi al-tahara.
4
Apply the ruling to analogous cases
This ruling applies to any large communal water source where the water is frequently replenished, such as mosque fountains or public taps.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا عرفت هذا لم تتأخر عن الحكم بصحة الوضوء من الفساقي الموضوعة في المدارس عند عدم غلبة الظن بغلبة الماء المستعمل أو وقوع نجاسة في الصغار منها.
So when you have understood this, you will not hesitate to judge the validity of wudu from the water basins placed in schools, in the absence of a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that used water is dominant or that impurity has fallen into the small ones among them.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This is a practical fatwa applying the earlier principles. The 'fasaqi' (singular: faskiyyah) are water basins or fountains placed in schools for students to perform wudu. The ruling: wudu from such basins is valid (sahih) as long as there is no overwhelming presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the dominant water in the basin is used water (musta'mal) or that some impurity (najasa) has fallen into the smaller basins. This follows the principle that pure water remains purifying unless used water dominates, and mere possibility does not affect the ruling. The Hanafi school considers that the water in these basins is usually mostly fresh water from a tap or well, so the presumption is purity.

Key Terms
الفسقية (al-faskiyyah (pl. fasaqi)): A water basin or fountain used for ablution, commonly found in schools and mosques.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Overwhelming presumption; a degree of certainty just short of yaqin, which can affect rulings in fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Reconciling Rulings on Used Water in a Well
Resolves an intra-Hanafi objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconcile the apparent contradiction between the general Hanafi principle that used water (musta'mal) does not spoil pure water unless it dominates, and specific rulings from Qadikhan's Fatawa that require draining a well when wudu water from istinja is poured in.

Core Idea
Used water (musta'mal) does not spoil pure water unless dominant, but istinja water contains najasah and spoils regardless.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses an objection: Qadikhan's Fatawa state that pouring wudu water into a well requires draining, which seems to contradict the general principle that used water does not spoil unless dominant. The author resolves this by distinguishing between wudu water from ordinary use (which is tahir but musta'mal) and istinja water (which is najis). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying Hanafi water purity rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Qadikhan's Fatawa state that pouring wudu water into a well requires draining all water (Abu Hanifa) or twenty buckets (Muhammad). This seems to imply that even a small amount of used water spoils the entire well, contradicting the general principle that used water does not spoil unless it dominates.
The general principle is that musta'mal water is tahir and does not render pure water impure unless it changes its nature.
2
Examine the principle and its proof
The general principle is based on the idea that musta'mal water retains its essential purity (tahara) although it is no longer suitable for wudu. Its mixing does not transfer non-purifying status unless it overwhelms the pure water.
This is analogous to mixing a small amount of used water into a large body of pure water – it remains purifying.
3
Analyze the specific cases in Qadikhan
Qadikhan's ruling covers two scenarios: (1) wudu water from istinja (containing najasah), and (2) water used for ghusl with intention (making the whole body musta'mal by legal fiction). These are exceptions to the general rule.
In istinja, the water is physically impure (najis) due to contact with najasah, so it spoils the well regardless of quantity.
4
Trace the resolution
The author explains that Qadikhan's ruling does not contradict the principle because it applies only to water that is either najis (istinja) or rendered musta'mal for the entire well by legal construction (when the person intends ghusl). Ordinary wudu water without istinja does not trigger draining.
The judge (Qadi) suggests interpreting statements about 'used water spoiling' as referring to cases where the water's nature is changed, not to ordinary used water.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: ordinary used water (musta'mal) does not spoil pure water unless it dominates or equals it. Istinja water (najis) spoils any amount. Water used for ghusl with intention makes the entire body of water musta'mal and requires drainage.
This reconciles the general principle with the specific rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Now if you say: Qadikhan explicitly stated in his Fatawa that if one pours wudu water into the well, according to Abu Hanifa, all the water must be drained. According to his two companions, if he performed istinja with that water, then similarly. If he did not perform istinja with it, according to Muhammad, it is not impure, but twenty buckets are drawn from it to make the water pure. This appears to indicate that water becomes used by the falling of a small amount of used water into it according to Muhammad. Similarly, they stated that if a junub descends into the well with the intention of washing, the water becomes spoiled according to all, as stated by al-Akmal, the author of Miraj al-Diraya, and others. In some books, twenty buckets are drawn according to Muhammad, and were it not that all the water became used, they would not have ordered drawing. In Qadikhan's Fatawa, if one inserts his hand or foot into the vessel for cooling, the water becomes used due to lack of necessity. Similarly, they stated that water is spoiled if one inserts the palm into it. This is stated by the author of al-Mubtagha with the letter ghain, and it necessitates that all the water becomes used. The judge said: It is necessary to interpret what is in his commentary that he did not intend a single change, or that 'or' is in the meaning of 'and', so the wording becomes consistent. And Allah is the granter of inspiration. His statement: 'This is indicated by what is in al-Bada'i...' His apparent meaning is that the pronoun refers to the absence of distinction between them. His statement: 'If you say: Qadikhan explicitly stated...' The answer to the conditional will come after a page, and the source of the question is... End quote.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses an apparent contradiction: Qadikhan's fatawa state that pouring wudu water into a well requires draining all water (Abu Hanifa) or twenty buckets (Muhammad), which seems to suggest that a small amount of used water spoils the entire well. But the earlier principle stated that used water does not spoil unless dominant. The author resolves this by interpreting that Qadikhan's ruling applies when the used water is specifically from istinja (which contains physical impurity) or when the intention is washing (making the water musta'mal by action). The phrase 'ورود الكل' suggests that when the person uses the water with intention of washing, the entire water in the well becomes musta'mal by legal fiction (hukman). The judge (Qadi) says that the commentary's statement should be interpreted to mean that used water does not spoil unless it dominates or equals (i.e., mutlaq water is not spoiled by small amounts of musta'mal). The objection and its answer show the intricacy of Hanafi fiqh in reconciling primary principles (used water does not spoil unless dominant) with specific rulings from later fatawa (like pouring istinja water). The resolution is often that 'dominance' is defined differently in different contexts, or that the specific case involves additional factors like physical impurity from istinja.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): The act of washing the private parts after using the toilet, which involves removing physical impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the general principle is wrong
B) Because istinja water is physically impure (najis), not just used
C) Because the well is considered small water
D) Because Muhammad's opinion is followed

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction between the general principle (used water does not spoil unless dominant) and Qadikhan's ruling (draining required) is resolved by recognizing that istinja water is najis and intention to wash can make water musta'mal by legal fiction.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: The Junub Washing in Multiple Wells
Quotes and analyzes the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad about a junub washing in ten wells

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the status of wells when a junub washes in multiple wells, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Even within Hanafi, opinions differ: Abu Yusuf rules all wells impure; Muhammad rules only the first three become used, and intent matters.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about a junub washing in a series of wells. It contrasts the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and clarifies that the branches attributed to Abu Yusuf are based on a weaker narration. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh internal madhhab differences and identify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and disputing Imams
A junub intentionally washes in ten wells. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree on the water's status.
Intention is present for all washes in this scenario.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf says all wells become impure (najis), based on a narration that the junub makes the water najis.
This narration is later identified as weak.
3
State Muhammad's position and its basis
Muhammad says the person becomes pure after the third wash. The first three wells become used (musta'mal) if no physical impurity, else impure. Subsequent wells become used only if intention is present.
Used water is pure but not purifying.
4
Analyse the tarjih
The author clarifies that Abu Yusuf's ruling is based on a weak narration; his well-known opinion is that water remains pure. Muhammad's view is the mufta bihi.
Al-Isbijabi's branches are based on the weak narration.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if a junub accidentally falls into a well without intention, according to Muhammad the water stays pure, but according to Abu Yusuf's weak narration it becomes impure.
The mufta bihi avoids unnecessary declaration of impurity.

Al-Isbijabi in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi and Al-Walwaliji in his Fatawa: A junub washed in a well, then in a well up to ten, with the intention of washing. Abu Yusuf said: All the wells become impure. And Muhammad said: He comes out of the third pure. Then he considers: if there is physical impurity on his body, all the waters become impure; if not, all the waters become used (musta'mal). End of the branches. This is explicit that all the water becomes used according to Muhammad by washing in it. And Imam Qadi Abu Zaid al-Dabusi said in al-Asrar, in discussing the hadith 'None of you should urinate in water...' he said: Whoever says that used water is pure (tahir) and purifying (tahur) does not make washing in it forbidden. Likewise, whoever says it is pure but not purifying, because the madhhab of the one who holds that used water when it falls into other water does not spoil it until it dominates over it, just like milk falling into it. The amount that contacts the body of the user becomes used, and that amount is part of what is used for washing and is usually less than what remains from contact with the body. So it does not spoil and remains purifying, and washing in it is not forbidden unless one judges that the washing water is impure (najis), in which case it spoils everything even if the pure water is more than the impure, like a drop of wine falling into a water skin. Except that Muhammad says: Since he washed in a small quantity of water, all of it becomes used by legal fiction (hukman). End quote. So this expression's intended meaning is what he argued first: that used water does not spoil purifying water unless it dominates or equals it. His statement: 'Then he considers: if there is physical impurity on his body, all the waters become impure...' If he means the waters of the ten wells, it is not clear to us, so ponder and review. Similarly, the impurity of all wells according to Abu Yusuf is problematic. Then it became clear that this is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf that whoever descends into a well while in a state of janabah, the water becomes impure and the man becomes impure, as the commentator will mention in the issue of the well. He argued this because Al-Isbijabi mentioned this narration from him, then mentioned these branches after it. So it appears that they are based on that narration, not on the well-known opinion that the man remains as he is and the water remains as it is. End quote. And Allah knows best. It appears that by 'impure or used waters' according to Muhammad, he means only the three wells, evidenced by the completion of Al-Isbijabi's expression as the commentator will mention there: 'Then after the third, if he finds intention in himself, it becomes used; if no intention, it does not become used.' End quote. So ponder. Then I saw the issue recorded in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj in a clearer way than the commentator mentioned, with the text of what we have established. He said: If a junub washes in a well, then in another well up to ten or more, all the waters become impure according to Abu Yusuf, whether or not there is physical impurity on his body, and the man remains in janabah. And Muhammad said: He comes out of the third well pure, and regarding the three waters, he considers: if there is physical impurity on his body, the water becomes impure; if not, the water becomes used, and used water is pure according to him. As for the fourth and beyond, if he finds intention, it becomes used; otherwise, meaning if no intention, the waters are pure. End quote. The apparent meaning of his statement 'washed' is that the washing in the first three was with intention, and the reason for their being used is that the obligation is discharged with them along with worship (qurbah) and the sunnah of three washes. As for the washing in the subsequent ones, it depends on intention as well for the sake of obtaining worship by renewing the washing due to a different session, and it seems that it is recommended like wudu, so ponder. And the fourth and subsequent do not become impure if there was impurity on him because he becomes pure by coming out of the third. His statement: (So this expression...
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This is a complex intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a junub who washes in a series of wells (up to ten) with the intention of ritual purification. Abu Yusuf holds that all wells become najis (impure), regardless of physical impurity on the body. This is based on a narration from him that when a junub enters a well, both the water and the person become najis. Muhammad's position is more nuanced: He comes out of the third well tahir (pure). The first three wells: if there is physical impurity ('ayn al-najasah) on his body, the water becomes najis; if not, it becomes musta'mal (used), which is tahir but not mutahhir. After the third well, for the fourth and beyond, the water becomes musta'mal only if he has intention (niyyah) for ghusl; otherwise, the water remains pure. This ruling is based on the principles that used water does not spoil pure water unless it dominates (Muhammad's general view), but when a person washes in a small well with the intention of ghusl, all the water in that well becomes musta'mal by legal fiction (hukman). The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq analyzes the text and clarifies that the branches are based on a specific narration from Abu Yusuf, not his well-known opinion. He also resolves that 'all waters' for Muhammad refers only to the first three wells, as the continuation of Al-Isbijabi's text shows. The passage from Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj confirms this interpretation, adding that the fourth and subsequent wells depend on intention. The commentary also notes that the washing in the first three wells has the sunnah of three washes and the discharge of obligation, so intention is inherent. For later wells, intention is required to make the water musta'mal, and a person would only have that intention if he wishes to renew the washing for worship, which is mustahabb (recommended).

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Intention, specifically the intention for ghusl (ritual purification). In this context, it determines whether water becomes musta'mal.
الماء المستعمل حكماً (al-ma' al-musta'mal hukman): Water that is legally considered used by legal fiction, even if physically it hasn't changed. This applies when a person washes in a small body of water with intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a junub washes in a series of wells with intention, how does the status of the water change?
A) All wells become impure regardless of physical impurity
B) The first three wells become used; subsequent wells become used only if he has intention
C) Only the first well becomes used; the rest remain pure
D) The water remains pure in all wells

Key Takeaway
The well-known Hanafi ruling: a junub's washing in a small body of water renders the water musta'mal (used but pure) only if he had intention; after three washes he becomes pure, and subsequent wells require intention to become musta'mal.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on a Junub Bathing in Multiple Wells
Intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple well ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the status of water when a junub bathes in multiple wells, and identify the conditions that affect the ruling.

Core Idea
Water status after ghusl in multiple wells differs between Abu Yusuf (all najis) and Muhammad (musta'mal unless actual impurity).

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of ghusl and the purity of water when a person in major ritual impurity bathes in several wells consecutively. The opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ on whether the water becomes impure (najis) or merely used (musta'mal), with important implications for subsequent purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
A junub bathes in multiple wells (up to ten) with the intention of performing ghusl in each. Determine the ruling on the water status and the person's purity after each bath.
The intention (qasd al-ightisal) is key; if no intention, the water does not become musta'mal.
2
State Abu Yusuf's ruling
Abu Yusuf holds that all wells become najis (impure). This is because the water from the first well, already contaminated by contact with the junub, is carried to subsequent wells, rendering all water impure.
3
State Muhammad's ruling
Muhammad holds that the person emerges pure after the third well. The water status depends on whether there is actual impurity (ayn najasah) on the body: if yes, all waters become najis; if no, all waters become musta'mal (used but not purifying). Subsequent wells (4th onward) only become musta'mal if intention is present again.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Yusuf's view, the person must perform ghusl again with pure water and all wells are unusable. Under Muhammad's view, the person's ghusl is valid and the first three wells' water is musta'mal (usable for non-purification), but later wells remain pure.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a junub with no actual impurity bathes in three wells with intention. According to Muhammad, the water in the wells becomes musta'mal. The junub is pure after the third well. The water can be used for drinking but not for wudu/ghusl until its purifying quality is restored by drawing twenty buckets (as per later fatwa).
See lesson 2 for the restoration process.

إلا أنه يقول بخلافه. وفي الخلاصة: رجل توضأ في طست ثم صب ذلك الماء في بئر ينزح منه الأكثر من عشرين دلواً، ومما صب فيه عند محمد وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ينزح ماء البئر كله لأنه نجس عندهما اهـ. وهذا يفيد صيرورة ماء البئر مستعملاً بالماء القليل المستعمل فيه فبالأولى إذا توضأ فيها أو اغتسل. قلت: قد وقع في جواز الوضوء من الفساقي الصغار الموضوعة في المدارس كلام كثير بين الحنفية من الطلبة والأفاضل في عصرنا وقبله وقد ألف الشيخ العلامة قاسم فيها رسالة وسماها «رفع مسألة المياه» واستدل فيها بما ذكرناه عن البدائع، ووافقه على ذلك بعض أهل عصره وأفتى به وتعقبه البعض الآخر وألف فيها رسالة وسماها «زهر الروض في مسألة الحوض» ونبه عليها في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان وقال: لا تغتر بما ذكره شيخنا العلامة. قوله: (كشفت اللبس الخ) قال أخوه المحقق فيما نقل عنه في هوامش هذا الكتاب على ما في بعض النسخ: كشفت اللبس من حيث آخرها إلا أن محمداً يقول: لما اغتسل بالماء القليل صار الكل مستعملاً حكماً فلنا صورتان صورة وقوع ماء مستعمل في ماء غير مستعمل فيعتبر غلبة الماء الذي ليس بمستعمل، والصورة الثانية ماء واحد توضأ به شخص أو أدخل يده لحاجة صار مستعملاً كله حكماً كما رأيت اهـ. قوله: (فما في البدائع محمول على أن مقتضى مذهب محمد عدم الاستعمال) أي حقيقة أن صاحب البدائع نسب إلى محمد عدم الاستعمال بناء على ما اقتضاه مذهبه من أن المستعمل لا يفسد الماء ما لم يغلبه أو يساوه لكن محمداً ما قال بذلك الذي اقتضاه مذهبه، بل قال في هذه الصورة إنه صار مستعملاً حكماً كما صرحت به عبارة الدبوسي. قوله: (ومما صب فيه) أي وينزح ما ذكر أيضاً من بئر أخرى صب فيها دلو مثلاً من هذه البئر كذا قيل والأظهر أن المراد أنه ينظر في العشرين دلواً وفي المصبوب فأيهما أكثر ينزح بدليل ما سيأتي في أحكام الآبار. ولو وقعت الفأرة في حب فأريق الماء في البئر قال محمد: ينزح الأكثر من المصبوبة ومن عشرين دلواً وهو الأصح. لأن الفارة لو وقعت فيها ينزح عشرون فكذا إذا صب فيها ما وقع فيه إلا إذا زاد المصبوب على ذلك فتنزح الزيادة مع العشرين.ا.هـ. قوله: (ونبه عليها في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان الخ) وهو العلامة ابن الشحنة فإنه قال فيه عند الكلام على مسألة المحدث والجنب إذا وقع في بئر ما نصه: والذي تحرر أنه يختلف الحكم فيها باختلاف أصول أئمتنا فيه والتحقيق النزح للجميع عند الإمام على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل، وقيل أربعون عنده وتحقيق مذهب محمد أنه يسلبه الطهورية وهو الصحيح عن الإمام، والثاني وعليه الفتوى ينزح منه عشرون ليصير طهوراً. وهذا على القول بعدم اعتبار الضرورة، أما لو اعتبرت الضرورة ودفع الحرج فلا يصير الماء مستعملاً في كل موضع تتحقق [؟].
Al-Ispijabi in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi and al-Walwaliji in his fatawa: A junub bathed in a well, then in a well up to ten with the intention of bathing. Abu Yusuf said: All the wells become impure. Muhammad said: He emerges from the third pure; then it is considered: if there was actual impurity on his body, all the waters become impure; if there was no actual impurity, all the waters become musta'mal, to the end of the branches. This is explicit that according to Muhammad, all the water becomes musta'mal by bathing in it. Imam al-Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi said in al-Asrar, commenting on the hadith 'None of you should urinate in water...' he said: Whoever says that musta'mal water is pure and purifying does not make bathing in it unlawful; likewise whoever says it is pure but not purifying, because according to his school, when musta'mal water falls into other water, it does not spoil it until it overwhelms it, like milk falling into it; and the amount that contacts the body of the user becomes musta'mal, and that amount is usually less than what remains from contacting his body, so it does not spoil it and remains purifying; therefore bathing in it is not unlawful unless one rules that the wash water is impure, then it spoils the whole even if it is more than the wash water, like a drop of wine falling into a tank. But Muhammad says: When he bathed in the small amount of water, all became musta'mal by legal fiction. End. This statement cleared the confusion and clarified every guess and conjecture, for it indicated that the implication of Muhammad's school is that water becomes musta'mal by mixing with a little musta'mal water, but Muhammad ruled that the whole became musta'mal by legal fiction, not in reality. So what is in al-Bada'i is interpreted as meaning that the implication of Muhammad's school is non-usage (i.e., it does not become musta'mal), but he says otherwise. And in al-Khulasah: A man performed wudu in a basin then poured that water into a well; he draws from it more than twenty buckets; and from what was poured into it, according to Muhammad and according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he draws all the well water because it is impure according to them. End. This indicates that the well water becomes musta'mal by the small amount of musta'mal water poured into it, so a fortiori if he performed wudu in it or bathed. I say: There has been much discussion among Hanafi students and scholars in our time and before regarding the permissibility of wudu from the small water basins placed in schools. Sheikh 'Allamah Qasim wrote a treatise on it called 'Raf' Mas'alat al-Miyah' and used as evidence what we mentioned from al-Bada'i. Some of his contemporaries agreed with him and issued fatwa accordingly, while others criticized him and wrote a treatise called 'Zahr al-Rawd fi Mas'alat al-Hawd' and pointed it out in his commentary on the poem of Ibn Wahban, saying: Do not be deceived by what our sheikh, the 'allamah, mentioned. His statement: (Cleared the confusion, etc.) His brother, the muhaqqiq, said in what was transmitted from him in the margins of this book according to some copies: 'Cleared the confusion' from its end, except that Muhammad says: When he bathed in the small amount of water, all became musta'mal by legal fiction. So we have two situations: one situation of musta'mal water falling into non-musta'mal water, in which the predominance of the non-musta'mal water is considered; the second situation is water that a person used for wudu or dipped his hand into for a need, which all becomes musta'mal by legal fiction, as you have seen. End. His statement: (So what is in al-Bada'i is interpreted as meaning that the implication of Muhammad's school is non-usage) meaning that the author of al-Bada'i attributed to Muhammad the opinion of non-usage based on what his school implies: that musta'mal water does not spoil water unless it overwhelms or equals it, but Muhammad did not say that which his school implied; rather, he said in this case that it becomes musta'mal by legal fiction, as stated by al-Dabusi. His statement: (And from what was poured into it) meaning that he also draws water from another well into which a bucket, for example, was poured from this well. It is said, and the more apparent is that it is considered in the twenty buckets and in what was poured: whichever is more, he draws, as will come in the rulings of wells. And if a mouse fell into a tank and the water was poured into the well, Muhammad said: He draws the greater of what was poured and of twenty buckets, and this is the most correct. Because if a mouse fell into it, he draws twenty; so likewise if what fell into it is poured into it, unless what was poured exceeds that, then he draws the extra with the twenty. End. His statement: (And he pointed it out in his commentary on the poem of Ibn Wahban, etc.) He is 'Allamah Ibn al-Shihnah, for he said in it, when discussing the issue of a person in a state of minor or major ritual impurity falling into a well, the text of which is: 'What is established is that the ruling differs according to the principles of our imams. The investigation is that drawing all the water is required according to the Imam based on the opinion of the impurity of musta'mal water; and it is said forty according to him. And the correct view of Muhammad's school is that it removes purifying quality, and this is the correct one from the Imam. The second view, and upon it fatwa is given, is that he draws twenty buckets from it to become purifying. This is on the view that necessity is not considered. But if necessity and repelling hardship are considered, then water does not become musta'mal in every place where necessity is realized. [؟]'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically discussing the ruling when a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) bathes in multiple wells consecutively. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, primarily between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, with later clarification from al-Dabusi and others. The ruling: Abu Yusuf holds that all wells become najis (impure) because the water from the first well is already contaminated by contact with the junub, and then each subsequent well becomes najis due to the water carried from the previous well. Muhammad holds that the person becomes pure after the third well, and the status of the water depends on whether there was actual physical impurity (ayn najasah) on his body. If yes, the water becomes najis; if no, it becomes musta'mal (used water), which according to Muhammad is still pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr tahur) in some views. The key point is that Muhammad makes a distinction: for the first three wells, the water becomes musta'mal due to direct contact; afterwards (fourth well onwards), it only becomes musta'mal if he has the intention (niyyah) for ghusl again, otherwise it remains pure. Abu Yusuf's view is more strict. The commentary by al-Dabusi clarifies that Muhammad's ruling is hukman (by legal fiction), not haqiqatan (in reality), meaning that even though the water is not actually all used, it is treated as such for legal purposes. The later discussion about wudu water poured into a well (from al-Khulasah) reinforces this: if musta'mal water is poured into a well, it does not necessarily spoil the whole well unless it overwhelms; but if one performs wudu directly in the well, it all becomes musta'mal. This shows the subtlety in Hanafi fiqh regarding water purity. The passage ends with a mention of later Hanafi scholars' opinions on practical issues like small water basins in schools, and the position that fatwa is given on drawing twenty buckets to restore purifying quality, but if necessity (darurah) is considered, the water does not become musta'mal.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a valid act of purification (wudu or ghusl) with intention, and is still pure but not purifying (according to some) or still purifying (according to others) in the Hanafi school
غسالة (ghusalah): Wash water that has been used to remove actual impurity (najasah) from the body; it is najis according to some Hanafi scholars
حكماً (hukman): By legal fiction, meaning that the ruling is applied as if it were real, even though physically it is not exactly so

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the status of the water in the first well when a junub with no actual impurity on his body bathes in it with intention?
A) The water becomes najis (impure).
B) The water becomes musta'mal (used, pure but not purifying).
C) The water remains pure and purifying.
D) The water becomes najis only if the ghusl is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between musta'mal and najis water is crucial in Hanafi fiqh, and the use of legal fiction (hukman) allows for practical rulings that avoid excessive hardship.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
The Ruling on Pouring Musta'mal Water into a Well: Hukman vs Haqiqatan
Expansion on the principle of hukman and the fatwa of twenty buckets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of hukman (legal fiction) to cases where musta'mal water is poured into a large body of water, and state the fatwa of drawing twenty buckets.

Core Idea
When musta'mal water is poured into a well, it does not spoil the entire well unless it overwhelms; but direct use in the well renders it all musta'mal by legal fiction.

In this lesson, we explore the extension of the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad to the case of pouring musta'mal water (e.g., from wudu) into a well. The commentary from al-Khulasah and later scholars clarifies the principle: if water that has become musta'mal is added to a well, it does not automatically render the entire well musta'mal unless it predominates. However, if one performs wudu or ghusl directly in the well, the entire well becomes musta'mal by legal fiction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the case from al-Khulasah
A man performs wudu in a basin and then pours that water into a well. The ruling on the well water is examined: according to Muhammad, one must draw more than twenty buckets; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the entire well water must be drawn because it is impure.
The text distinguishes between the well into which the water is poured and the water that was poured.
2
Apply the principle of hukman vs haqiqatan
When musta'mal water is poured into a well, it does not make the entire well musta'mal unless it overwhelms the well water (by quantity). This is in contrast to the case where one bathes directly in the well, where the entire well becomes musta'mal by legal fiction.
See al-Dabusi's analogy with milk and wine.
3
Interpret Muhammad's view on the poured water
Muhammad says: if the poured musta'mal water is less than twenty buckets, draw more than twenty buckets from the well to restore its purifying quality. If the poured water is more than twenty buckets, draw all the water.
This is based on the analogy that musta'mal water is like a drop of wine: it does not spoil the whole if it is less, but if it predominates, the whole becomes musta'mal.
4
Understand the fatwa of twenty buckets
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Ibn al-Shihnah) have established that the fatwa is to draw twenty buckets from the well after pouring musta'mal water, because this amount is sufficient to restore its purifying quality. This is the operative ruling in the school.
If necessity (darurah) is considered, the water may not become musta'mal at all, and no drawing is required.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
If a person pours a bucket of musta'mal water into a well used for drinking, the well water remains pure (tahir) but loses its purifying quality. To make it usable for wudu again, twenty buckets must be drawn out. This is a practical application of the hukman principle.

الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي والولوالجي في فتاواه: جنب اغتسل في بئر ثم في بئر إلى العشرة على قصد الاغتسال قال أبو يوسف: تنجس الآبار كلها. وقال محمد: يخرج من الثالثة طاهراً ثم ينظر إن كان على بدنه عين نجاسة تنجست المياه كلها، وإن لم يكن عين نجاسة صارت المياه كلها مستعملاً إلى آخر الفروع. وهذا صريح في استعمال جميع الماء عند محمد بالاغتسال فيه. وقال الإمام القاضي أبو زيد الدبوسي في الأسرار في الكلام على حديث لا يبولن أحدكم في الماء إلى آخره قال: من قال إن الماء المستعمل طاهر طهور لا يجعل الاغتسال فيه حراماً، وكذلك من قال طاهر غير طهور لأن المذهب عنده أن الماء المستعمل إذا وقع في ماء آخر لم يفسده حتى يغلب عليه بمنزلة اللبن يقع فيه وقدر ما يلاقي بدن المستعمل يصير مستعملاً وذلك القدر من جملة ما يغتسل فيه عادة يكون أقل مما فضل عن ملاقاة بدنه فلا يفسد ويبقى طهوراً لذلك ولا يحرم فيه الاغتسال إلا أن يحكم بنجاسة الغسالة فيفسد الكل وإن كان أكثر من الغسالة كقطرة خمر تقع في حب إلا أن محمداً يقول: لما اغتسل في الماء القليل صار الكل مستعملاً حكماً اهـ. فهذه العبارة كشفت اللبس وأوضحت كل تخمين وحدس فإنها أفادت أن مقتضى مذهب محمد أن الماء مستعملاً باختلاط القليل من الماء المستعمل إلا أن محمداً حكم بأن الكل صار مستعملاً حكماً لا حقيقة فما في البدائع محمول على أن مقتضى مذهب محمد عدم الاستعمال إلا أنه يقول بخلافه. وفي الخلاصة: رجل توضأ في طست ثم صب ذلك الماء في بئر ينزح منه الأكثر من عشرين دلواً، ومما صب فيه عند محمد وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ينزح ماء البئر كله لأنه نجس عندهما اهـ. وهذا يفيد صيرورة ماء البئر مستعملاً بالماء القليل المستعمل فيه فبالأولى إذا توضأ فيها أو اغتسل. قلت: قد وقع في جواز الوضوء من الفساقي الصغار الموضوعة في المدارس كلام كثير بين الحنفية من الطلبة والأفاضل في عصرنا وقبله وقد ألف الشيخ العلامة قاسم فيها رسالة وسماها «رفع مسألة المياه» واستدل فيها بما ذكرناه عن البدائع، ووافقه على ذلك بعض أهل عصره وأفتى به وتعقبه البعض الآخر وألف فيها رسالة وسماها «زهر الروض في مسألة الحوض» ونبه عليها في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان وقال: لا تغتر بما ذكره شيخنا العلامة. قوله: (كشفت اللبس الخ) قال أخوه المحقق فيما نقل عنه في هوامش هذا الكتاب على ما في بعض النسخ: كشفت اللبس من حيث آخرها إلا أن محمداً يقول: لما اغتسل بالماء القليل صار الكل مستعملاً حكماً فلنا صورتان صورة وقوع ماء مستعمل في ماء غير مستعمل فيعتبر غلبة الماء الذي ليس بمستعمل، والصورة الثانية ماء واحد توضأ به شخص أو أدخل يده لحاجة صار مستعملاً كله حكماً كما رأيت اهـ. قوله: (فما في البدائع محمول على أن مقتضى مذهب محمد عدم الاستعمال) أي حقيقة أن صاحب البدائع نسب إلى محمد عدم الاستعمال بناء على ما اقتضاه مذهبه من أن المستعمل لا يفسد الماء ما لم يغلبه أو يساوه لكن محمداً ما قال بذلك الذي اقتضاه مذهبه، بل قال في هذه الصورة إنه صار مستعملاً حكماً كما صرحت به عبارة الدبوسي. قوله: (ومما صب فيه) أي وينزح ما ذكر أيضاً من بئر أخرى صب فيها دلو مثلاً من هذه البئر كذا قيل والأظهر أن المراد أنه ينظر في العشرين دلواً وفي المصبوب فأيهما أكثر ينزح بدليل ما سيأتي في أحكام الآبار. ولو وقعت الفأرة في حب فأريق الماء في البئر قال محمد: ينزح الأكثر من المصبوبة ومن عشرين دلواً وهو الأصح. لأن الفارة لو وقعت فيها ينزح عشرون فكذا إذا صب فيها ما وقع فيه إلا إذا زاد المصبوب على ذلك فتنزح الزيادة مع العشرين.ا.هـ. قوله: (ونبه عليها في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان الخ) وهو العلامة ابن الشحنة فإنه قال فيه عند الكلام على مسألة المحدث والجنب إذا وقع في بئر ما نصه: والذي تحرر أنه يختلف الحكم فيها باختلاف أصول أئمتنا فيه والتحقيق النزح للجميع عند الإمام على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل، وقيل أربعون عنده وتحقيق مذهب محمد أنه يسلبه الطهورية وهو الصحيح عن الإمام، والثاني وعليه الفتوى ينزح منه عشرون ليصير طهوراً. وهذا على القول بعدم اعتبار الضرورة، أما لو اعتبرت الضرورة ودفع الحرج فلا يصير الماء مستعملاً في كل موضع تتحقق [؟].
Al-Ispijabi in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi and al-Walwaliji in his fatawa: A junub bathed in a well, then in a well up to ten with the intention of bathing. Abu Yusuf said: All the wells become impure. Muhammad said: He emerges from the third pure; then it is considered: if there was actual impurity on his body, all the waters become impure; if there was no actual impurity, all the waters become musta'mal, to the end of the branches. This is explicit that according to Muhammad, all the water becomes musta'mal by bathing in it. Imam al-Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi said in al-Asrar, commenting on the hadith 'None of you should urinate in water...' he said: Whoever says that musta'mal water is pure and purifying does not make bathing in it unlawful; likewise whoever says it is pure but not purifying, because according to his school, when musta'mal water falls into other water, it does not spoil it until it overwhelms it, like milk falling into it; and the amount that contacts the body of the user becomes musta'mal, and that amount is usually less than what remains from contacting his body, so it does not spoil it and remains purifying; therefore bathing in it is not unlawful unless one rules that the wash water is impure, then it spoils the whole even if it is more than the wash water, like a drop of wine falling into a tank. But Muhammad says: When he bathed in the small amount of water, all became musta'mal by legal fiction. End. This statement cleared the confusion and clarified every guess and conjecture, for it indicated that the implication of Muhammad's school is that water becomes musta'mal by mixing with a little musta'mal water, but Muhammad ruled that the whole became musta'mal by legal fiction, not in reality. So what is in al-Bada'i is interpreted as meaning that the implication of Muhammad's school is non-usage (i.e., it does not become musta'mal), but he says otherwise. And in al-Khulasah: A man performed wudu in a basin then poured that water into a well; he draws from it more than twenty buckets; and from what was poured into it, according to Muhammad and according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he draws all the well water because it is impure according to them. End. This indicates that the well water becomes musta'mal by the small amount of musta'mal water poured into it, so a fortiori if he performed wudu in it or bathed. I say: There has been much discussion among Hanafi students and scholars in our time and before regarding the permissibility of wudu from the small water basins placed in schools. Sheikh 'Allamah Qasim wrote a treatise on it called 'Raf' Mas'alat al-Miyah' and used as evidence what we mentioned from al-Bada'i. Some of his contemporaries agreed with him and issued fatwa accordingly, while others criticized him and wrote a treatise called 'Zahr al-Rawd fi Mas'alat al-Hawd' and pointed it out in his commentary on the poem of Ibn Wahban, saying: Do not be deceived by what our sheikh, the 'allamah, mentioned. His statement: (Cleared the confusion, etc.) His brother, the muhaqqiq, said in what was transmitted from him in the margins of this book according to some copies: 'Cleared the confusion' from its end, except that Muhammad says: When he bathed in the small amount of water, all became musta'mal by legal fiction. So we have two situations: one situation of musta'mal water falling into non-musta'mal water, in which the predominance of the non-musta'mal water is considered; the second situation is water that a person used for wudu or dipped his hand into for a need, which all becomes musta'mal by legal fiction, as you have seen. End. His statement: (So what is in al-Bada'i is interpreted as meaning that the implication of Muhammad's school is non-usage) meaning that the author of al-Bada'i attributed to Muhammad the opinion of non-usage based on what his school implies: that musta'mal water does not spoil water unless it overwhelms or equals it, but Muhammad did not say that which his school implied; rather, he said in this case that it becomes musta'mal by legal fiction, as stated by al-Dabusi. His statement: (And from what was poured into it) meaning that he also draws water from another well into which a bucket, for example, was poured from this well. It is said, and the more apparent is that it is considered in the twenty buckets and in what was poured: whichever is more, he draws, as will come in the rulings of wells. And if a mouse fell into a tank and the water was poured into the well, Muhammad said: He draws the greater of what was poured and of twenty buckets, and this is the most correct. Because if a mouse fell into it, he draws twenty; so likewise if what fell into it is poured into it, unless what was poured exceeds that, then he draws the extra with the twenty. End. His statement: (And he pointed it out in his commentary on the poem of Ibn Wahban, etc.) He is 'Allamah Ibn al-Shihnah, for he said in it, when discussing the issue of a person in a state of minor or major ritual impurity falling into a well, the text of which is: 'What is established is that the ruling differs according to the principles of our imams. The investigation is that drawing all the water is required according to the Imam based on the opinion of the impurity of musta'mal water; and it is said forty according to him. And the correct view of Muhammad's school is that it removes purifying quality, and this is the correct one from the Imam. The second view, and upon it fatwa is given, is that he draws twenty buckets from it to become purifying. This is on the view that necessity is not considered. But if necessity and repelling hardship are considered, then water does not become musta'mal in every place where necessity is realized. [؟]'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically discussing the ruling when a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) bathes in multiple wells consecutively. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, primarily between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, with later clarification from al-Dabusi and others. The ruling: Abu Yusuf holds that all wells become najis (impure) because the water from the first well is already contaminated by contact with the junub, and then each subsequent well becomes najis due to the water carried from the previous well. Muhammad holds that the person becomes pure after the third well, and the status of the water depends on whether there was actual physical impurity (ayn najasah) on his body. If yes, the water becomes najis; if no, it becomes musta'mal (used water), which according to Muhammad is still pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr tahur) in some views. The key point is that Muhammad makes a distinction: for the first three wells, the water becomes musta'mal due to direct contact; afterwards (fourth well onwards), it only becomes musta'mal if he has the intention (niyyah) for ghusl again, otherwise it remains pure. Abu Yusuf's view is more strict. The commentary by al-Dabusi clarifies that Muhammad's ruling is hukman (by legal fiction), not haqiqatan (in reality), meaning that even though the water is not actually all used, it is treated as such for legal purposes. The later discussion about wudu water poured into a well (from al-Khulasah) reinforces this: if musta'mal water is poured into a well, it does not necessarily spoil the whole well unless it overwhelms; but if one performs wudu directly in the well, it all becomes musta'mal. This shows the subtlety in Hanafi fiqh regarding water purity. The passage ends with a mention of later Hanafi scholars' opinions on practical issues like small water basins in schools, and the position that fatwa is given on drawing twenty buckets to restore purifying quality, but if necessity (darurah) is considered, the water does not become musta'mal.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a valid act of purification with intention; it is pure but not purifying according to the fatwa view.
غلبة (ghalabah): Predominance; when the added substance (musta'mal water or impurity) is greater in quantity or has changed the water's properties, it renders the whole like itself.
حكماً (hukman): By legal fiction; used to explain why direct use of water in a well renders the entire well musta'mal even though only a small part contacts the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa of later Hanafi scholars, what is the required action when a small amount of musta'mal water (e.g., from wudu) is poured into a well?
A) All the well water must be drawn out because it becomes najis.
B) More than twenty buckets should be drawn to restore purifying quality.
C) The well water remains pure and purifying; no action is needed.
D) Forty buckets must be drawn as per a minority view.

Key Takeaway
When musta'mal water is poured into a large body of water, it does not make the entire body najis; it becomes musta'mal, and drawing twenty buckets restores purifying quality.

When Does Water Become Musta'mal? The Hanafi Distinction Between Immersion and Pouring
Intra-Hanafi dispute on when water becomes musta'mal hukman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios of immersion and pouring, and apply the Hanafi ruling that immersion makes all water musta'mal hukman while pouring does not unless the used water prevails.

Core Idea
Immersion in water makes all of it musta'mal hukman; pouring used water does not affect the receiver unless it equals or prevails.

This passage addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute about when water becomes musta'mal (legally used). The distinction between immersion (direct body contact) and pouring (mixing used water) has practical implications for students using shared basins in schools or wells for purification. The author navigates through classical sources to establish the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the legal category of musta'mal water
Recall that musta'mal water is tahir but not tahur; it cannot be used for purification. This lesson focuses on when water attains this status.
Distinguish between haqiqatan (literally) and hukman (legally).
2
Recognize the two scenarios: immersion vs. pouring
Immersion (inghimas) occurs when a person in hadath directly contacts the water. Pouring (sabb) involves adding musta'mal water into pure water. These are treated differently in Hanafi fiqh.
The key is whether the body entered the water (mulāqī) or used water was added (mulqa).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference in the pouring case
According to Imam Muhammad, pouring musta'mal water into a well requires drawing only the greater of 20 buckets or the amount poured. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the entire well becomes najis and must be drained.
This difference is based on their view of the nature of musta'mal water.
4
Apply the ruling to the case of school basins
The author refutes Sheikh Qasim's opinion that immersion in a basin does not make all water musta'mal. Instead, the mufta bihi position is that immersion spreads the ruling hukman, so wudu from such basins is not valid without continuous fresh water.
Later Hanafi texts like Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Asrar support this.

Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning when water becomes musta'mal (used) through immersion or mixing. The author begins by clarifying the position of Imam Muhammad: when a small amount of musta'mal water is mixed with pure water, the entire mixture becomes musta'mal hukman (legally) not haqiqatan (literally). The author then relates a case from al-Khulasa: a man performs wudu in a basin and pours that water into a well. According to Imam Muhammad, one must draw out the greater of either 20 buckets or the amount poured in; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, all the well water must be drawn out because it becomes najis (impure) in their view. This indicates that the well water becomes musta'mal by the small used water, and a fortiori if one performs wudu or ghusl directly in the well. The author then discusses a contemporary debate about performing wudu from the small basins (fasāqī) in schools. Sheikh Qasim wrote a treatise permitting it, citing al-Bada'i', but others including Ibn al-Shihna and the author reject this. The author explains that al-Dabusi in al-Asrar presented the objection of Abu Yusuf to Muhammad and Muhammad's response, which shows that according to Muhammad, immersion makes all the water musta'mal hukman. The author supports this with references from al-Bada'i' (explicit statement that immersion makes water musta'mal according to all three imams), Fatawa Qadikhan (inserting hand corrupts the water), and a statement from al-Shurunbulali rejecting the idea that only the part touching the body becomes musta'mal. The author distinguishes between two cases: (1) when a person immerses or inserts a limb – the entire water becomes musta'mal hukman; (2) when musta'mal water is poured into pure water – the water does not become musta'mal unless the poured amount equals or prevails. The author refutes the claim that al-Asrar contains a weak narration from Muhammad, arguing that the evidence from al-Muhit and al-Siraj al-Hindi concerns only the case of pouring (mulqa), not contact (mulāqī). Thus, the author affirms that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that immersion makes all the water musta'mal hukman, and this applies to the school basins as well.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl by a person in a state of minor or major impurity; it is tahir but not tahur according to the Hanafi school (except for some positions).
حكماً (hukman): Legally treated as musta'mal, even though in reality only a part touched the body; the entire body of water is given the ruling of musta'mal.
نجس (najis): In this context, water becomes impure (najis) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf when musta'mal water is poured into it, because they consider the musta'mal water to be najis or to carry impurity.

Key Takeaway
Immersion in pure water makes all of it musta'mal hukman, even if only a limb enters; pouring used water does not affect the receiver unless it equals or prevails.
