Taharah — Purification
intermediate
15 min
Immersion vs. Pouring: The Spread of Isti'mal in Water
Intra-Hanafi debate on isti'mal by immersion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the legal effect of immersion (mulaqi) and pouring (mulqi) of used water, and state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on whether immersion renders water musta'mal.

Core Idea
Immersion (mulaqi) makes all water musta'mal by legal fiction; pouring (mulqi) only affects the poured portion unless it overwhelms.

This lesson examines a crucial intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens to water when a person immerses in it for purification. The majority of Hanafi imams hold that the entire body of water becomes musta'mal (used) by a legal fiction, even though only a part directly contacts the body. Others, relying on a weak narration from Imam Muhammad, argue that only the contacting part becomes musta'mal. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct rulings on reusing water for wudu or ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the dispute hinges on whether the person enters the water (mulaqi) or used water is added to clean water (mulqi). In immersion, the body enters the water; in pouring, already-used water is introduced. The Hanafi school distinguishes these two cases in the spread of isti'mal.
2
State the majority Hanafi position on immersion
According to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad's reliable narrations, immersion renders the entire body of water musta'mal by legal fiction (hukman). The effect spreads to all the water because the body is in it.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the opposing minority view
A weak narration from Muhammad and some later scholars (e.g., Zayn al-Din Qasim) argue that only the water directly contacting the body becomes musta'mal; the rest remains tahur. They analogize it to pouring used water into a larger quantity.
The author labels this riwaya da'ifa.
4
Apply the key distinction: mulqi vs. mulaqi
The majority responds that pouring (mulqi) is different because the used water is added from outside; thus only the poured part is musta'mal unless it overwhelms. Immersion (mulaqi) is different because the person's body enters the water, so the usage legally spreads. This distinction is supported by al-Dabusi and al-Shurunbulali.
The opponent denies this distinction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the majority view: immersion makes the water musta'mal. Practically, this means if you immerse in a small pool for ghusl, that water cannot be used for wudu or ghusl again. The minority view would allow reuse.
The korist of this ikhtilaf is directly practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الضرورة في الانغماس في الماء أو إدخال العضو فيه واعتبار الضرورة في مثل ذلك مذكور في الصغرى وغيرها ولا تغتر بما ذكره شيخنا العلامة زين الدين قاسم تغمده الله تعالى برحمته في رسالته المسماة برفع الاشتباه فإنه خالف فيها صريح المنقول عن أئمتنا واستند إلى كلام وقع في البدائع على سبيل البحث يوهم عدم صيرورة الماء القليل مستعملاً بالانغماس فيه لأن المستعمل منه ما لاقى بدن المحدث وهو قليل لاقى طهوراً أكثر منه فلا يسلبه وصف الطهورية، وتبعه على ذلك بعض من ينتحل مذهب الحنفية ممن لا رسوخ له في فقههم وكتب فيه كتابة مشتملة على خلط و خبط ومخالفة النصوص المنقولة عن محمد رحمه الله وقد بينت ذلك في مقدمة كتبتها حققت فيها المذهب في هذه المسألة والحاصل أن أبا زيد الدبوسي في كتاب الأسرار أورد ما ذكره في البدائع على سبيل الإلزام من أبي يوسف لمحمد رحمهما الله، وذكر جواب محمد عنه فكشف اللبس وأوضح كل تخمين وحدس فإنه قال بعد ذكر مذاهب علمائنا في الماء المستعمل : والاستدلال لمحمد وعامة مشايخنا ينصرون قول محمد وروايته عن أبي حنيفة ثم قال يحتج للقول الآخر بما روي فذكر حديث لا يبولن أحدكم ثم قال ومن قال إن الماء المستعمل طاهر طهور لا يجعل الاغتسال فيه حراماً إلى آخر ما قدمه الشارح هنا عن الدبوسي وفي البدائع أيضاً: التصريح بأن الطاهر إذا انغمس في البئر للاغتسال صار مستعملاً عند أصحابنا الثلاثة. وصرح في فتاوى قاضيخان بأن إدخال اليد في الإناء للغسل يفسد الماء عند أئمتنا الثلاثة، وتكفل بإيضاح هذا وتحريره رسالتي المسماة بزهر الروض في مسألة الحوض وما كتبته بعد ذلك حين رؤية ما أفتى به بعض أصحابنا فانظره اهـ. وقال العلامة الشيخ حسن الشرنبلالي في شرحه على الوهبانية: وما ذكر أن الاستعمال بالجزء الذي يلاقي جسده دون باقي الماء فيصير ذلك الجزء مستهلكاً في كثير فهو مردود لسريان الاستعمال في الجميع حكماً وليس كالغالب بصب القليل من الماء فيه اهـ. أنه لما انغمس أو أدخل يده مثلاً صار مستعملاً لجميع ذلك الماء الذي انغمس فيه أو أدخل يده فيه حكماً لأن المستعمل حقيقة هو ما لاقى جسده وذلك بخلاف ما إذا صب المستعمل فيه فإن المستعمل حقيقة وحكماً هو ذلك الملقى فلا وجه للحكم على الملقى فيه بالاستعمال ما لم يساوه أو يغلب عليه إذ لم يدخل فيه جسده حتى يحكم عليه بالاستعمال حكماً يدل عليه ما الأسرار تي للدبوسي. وقولهم في مسألة البئر جحط لو انعمس بقصد الاغتسال للصلاة صار الماء مستعملاً اتفاقاً، وأما ما ادعاه الشارح من أن ما في الأسرار رواية ضعيفة عن محمد مستدلاً بما نقله عن المحيط والسراج الهندي فهو مبني على دعوى عدم الفرق بين ما لاقاه المستعمل أو ألقى فيه وإلا فلا دلالة فيه على ذلك لأن ما ذكره في المحيط والهندي في الملقى ولا كلام فيه، وإنما الكلام في الملاقي فيحتاج إلى إثبات عدم الفرق وليس في شيء مما ذكره من النقول ما يثبته. قوله : (فأقول وبالله التوفيق أقول : إن كان الخلاف الذي جرى بين أهل العصر في جواز التوضؤ من الفساقي من يعني إن ما ذكره في البدائع صريح في عدم صيرورة الماء القليل مستعملاً باختلاط المستعمل الأقل منه به، وكذا ما ذكره الشارحون كالزيلعي والمحقق الكمال والسراج الهندي في بحث الماء المقيد كما نقلناه صريح في ذلك. وأما ما ذكره الدبوسي في الأسرار وما ذكره في الخلاصة وغيرها من نزح عشرين دلواً، وما ذكره الأكمل وشراح الهداية من كونه يفسد عند الكل، وما ذكره القاضي الاسبيجابي والولوالجي عن محمد فكله مبني على رواية ضعيفة عن محمد لا على الصحيح من مذهب محمد، وسيظهر لك صدق هذه الدعوى الصادقة بالبينة العادلة. قال في المحيط : وإذا وقع الماء المستعمل في البئر يفسد الماء وينزح كله عند أبي يوسف لأنه نجس، وعند محمد لا يفسد ويجوز التوضؤ به ما لم يغلب على الماء وهو الصحيح لأن الماء المستعمل طاهر غير طهور فصار كالماء المقيد إذا اختلط بالماء المطلق ا هـ بلفظه . وقال الشيخ العلامة المحقق سراج الدين الهندي في شرح الهداية : إذا وقع الماء المستعمل في البئر لا يفسد عند محمد، ويجوز الوضوء به ما لم يغلب على الماء وهو الصحيح كالماء المقيد إذا اختلط بالماء المطلق. وفي التحفة : يجوز الوضوء به ما لم يغلب على الماء على المذهب المختار. وإذا وقع الماء المستعمل في الماء المطلق القليل قال بعضهم : لا يجوز الوضوء به بخلاف بول الشاة أن كلاً منهما طاهر عند محمد والفرق له أن الماء المستعمل من جنس ماء البئر فلا يستهلك فيه والبول ليس من جنسه فيعتبر الغالب فيه. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : لو صب الماء المستعمل في بئر ينزح منها عشرون دلواً لأنه طاهر عنده وكان دون الفأرة، وهذا على القول الذي لا يجوز استعمال ماء البئر . اهـ كلام العلامة السراج. فقد استفيد من هذا فوائد منها أن المشايخ اختلفوا في الماء القليل المستعمل إذا اختلط بالماء المطلق الأكثر منه القليل في نفسه ؛ مع وعدمه مطلقاً، سواء كان بانغماس بجسد أو يد أو بغيره، فلا كلام في أن ما ذكره من النقول يدل على مدعاه من الجواز فعبارة البدائع تدل على الجواز في الانغماس وغيرها في غيره. وأما إذا كان الخلاف في أنه بالانغماس يصير الماء مستعملاً بخلاف ما إذا كان بغيره كما هو ظاهر عبارة الشرنبلالي التي ذكرناها آنفاً وأيدناها بما ذكره عن الدبوسي، وهو ظاهر ما يأتي في قوله وإذا عرفت هذا الخ» فإنه يدل على أن الخلاف في الملقى والملاقي فما ذكره من النقول لا يدل على عدم الاستعمال بالملاقي سوى ما قدمه عن البدائع فإنه يدل عليه ولكن قد علمت ما فيه مما نقلناه عن ابن الشحنة وأما غير عبارة البدائع فهو في الملقى وقد علمت أنه لا نزاع فيه، ولذا قال أخو الشارح فيما نقل عنه في هوامش هذا الكتاب عند قوله الآتي «قال في المحيط الخ» ما نصه : لا يخفاك أن العبارة في وقوع الماء لا المغتسل، وكذا فيما بعده اهـ. وكذا ما نقلنا عنه سابقاً وكأنه استدل بذلك بناء على ما سيذكره من عدم الفرق بينهما. وإذا ثبت ذلك يصح ولكن الكلام في ذلك فإن الخصم لا يسلم عدم الفرق فتأمل في هذا المقام فإنه من مزال الأقدام
The necessity of immersion in water or inserting a limb into it, and consideration of necessity in such matters is mentioned in al-Sughra and others. Do not be deceived by what our teacher, the Allamah Zayn al-Din Qasim (may Allah envelop him in His mercy) mentioned in his treatise called Raf' al-Ishtibah, for he contradicted in it the explicit transmitted (manqul) from our imams, relying on words that occurred in al-Bada'i' by way of investigation (bahth) that give the impression that a small quantity of water does not become musta'mal (used) by immersion in it, because what is musta'mal is that which contacted the body of a hadath-person, and it is a small amount that contacted a larger amount of pure water, so it does not strip it of the description of being purifying (tahur). Some individuals who affiliate with the Hanafi school but have no deep roots in its fiqh followed him on that, and wrote a treatise containing confusion, disorder, and contradiction of the transmitted texts from Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). I have clarified that in an introduction I wrote, in which I verified the school on this issue. The conclusion is that Abu Zayd al-Dabusi in his book al-Asrar presented what was mentioned in al-Bada'i' by way of lizam (binding argument) from Abu Yusuf to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), and mentioned Muhammad's response to it, thus removing the confusion and clarifying every speculation and guess. For he said after mentioning the views of our scholars on musta'mal water: 'The evidence for Muhammad, and the majority of our mashayikh support the statement of Muhammad and his narration from Abu Hanifa.' Then he said: 'The other view is argued based on what was narrated' and mentioned the hadith 'None of you should urinate...' then said: 'And whoever says that musta'mal water is tahir (pure) and tahur (purifying) does not deem bathing in it as haram...' up to what the commentator (sharh) has presented here from al-Dabusi. Also in al-Bada'i', there is an explicit statement that if a pure person immerses in a well to bathe, it becomes musta'mal according to our three imams. And it is explicitly stated in Fatawa Qadikhan that inserting the hand into a vessel for washing spoils the water according to our three imams. My treatise called Zahr al-Rawd on the issue of the tank (hawd), and what I wrote after that upon seeing the fatwa of some of our colleagues, suffice for clarifying and establishing this — so look at it. And the Allamah Shaykh Hasan al-Shurunbulali said in his commentary on al-Wahbaniyya: 'What is mentioned that isti'mal (usage) applies only to the part that contacts his body, not the rest of the water, so that part becomes consumed (mustahlak) in the larger quantity, is rejected because usage spreads to all of it legally (hukman), and it is not like the dominant case of pouring a small amount of water into it.' That is, when he immerses or inserts his hand, for example, all of that water in which he immersed or inserted his hand becomes musta'mal legally, because musta'mal in reality is what contacted his body, and this is different from the case where used water is poured into it, for then the used water in reality and legally is that which is poured, so there is no basis to rule on the water into which it is poured as musta'mal unless it equals or overwhelms it, since his body did not enter it so as to rule on it as musta'mal legally. This is indicated by what is in al-Asrar of al-Dabusi. And their statement in the well issue: 'If he immerses with the intention of bathing for prayer, the water becomes musta'mal by agreement.' As for what the commentator claimed, that what is in al-Asrar is a weak narration from Muhammad, using as evidence what he transmitted from al-Muhit and al-Siraj al-Hindi, it is based on the claim that there is no difference between what is contacted by used water or that into which it is poured; otherwise, there is no evidence for that, because what al-Muhit and al-Hindi mentioned is about the poured (mulqa), and there is no dispute about that. The dispute is only about the contacting (mulaqi), so one needs to prove no difference, and nothing in the quotations he mentioned establishes that. His statement: 'I say, and with Allah is success: I say: If the dispute that occurred among the contemporaries about the permissibility of performing wudu from the fasaqi (water channels?)...' meaning that what was mentioned in al-Bada'i' is explicit that a small quantity of water does not become musta'mal by mixing with a smaller amount of musta'mal water. Similarly, what the commentators like al-Zayla'i, al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal, and al-Siraj al-Hindi mentioned in the discussion of restricted water (al-ma' al-muqayyad) as we transmitted is explicit on that. As for what al-Dabusi mentioned in al-Asrar, what was mentioned in al-Khulasa and others about drawing twenty buckets, and what al-Akmal and the commentators of al-Hidayah mentioned that it becomes spoiled according to all, and what al-Qadi al-Isbijabi and al-Walwaliji mentioned from Muhammad — all of it is based on a weak narration from Muhammad, not on the correct view of Muhammad's school. And you will soon see the truth of this truthful claim with just evidence. It is stated in al-Muhit: 'When musta'mal water falls into a well, it spoils the water and all of it must be drawn out according to Abu Yusuf because it is najis. According to Muhammad, it does not spoil, and it is permissible to perform wudu with it as long as it does not overwhelm the water — and this is the correct view, because musta'mal water is tahir (pure) but not tahur (purifying), so it becomes like restricted water (al-ma' al-muqayyad) when mixed with unrestricted water (al-ma' al-mutlaq).' End of his words. And the Allamah, the Muhaqqiq Siraj al-Din al-Hindi said in his commentary on al-Hidayah: 'When musta'mal water falls into a well, it does not spoil according to Muhammad, and it is permissible to perform wudu with it as long as it does not overwhelm the water — and this is the correct view, like restricted water when mixed with unrestricted water.' And in al-Tuhfa: 'It is permissible to perform wudu with it as long as it does not overwhelm the water, according to the chosen view (al-madhhab al-mukhtar).' And when musta'mal water falls into a small quantity of unrestricted water, some said it is not permissible to perform wudu with it, unlike the urine of a sheep, because each is tahir according to Muhammad, and the difference for him is that musta'mal water is of the same kind as well water, so it does not become consumed (mustahlik) in it, while urine is not of its kind, so it is considered by what is dominant. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: 'If musta'mal water is poured into a well, twenty buckets are drawn from it because it is tahir according to him, and it is less than a mouse. This is according to the view that does not permit using well water.' End of the words of Allamah Siraj. Benefits are derived from this: one of them is that the mashayikh differed concerning a small quantity of musta'mal water when mixed with a larger quantity of unrestricted water that is itself small; and its non-occurrence absolutely, whether by immersion of body or hand or otherwise. So there is no doubt that what he mentioned of quotations supports his claim of permissibility — the phrase of al-Bada'i' indicates permissibility regarding immersion, and others indicate permissibility in other cases. But if the dispute is that by immersion the water becomes musta'mal, unlike the case where it is by other means — as is apparent from the statement of al-Shurunbulali we mentioned earlier and supported by what al-Dabusi stated — and it is apparent from what follows in his statement 'And when you know this...' that the dispute is about the poured (mulqa) and the contacting (mulaqi). So what he mentioned of quotations does not indicate the non-occurrence of isti'mal by the contacting (mulaqi), except what he presented from al-Bada'i', for it does indicate it, but you already know what is in it from what we transmitted from Ibn al-Shihna. As for other than the phrase of al-Bada'i', it is about the poured (mulqa), and you already know there is no dispute about it. That is why the brother of the commentator said in what is transmitted from him in the margins of this book at the commentary's upcoming statement 'He said in al-Muhit...': 'It is not hidden from you that the phrase is about the falling of water, not the bather, and similarly in what follows.' And similarly what we transmitted from him earlier — as if he argued by that based on what he will mention about no difference between them. If that is established, it is correct, but the problem is that the opponent does not accept the absence of difference. So reflect on this place, for it is a slippery ground.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the legal effect of immersion (inghimas) in water versus simply pouring used water (musta'mal) into clean water. The author (likely Ibn Nujaym) vigorously defends the majority view that immersion renders the entire body of water legally musta'mal (used) by legal fiction (hukman), even though in reality only the part contacting the body is directly used. He contrasts this with the case of pouring used water into clean water, where only the poured water is considered musta'mal unless it overwhelms the clean water. The author warns against following a weak narration attributed to Imam Muhammad that suggests immersion does not render water musta'mal. He cites authorities like al-Dabusi, al-Shurunbulali, and al-Siraj al-Hindi to support the majority position. The key distinction is between mulqi (that which is poured) and mulaqi (that which contacts), a distinction the opponent denies. The author declares that the opposing view relies on a weak narration (riwaya da'ifa) from Muhammad, while the correct position of Muhammad (as per Zahir al-Riwayah) is that immersion does cause isti'mal. The passage ends with a note that the opponent does not concede the distinction, making the issue a slippery slope.

Key Terms
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for the purpose of removing ritual impurity (hadath) or physical impurity (najasa), thus losing its purifying property (tahuriyya) but remaining tahir (pure) in the Hanafi school.
الملاقي (al-mulaqi): That which contacts water; in this context, a person who immerses or inserts a limb into water, making the entire water musta'mal by legal fiction.
الملقى (al-mulqa): That which is thrown into water; i.e., used water that is poured into clean water. In this case, only the poured water is musta'mal unless it overwhelms the clean water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on water when a person immerses their entire body in a small pool for ghusl?
A) The water becomes najis (impure).
B) The water becomes musta'mal (used) and retains its purifying property (tahur).
C) The water becomes musta'mal (used) and loses its purifying property (tahur), but remains tahir (pure).
D) The water remains completely unchanged because the used part is negligible.

Key Takeaway
Immersion (mulaqi) legally renders all water musta'mal by legal fiction; pouring (mulqi) only affects the poured portion unless it overwhelms — a distinction that determines the water's usability for future purification.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Musta'mal Water Mixed with Mutlaq Water: The Correct Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi dispute on musta'mal water mixing with mutlaq water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi ruling on mixing musta'mal water with mutlaq water and distinguish it from the weak opinion, citing the tarjih authority.

Core Idea
Musta'mal water is pure but not purifying; mixing it with mutlaq water does not render the mixture impure unless it dominates.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates an internal Hanafi dispute about the effect of mixing water used for wudu (musta'mal) with pure absolute water (mutlaq). While Abu Yusuf held that musta'mal is impure and spoils the mixture, the correct and mufta bihi position—from Imam Muhammad and endorsed by later authorities—is that musta'mal water is tahir (pure) but not tahur (purifying). Therefore, the mixture remains permissible for wudu as long as the musta'mal component does not dominate. Understanding this ruling requires tracing the competing narrations and the tarjih that settled the school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is the mixing of musta'mal water (used for wudu) with mutlaq water (pure, absolute water). The dispute is whether this mixing renders the whole mixture impure or merely non-purifying.
The ruling concerns the permissibility of using such a mixture for wudu.
2
Locate the two main positions
Abu Yusuf holds that musta'mal water is impure (najis), so the mixture becomes impure and cannot be used. The correct position from Muhammad is that musta'mal is pure but not purifying; the mixture remains pure unless musta'mal dominates.
A weak narration from Muhammad also claims impurity, but it is rejected.
3
Analyze the tarjih evidence
Authorities like al-Muhit, al-Tuhfah, and Ibn al-Humam prefer Muhammad's position, analogizing musta'mal to restricted water (muqayyad) when mixed with absolute water.
The key distinction: musta'mal is like water mixed with a pure substance of the same kind, so it does not alter the ruling unless it becomes the majority.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If the musta'mal water does not dominate the mixture, wudu is valid. If it dominates, the mixture takes the ruling of musta'mal (tahir but not tahur), so wudu is not valid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf—the practical difference between the opinions.

إن ما ذكره في البدائع صريح في عدم صيرورة الماء القليل مستعملاً باختلاط المستعمل الأقل منه به، وكذا ما ذكره الشارحون كالزيلعي والمحقق الكمال والسراج الهندي في بحث الماء المقيد كما نقلناه صريح في ذلك. وأما ما ذكره الدبوسي في الأسرار وما ذكره في الخلاصة وغيرها من نزح عشرين دلواً، وما ذكره الأكمل وشراح الهداية من كونه يفسد عند الكل، وما ذكره القاضي الاسبيجابي والولوالجي عن محمد فكله مبني على رواية ضعيفة عن محمد لا على الصحيح من مذهب محمد، وسيظهر لك صدق هذه الدعوى الصادقة بالبينة العادلة. قال في المحيط : وإذا وقع الماء المستعمل في البئر يفسد الماء وينزح كله عند أبي يوسف لأنه نجس، وعند محمد لا يفسد ويجوز التوضؤ به ما لم يغلب على الماء وهو الصحيح لأن الماء المستعمل طاهر غير طهور فصار كالماء المقيد إذا اختلط بالماء المطلق ا هـ بلفظه . وقال الشيخ العلامة المحقق سراج الدين الهندي في شرح الهداية : إذا وقع الماء المستعمل في البئر لا يفسد عند محمد، ويجوز الوضوء به ما لم يغلب على الماء وهو الصحيح كالماء المقيد إذا اختلط بالماء المطلق. وفي التحفة : يجوز الوضوء به ما لم يغلب على الماء على المذهب المختار. وإذا وقع الماء المستعمل في الماء المطلق القليل قال بعضهم : لا يجوز الوضوء به بخلاف بول الشاة أن كلاً منهما طاهر عند محمد والفرق له أن الماء المستعمل من جنس ماء البئر فلا يستهلك فيه والبول ليس من جنسه فيعتبر الغالب فيه. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : لو صب الماء المستعمل في بئر ينزح منها عشرون دلواً لأنه طاهر عنده وكان دون الفأرة، وهذا على القول الذي لا يجوز استعمال ماء البئر . اهـ كلام العلامة السراج. فقد استفيد من هذا فوائد منها أن المشايخ اختلفوا في الماء القليل المستعمل إذا اختلط بالماء المطلق الأكثر منه القليل في نفسه ؛
مع
وعدمه مطلقاً، سواء كان بانغماس بجسد أو يد أو بغيره، فلا كلام في أن ما ذكره من النقول يدل على مدعاه من الجواز فعبارة البدائع تدل على الجواز في الانغماس وغيرها في غيره. وأما إذا كان الخلاف في أنه بالانغماس يصير الماء مستعملاً بخلاف ما إذا كان بغيره كما هو ظاهر عبارة الشرنبلالي التي ذكرناها آنفاً وأيدناها بما ذكره عن الدبوسي، وهو ظاهر ما يأتي في قوله وإذا عرفت هذا الخ» فإنه يدل على أن الخلاف في الملقى والملاقي فما ذكره من النقول لا يدل على عدم الاستعمال بالملاقي سوى ما قدمه عن البدائع فإنه يدل عليه ولكن قد علمت ما فيه مما نقلناه عن ابن الشحنة وأما غير عبارة البدائع فهو في الملقى وقد علمت أنه لا نزاع فيه، ولذا قال أخو الشارح فيما نقل عنه في هوامش هذا الكتاب عند قوله الآتي «قال في المحيط الخ» ما نصه : لا يخفاك أن العبارة في وقوع الماء لا المغتسل، وكذا فيما بعده اهـ. وكذا ما نقلنا عنه سابقاً وكأنه استدل بذلك بناء على ما سيذكره من عدم الفرق بينهما. وإذا ثبت ذلك يصح ولكن الكلام في ذلك فإن الخصم لا يسلم عدم الفرق فتأمل في هذا المقام فإنه من مزال الأقدام
الاستدلال

فمنهم من قال يصير الكل مستعملاً عند محمد فيحتاج إلى الفرق بينه وبين بول الشاة فأفاد الفرق بقوله «والفرق له إلى آخره وهي الفائدة الثانية . ومنهم من قال : لا يصير مستعملاً ما لم يغلب
على المطلق وصححه صاحب المحيط والعلامة كما رأيت ونقل العلامة عن التحفة أنه المختار . ومنها حمل ما نقله قاضيخان وغيره من نزح عشرين دلواً على القول الضعيف، أما على القول الصحيح فلا ينزح شيء فإذا علمت هذا تعين عليك حمل قول من نقل عدم الجواز على القول الضعيف لا الصحيح كما فعله العلامة وأما ما في كثير من الكتب من أن الجنب إذا أدخل يده أو رجله في الماء فسد الماء فهذا محمول على الرواية القائلة بنجاسة الماء المستعمل لا على المختارة للفتوى لأن ملاقاة النجس للماء القليل تقتضي نجاسته لا ملاقاة الطاهر له، وقد كشف عن هذا ختام المحققين العلامة كمال الدين بن الهمام في شرح الهداية حجاب الأستار فقال : حوضان صغيران يخرج الماء من أحدهما ويدخل في الآخر فتوضأ في خلال ذلك جاز لأنه جار، وكذا إذا قطع الجاري من فوق وقد بقي جري الماء كان جائزاً أن يتوضأ بما يجري في النهر. وذكر في فتاوى قاضيان في المسألة الأولى قال : والماء الذي اجتمع في الحفيرة الثانية فاسد وهذا مطلقاً إنما هو بناء على كون المستعمل نجساً، وكذا كثير من أشباه هذا. فأما على من رواية أنه طاهر غير طهور ،فلا فلتحفظ ليفرع عليها ولا يفتى بمثل هذه الفروع . ا هـ كلام المحقق.
Book of Purification. Indeed, what he mentioned in al-Bada'i' is explicit about water (little) not becoming musta'mal by mixing with musta'mal that is less than it, and likewise what the commentators like al-Zayla'i, al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal, and al-Siraj al-Hindi mentioned in the discussion of restricted water as we quoted is explicit about that. As for what al-Dabusi mentioned in al-Asrar and what was mentioned in al-Khulasa and others about drawing twenty bucketfuls, and what al-Akmal and the commentators of al-Hidayah mentioned about it becoming corrupted according to all, and what al-Qadi al-Isbijabi and al-Walwalji mentioned from Muhammad, all of it is based on a weak narration from Muhammad, not on the correct (opinion) from Muhammad's school, and you will see the truth of this claim with just evidence. He said in al-Muhit: If musta'mal water falls into a well, it corrupts the water and all of it is drawn (removed) according to Abu Yusuf because it is impure; according to Muhammad it does not corrupt and it is permissible to perform wudu with it as long as it does not dominate the water, and this is the correct (opinion) because musta'mal water is pure but not purifying, so it becomes like restricted water when mixed with absolute water. End quote. And Shaykh al-Alama al-Muhaqqiq Siraj al-Din al-Hindi said in Sharh al-Hidayah: If musta'mal water falls into a well, it does not corrupt according to Muhammad, and wudu with it is permissible as long as it does not dominate the water, and this is the correct (opinion) like restricted water when mixed with absolute water. And in al-Tuhfah: Wudu with it is permissible as long as it does not dominate the water according to the chosen school. If musta'mal water falls into little absolute water, some said: wudu with it is not permissible, contrary to sheep urine, since each of them is pure according to Muhammad, but the distinction is that musta'mal water is of the same kind as well water so it is not consumed in it, while urine is not of its kind so the dominant (one) is considered. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: If one pours musta'mal water into a well, twenty bucketfuls are drawn because it is pure according to him and it was less than a mouse, and this is according to the opinion that does not permit using well water. End quote of Alama al-Siraj. Benefits are derived from this, among them that the shuyukh differed concerning little musta'mal water when mixed with more absolute water: whether it becomes musta'mal in itself or not absolutely, whether by immersion of body or hand or otherwise. There is no dispute that what he mentioned of quotations indicates his claim of permissibility; the phrase of al-Bada'i' indicates permissibility in immersion and others in other (cases). But if the dispute is that by immersion it becomes musta'mal unlike by anything else, as is apparent from the phrase of al-Sharnbalali we mentioned earlier and supported by what he mentioned from al-Dabusi, and it is apparent from what comes in his saying 'And if you understood this...' then it indicates that the dispute is about the thrown (water) and the meeting (object). So what he mentioned of quotations does not indicate non-usage by the meeting except what he presented from al-Bada'i', which does indicate it, but you have known what is in it from what we quoted from Ibn al-Shihna. Other than the phrase of al-Bada'i', it is about the thrown, and you know there is no dispute about it. Therefore the brother of the commentator said in what was quoted from him in the margins of this book at his coming saying 'He said in al-Muhit...' the text: It is not hidden from you that the phrase is about the falling of water, not the person washing, and likewise in what follows. And likewise what we quoted earlier, and it is as if he deduced from that based on what he will mention of no difference between them. If that is established, it is correct, but the discussion is about that, for the opponent does not concede lack of difference, so reflect on this place, for it is a place of slipping feet. Istidlal (deduction). Then some said: all becomes musta'mal according to Muhammad, so he needs to distinguish between it and sheep urine, so he provided the distinction with his saying 'and the distinction for him' etc., and that is the second benefit. And some said: it does not become musta'mal as long as it does not dominate the absolute water, and this was corrected by the author of al-Muhit and the Alama as you saw, and the Alama quoted from al-Tuhfah that it is the chosen (opinion). And among them is carrying what Qadikhan and others narrated about drawing twenty bucketfuls on the weak opinion. As for the correct opinion, nothing is drawn. So when you know this, you must carry the statement of those who narrate impermissibility on the weak opinion, not the correct, as the Alama did. As for what is in many books that if a junub puts his hand or foot in water, the water becomes spoiled, this is carried on the narration saying that musta'mal water is impure, not on the chosen (opinion) for fatwa, because the meeting of an impurity with little water necessitates its impurity, not the meeting of a pure thing with it. And this was uncovered by the seal of the investigators, the Alama Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam in Sharh al-Hidayah Hijab al-Asrar. He said: Two small basins, water exits from one and enters the other, and one performs wudu in between, it is permissible because it is flowing. Likewise, if the flowing water is cut from above while the flow of water remains, it is permissible to perform wudu with what flows in the river. And he mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan in the first issue: The water that collects in the second pit is spoiled, and this absolutely is only based on considering musta'mal water impure. Likewise many similar cases. As for the narration that it is pure but not purifying, then no, so let it be memorized to derive branches from it, and do not give fatwa with such branches. End quote of the investigator.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school) regarding the ruling on musta'mal water (water used for wudu) when it mixes with mutlaq water (pure, absolute water). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and expanding on the different opinions. The main issue: does musta'mal water render the mixture impure or simply non-purifying? The passage clarifies that the correct opinion in the school (al-mukhtar) is that musta'mal water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (tahirun la tawhoor). Therefore, when it mixes with mutlaq water, it does not make the mixture impure; rather, it is permissible to use the mixture for wudu as long as the musta'mal water does not dominate (ghalaba) the mutlaq water. This is the position of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which is considered the sahih (correct) and mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa). The passage notes that other transmissions from Muhammad are weak and should not be followed. It also addresses a secondary distinction: whether the mixing occurs by immersion (ighitimas) or by pouring (sabb). Some scholars said that immersion renders the water musta'mal throughout, while pouring does not. However, the author prefers the view that there is no difference; the key is whether the musta'mal water dominates the mutlaq. The passage concludes with a quote from Ibn al-Humam supporting the correct opinion and warning against giving fatwa based on the weak narration that considers musta'mal water impure.

Key Terms
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl, which is considered pure but not purifying (according to the correct Hanafi opinion).
الماء المطلق (al-ma' al-mutlaq): Pure, absolute water that has not been used or mixed with anything that alters its properties.
طاهر غير طهور (tahir ghayr tahur): Pure in itself but not capable of purifying other things (e.g., cannot be used for wudu).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi opinion, what is the ruling on a mixture of musta'mal water and mutlaq water when the musta'mal does not dominate?
A) The mixture is impure and cannot be used for wudu.
B) The mixture is pure but not purifying, so wudu is invalid.
C) The mixture is pure and purifying, so wudu is valid.
D) The mixture is pure but wudu is only valid if the musta'mal was added by immersion.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position is that musta'mal water is pure but not purifying; mixing it with mutlaq water does not render the mixture impure unless the musta'mal dominates.

Methodological Principles: Understanding Implicit Conditions and the Basis of Rulings
Methodological reflection with a concrete fiqh application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methodological principles for understanding fiqh rulings and apply them to analyze a common error about musta'mal water.

Core Idea
Understanding the wajh of a ruling prevents error; ignore it and you'll confuse similar cases.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq by Ibn Nujaym provides two essential principles for any serious student of fiqh. First, the apparently absolute statements of jurists are usually qualified by implicit conditions that the trained student must recognize. Second, many rulings are based on a discernible reason (wajh), and knowing that reason is key to applying the ruling correctly. Ibn Nujaym then applies these principles to expose a flawed argument about musta'mal water, showing how neglect of the underlying basis leads to error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two principles
Read the opening lines and extract the two methodological principles introduced by Ibn Nujaym: (1) mutlaq statements are often muqayyad by implicit conditions, (2) rulings have a wajh that must be known.
The first principle is about the nature of itlaqat; the second is about the rationality of fiqh rulings.
2
Recognize the implicit conditions
Reflect on examples from your own study: how many rulings have hidden conditions that the jurist assumed the reader knows? This principle warns against literalism.
E.g., 'water is pure' may be restricted to water not changed by usage.
3
Apply to the musta'mal case
Ibn Nujaym applies the principles to critique a contemporary error: some distinguish between pouring and immersion for musta'mal water. Trace his argument step by step.
The error stems from not knowing the wajh (dominance) and taking absolute statements superficially.
4
Analyze the faulty analogy
Identify the flawed reasoning: the claim that mixing is different. Ibn Nujaym refutes it by showing mixing is identical in both cases. Understand why the wajh (dominance) is the same.
The only relevant factor is whether the mutlaq water dominates, not the method.
5
Derive the correct ruling
Conclude that the correct ruling depends solely on dominance of the mutlaq water. If musta'mal dominates, the mixture is musta'mal; if mutlaq dominates, it remains mutlaq.
This aligns with the chosen narration that musta'mal water is tahir ghayr mutahhir.

And from here it is known that understanding the issues in a precise way requires knowledge of two principles: One of them is that the absolute statements of the jurists are in most cases restricted by conditions that are known by the person of sound understanding who practices the usul and furu', and they remain silent about them relying on the sound understanding of the student. The second is that these issues are ijtihadi, reasonable in meaning; the ruling is not known completely except by knowing the basis (wajh) of the ruling on which it is built and from which it branches. Otherwise, the issues become confusing for the student and his mind becomes perplexed due to lack of knowledge of the basis and foundation. Whoever neglects what we mentioned becomes lost in error and mistake. And when you know this, the weakness becomes apparent to you of those who say in our time that if musta'mal water is poured on absolute water and the absolute water is dominant, wudu with the whole is permissible, but if one performs wudu in a cistern, the whole becomes musta'mal, as there is no meaning to the difference between the two issues. And what might be imagined as the difference – that in wudu the usage spreads to all unlike in pouring – is refuted because the dissemination and mixing are the same in both cases. Rather, one may say: throwing the washing water from outside is stronger in effect than other (ways) because the used water is specified by visual observation and identification, and the separateness of the separation. In short, no difference is understood between the chosen (opinion). And Allah Almighty is the inspirer of guidance. His statement: 'As for the chosen from the narration that it is pure but not purifying, then no.' His brother said in what was quoted from him: that is, one should not say spoiled, but rather it is pure but not purifying, and it is from heedlessness of understanding the words of the scholars. Commentary
This passage provides a methodological reflection on how to properly understand fiqh rulings. It identifies two foundational principles: (1) The general statements of jurists are often qualified by implicit conditions that the trained student should recognize; (2) Many fiqh rulings are based on discernible reasons (wajh), and understanding these reasons is essential to apply the rulings correctly to new cases. The author then applies these principles to critique a contemporary error: some people claim that pouring musta'mal water onto mutlaq water is permissible for wudu, but if one performs wudu directly in a tank (fisqiyya), the entire tank becomes musta'mal and invalid. The author argues that this distinction is baseless because the physical mixing is identical in both cases. In fact, pouring may have a stronger effect because the used water is visually distinct. Therefore, the correct position is that the ruling depends on whether the musta'mal water dominates, regardless of the method of contact. The passage ends with a remark clarifying that the term 'spoiled' (fasad) applies only to the weak narration that considers musta'mal water impure; on the correct narration, it is simply pure but not purifying.

Key Terms
وجه الحكم (wajh al-hukm): The underlying reason or basis upon which a fiqh ruling is built, enabling proper analogical reasoning.
الإطلاقات (al-itlaqat): Absolute or unqualified statements made by jurists that are implicitly restricted by conditions known to the trained student.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary factor that determines whether a mixture of musta'mal and mutlaq water can be used for wudu?
A) Whether the mixing occurred by pouring or by immersion.
B) Whether the musta'mal water was used by a junub or a non-junub.
C) Whether the musta'mal water dominates the mutlaq water.
D) Whether the mutlaq water is from a well or a cistern.

Key Takeaway
To understand fiqh rulings correctly, one must recognize implicit conditions in jurists' statements and seek the underlying reason (wajh) of each ruling.

Ruling on Used Water Mixed with Pure Water in a Basin
Commentary establishing the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on used water in basins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on used water mixed with pure water in a basin and apply the condition that used water must not be predominant for wudu to be valid.

Core Idea
Used water is pure but not purifying; mixing it does not spoil pure water unless the used water becomes predominant.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical concern: what is the ruling when used water from wudu collects in a small basin and mixes with fresh water? The commentator navigates between weak and strong opinions, clarifies the crucial distinction between used water and impurity, and provides principles to resolve confusion. By the end, you will understand the relied-upon Hanafi position and the conditions under which wudu remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What happens when used water (water that has been used for wudu or ghusl) mixes with fresh pure water? Does it spoil the whole body of water?
The answer depends on the legal status of used water: is it najis, or merely tahir ghayr mutahhir?
2
Distinguish the two intra-Hanafi opinions
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, used water becomes najis and spoils everything it touches. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it remains pure but loses its purifying ability. The text adopts the latter as the corrected opinion.
The weaker opinion leads to many restrictions; the stronger one allows ease.
3
Apply the distinction to the basin scenario
If used water is not najis, its mere presence does not render the basin's water impure. The water is still pure (tahir) and can be used for wudu, provided the used water does not predominate.
Predominance means the used water is more in quantity or equal to the pure water, or one strongly believes so.
4
Recognize the key principles
The commentator extracts two principles: jurists' general statements are implicitly qualified, and these rulings are based on rational meanings (ma'qul al-ma'na) that must be understood to avoid error.
This encourages deep understanding rather than blind following of surface statements.
5
Refute the mistaken contemporary view
Some claimed that pouring used water into pure water is different from performing wudu in a basin, but the text shows the mixing is identical. The correct position is that both are permissible if used water does not predominate.
The fatwa from Siraj al-Din and other authorities confirms this.

فمنهم من قال يصير الكل مستعملاً عند محمد فيحتاج إلى الفرق بينه وبين بول الشاة فأفاد الفرق بقوله «والفرق له إلى آخره وهي الفائدة الثانية . ومنهم من قال : لا يصير مستعملاً ما لم يغلب على المطلق وصححه صاحب المحيط والعلامة كما رأيت ونقل العلامة عن التحفة أنه المختار . ومنها حمل ما نقله قاضيخان وغيره من نزح عشرين دلواً على القول الضعيف، أما على القول الصحيح فلا ينزح شيء فإذا علمت هذا تعين عليك حمل قول من نقل عدم الجواز على القول الضعيف لا الصحيح كما فعله العلامة وأما ما في كثير من الكتب من أن الجنب إذا أدخل يده أو رجله في الماء فسد الماء فهذا محمول على الرواية القائلة بنجاسة الماء المستعمل لا على المختارة للفتوى لأن ملاقاة النجس للماء القليل تقتضي نجاسته لا ملاقاة الطاهر له، وقد كشف عن هذا ختام المحققين العلامة كمال الدين بن الهمام في شرح الهداية حجاب الأستار فقال : حوضان صغيران يخرج الماء من أحدهما ويدخل في الآخر فتوضأ في خلال ذلك جاز لأنه جار، وكذا إذا قطع الجاري من فوق وقد بقي جري الماء كان جائزاً أن يتوضأ بما يجري في النهر. وذكر في فتاوى قاضيان في المسألة الأولى قال : والماء الذي اجتمع في الحفيرة الثانية فاسد وهذا مطلقاً إنما هو بناء على كون المستعمل نجساً، وكذا كثير من أشباه هذا. فأما على من رواية أنه طاهر غير طهور ،فلا فلتحفظ ليفرع عليها ولا يفتى بمثل هذه الفروع . ا هـ كلام المحقق. ومن هنا يعلم أن فهم المسائل على وجه التحقيق يحتاج إلى معرفة أصلين : أحدهما أن إطلاقات الفقهاء في الغالب مقيدة بقيود يعرفها صاحب الفهم المستقيم الممارس للأصول والفروع وإنما يسكتون عنها اعتماداً على صحة فهم الطالب. والثاني أن هذه المسائل اجتهادية معقولة المعنى لا يعرف الحكم فيها على الوجه التام إلا بمعرفة وجه الحكم الذي بنى عليه وتفرع عنه وإلا فتشتبه المسائل على الطالب ويحار ذهنه فيها لعدم معرفة الوجه والمبنى، ومن أهمل ما ذكرناه حار في الخطأ والغلط . وإذا عرفت هذا ظهر لك ضعف من يقول في عصرنا إن الماء المستعمل إذا صب على الماء المطلق وكأن الماء المطلق غالباً يجوز الوضوء بالكل، وإذا توضأ في فسقية صار الكل مستعملاً إذ لا معنى للفرق بين المسألتين. وما قد يتوهم في الفرق من أن في الوضوء يشيع الاستعمال في الجميع بخلافه في الصب مدفوع بأن الشيوع والاختلاط في الصورتين سواء، بل لقائل أن يقول : إلقاء الغسالة من خارج أقوى تأثيراً من غيره لتعين المستعمل فيه بالمعاينة والتشخيص وتشخص الانفصال. وبالجملة فلا يعقل فرق بين الصورتين من جهة الحكم، فالحاصل أنه يجوز الوضوء من الفساقي الصغار ما لم يغلب على ظنه أن الماء المستعمل أكثر أو مساءٍ ولم يغلب على ظنه وقوع نجاسة قال العلامة قاسم في رسالته : فإن قلت إذا تكرر الاستعمال قد يجمع ويمنع قلت : الظاهر عدم اعتبار هذا المعنى في النجس فكيف بالطاهر. قال في المبتغى يعني بالغين المعجمة . قوم يتوضؤون صفاً على شط النهر جاز فكذا في الحوض لأن حكم ماء الحوض في حكم ماء جار ا هـ بلفظه . قال العبد الضعيف : الظاهر أنه يجمع ويمنع ، وأما ما استشهد به من عبارة المبتغى فلا يمس محل النزاع لأن كلاً منافي الحوض الصغير الذي لا يكون في حكم الجاري، وما في المبتغى مصوّر في الحوض الكبير بدليل قوله لأن حكم ماء الحوض في حكم ماء جار. وقد نقل المحقق العلامة كمال الدين بن الهمام عبارة المبتغى ثم قال : وإنما أراد الحوض الكبير بالضرورة، وأيضاً ما في المبتغى مفرع على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل لا على القول بطهارته بدليل أن الحدادي في شرح القدوري ذكر ما في المبتغى تفريعاً على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل وكلامنا هنا على القول بطهارته . ثم رأيت العلامة ابن أمير حاج في شرحه على منية المصلي قال في قول صاحب المنية وعن الفقيه أبي جعفر لو توضأ في أجمة القصب فإن كان لا يخلص بعضه إلى بعض جاز» ما نصه : وإنما قيد الجواز بالشرط المذكور لأنه لو كان يخلص بعضه إلى بعض لا يجوز كما هو المفهوم المخالف لجواب المسألة لكن على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل، أما على طهارته فلا، بل يجوز ما لم يغلب على ظنه أن القدر الذي يغترفه منه لإسقاط فرض من مسح أو غسل ماء مستعمل أو ماء اختلط بماء مستعمل مساو له أو غالب عليه ا هـ . والأجمة محرك ركة الشجر الكثير الملتف . ثم قال أيضاً : واتصال الزرع بالزرع لا يمنع اتصال الماء بالماء وإن كان مما يخلص فيجوز على الرواية المختارة في طهارة المستعمل بالشرط الذي سلف ولا يجوز على القول بنجاسته ا هـ . ثم ذكر أيضاً مسائل على هذا المنوال وهو صريح فيما قدمناه من جواز الوضوء بالماء الذي به ماء مستعمل قليل، ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره الشيخ سراج الدين قارىء الهداية في فتاويه التي جمعها تلميذه ختام المحققين الكمال بن الهمام بما لفظه : سئل عن فسقية صغيرة يتوضأ فيها الناس وينزل فيه الماء المستعمل وفي كل يوم ينزل فيها ماء جديد، هل يجوز الوضوء فيها؟ أجاب : إذا لم يقع فيها غير الماء المذكور لا يضر ا هـ . يعني إذا وقعت فيها نجاسة تنجست لصغرها ا هـ .
Some of them said that the entire water becomes musta'mal according to Muhammad, so one needs to distinguish between it and the urine of a sheep; so he made the distinction by his statement “and the distinction is for him to the end” and that is the second benefit. And some of them said: it does not become musta'mal unless it overcomes the pure water, and the author of al-Muhit and the 'Allama corrected this, as you have seen, and the 'Allama transmitted from al-Tuhfah that it is the chosen [opinion]. And among that is to interpret what Qadikhan and others transmitted of drawing twenty buckets as being upon the weak opinion; as for the correct opinion, nothing is drawn. So when you know this, it is incumbent upon you to interpret the statement of those who transmitted non-permissibility as being upon the weak opinion, not the correct one, as the 'Allama did. And as for what is in many books that if a junub inserts his hand or foot into water, the water becomes spoiled—this is carried upon the narration that says the used water is najis, not upon the chosen [opinion] for fatwa, because the contact of impurity with a small amount of water necessitates its impurity, not the contact of a pure thing with it. The seal of the verifiers, the 'Allama Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam, uncovered this in Sharh al-Hidayah, Hijab al-Asrar, and said: “Two small basins, water flows out of one and into the other; if he performs wudu in the meantime, it is permissible because it is flowing. Similarly, if the flowing water is cut off from above but the water’s flow remains, it is permissible to perform wudu with what flows in the river.” And he mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan in the first issue: “The water that gathers in the second pit is spoiled, and this is absolutely only based on the premise that the used water is najis, and likewise many similar cases. As for the narration that it is tahir ghayr tahur, then not—so it should be memorized to derive branches from it, and such branches should not be given as fatwa.” End of the words of the verifier. From here it is known that understanding the issues truly requires knowledge of two principles: first, that the general statements of jurists are mostly qualified by restrictions known to the one with sound understanding who practices the principles and branches; they omit them only relying on the correctness of the student’s understanding. Second, that these issues are ijtihadi, rationally meaningful; the ruling cannot be fully known except by knowing the basis on which it was built and from which it branched; otherwise the issues confuse the student and his mind becomes perplexed due to not knowing the basis and foundation. Whoever neglects what we have mentioned will be lost in error and mistake. When you know this, the weakness of whoever says in our time that if used water is poured onto pure water and the pure water is predominant, then wudu is permissible with the whole; but if one performs wudu in a basin, the whole becomes musta'mal—since there is no meaning to the distinction between the two issues—becomes apparent to you. And what may be imagined of a distinction—that in wudu the usage spreads to all, contrary to pouring—is refuted because the spreading and mixing are the same in both cases. Rather, one could say that throwing the washing water from outside has a stronger effect than other [contact] because of the certainty of the used water by sight and identification and the distinct separation. In total, there is no rational distinction between the two forms in terms of ruling. The conclusion is that it is permissible to perform wudu in the small basins as long as one does not strongly think that the used water is more or equal, and one does not strongly think that impurity has fallen. Al-'Allama Qasim said in his epistle: “If you say: when use is repeated, it may accumulate and prevent, I say: it is apparent that this meaning is not considered in impurity, so how about pure?” He said in al-Mubtagha—that is, with a ghayn—: “A group of people performed wudu in a row on the bank of a river; it is permissible, and likewise in a basin, because the ruling of the basin’s water is in the ruling of flowing water.” End of his statement. The weak servant said: “It is apparent that it accumulates and prevents. As for what he cited from the statement of al-Mubtagha, it does not touch the locus of dispute because each [case] is different from the small basin which is not in the ruling of flowing water. What is in al-Mubtagha is depicted in a large basin, evidenced by his saying 'because the ruling of the basin’s water is in the ruling of flowing water.' And the verifier 'Allama Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam transmitted the statement of al-Mubtagha and then said: 'He only meant the large basin necessarily. Also, what is in al-Mubtagha is a branch on the opinion that used water is najis, not on the opinion of its purity, as evidenced by the fact that al-Haddadi in Sharh al-Quduri mentioned what is in al-Mubtagha as a branch on the opinion of impurity of used water, and our discussion here is on the opinion of its purity.' Then I saw the 'Allama Ibn Amir Hajj in his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli, regarding the statement of the author of al-Munya: 'And from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: if he performs wudu in a thicket of reeds, and if some does not reach others, it is permissible.' He said, verbatim: 'He only conditioned permissibility with the mentioned condition because if some reaches others, it is not permissible, as is the understood contrary to the answer of the issue, but upon the opinion of impurity of used water. As for its purity, it is not so; rather it is permissible unless he strongly thinks that the amount he takes from it to perform a fard of wiping or washing is used water or water mixed with used water that is equal to it or predominant over it.' End. Al-Ajjama means, with a fatha, dense intertwined trees. Then he also said: 'The connection of plants with plants does not prevent the connection of water with water; if it penetrates, then it is permissible upon the chosen narration of purity of used water with the condition that passed, and it is not permissible upon the opinion of impurity.' End. Then he also mentioned issues in this vein, and it is explicit in what we have presented of the permissibility of wudu with water that contains a little used water. This is also indicated by what Shaykh Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidaya mentioned in his fatwas, collected by his student the seal of the verifiers al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, verbatim: 'He was asked about a small basin where people perform wudu and used water falls into it, and new water falls into it every day: is it permissible to perform wudu in it?' He answered: 'If nothing other than the mentioned water has fallen into it, it does not harm.' End. Meaning: if impurity falls into it, it becomes impure due to its smallness. End.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of used water (ماء مستعمل) when it mixes with pure water in a basin. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) begins by presenting two intra-Hanafi opinions: the first, attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani, holds that the entire body of water becomes musta'mal if any part is used; the second, which is the corrected and chosen opinion, holds that it does not become musta'mal unless the used water predominates over the pure. The commentator then applies this to the case of a junub inserting a limb—the water does not become spoiled because the contact is with a pure thing, not an impurity. He quotes Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam's example of two connected basins to illustrate that flowing water (even if artificially connected) prevents the spread of impurity. Then he extracts two crucial principles: (1) jurists' general statements are often qualified by implicit conditions; (2) these rulings are based on rational meanings (ma'qul al-ma'na), so one must know the underlying basis. He then refutes a contemporary mistaken view that there is no difference between pouring used water into pure water and performing wudu in a basin, arguing that in both cases the mixing is identical, and the correct view is that wudu is permissible in small basins as long as one does not strongly believe the used water is predominant or that impurity has fallen. He supports this with statements from al-Mubtagha, Ibn Amir Hajj, and a fatwa from Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidaya, all confirming the permissibility with the condition that the used water is not predominant. The commentary firmly establishes the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (mā' musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl, having lost its purifying property (ṭahūr) but remaining pure (ṭāhir) in itself.
المختار (al-mukhtār): The chosen or relied-upon opinion for issuing fatwas, as opposed to weak or rare narrations.
فسقية (faṣqiyyah): A small basin or pool used for performing wudu, often found in mosques.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing wudu in a small basin where used water from previous wudu has collected?
A) Permissible unconditionally
B) Permissible as long as the used water is not predominant and no impurity is known to have fallen
C) Not permissible because the water becomes najis
D) Only permissible if the basin is 10x10 cubits

Key Takeaway
Used water is pure but not purifying; it does not spoil pure water unless it becomes predominant or impurity is known.

Ruling on Stagnant Water Containing Impurity and the 10x10 Condition
Commentary on the matn about stagnant water with impurity and the exception for 10x10.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for performing wudu with stagnant water that contains impurity and identify the size condition that changes the ruling.

Core Idea
Stagnant water less than 10x10 cubits cannot be used for wudu if impurity is present; larger bodies are like flowing water.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on a matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the permissibility of using stagnant (dā'im) water that has come into contact with impurity. The ruling hinges on a single condition: the size of the water body. Understanding this condition and its reasoning is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi school's position on purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the basic ruling
First, recognise the act being ruled upon: using stagnant water for wudu when it contains an impurity (najis). The basic ruling from the matn is that it is not permissible (i.e., wudu is not valid with such water).
The text begins by stating the ruling for water that is not ten by ten.
2
Locate the condition that changes the ruling
Next, identify the exception: 'unless it is ten by ten (10x10 cubits).' If the stagnant water meets this dimension, it is treated like flowing water (kāl-jārī), and the impurity does not render it unusable unless it changes the water's colour, taste, or smell.
The measure is spatial, not volume-based.
3
Understand the underlying reasoning (talil)
The commentator explains the rationale: impurity contaminates the entire small body of water, but a large body (10x10 or more) is like a flowing stream – the quantity dilutes the impurity unless it visibly alters the water. This is supported by two Hanafi riwayahs (narrations) about the nature of used water.
The text mentions 'riwayat al-najasah' and 'riwayat al-taharah' as proof for the similarity.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Be aware that some Hanafi narrations suggest that even small amounts may remain unaffected if the impurity is not visible, but the relied-upon (muftā bihi) position requires the 10x10 size for immunity.
This ikhtilaf is resolved in favour of the 10x10 condition by 'some of our shaykhs'.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
Combine the above: the operative ruling (muftā bihi) is that stagnant water containing impurity is fit for wudu only if the water body is at least 10 cubits by 10 cubits. If smaller, wudu is invalid; if larger, it is permissible provided no change in the water's properties.
This is the position to be relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه غيره أجزأ أو بماء دائم فيه نجس إن لم يكن عشراً في عشر وإلا فهو كالجاري. أي لا يتوضأ بماء ساكن للفرق بين المسألتين قال بعض مشايخنا يدل عليه أنه أيضاً رواية النجاسة فإن النجس ينجس غیره، سواء كان ملقى أو ملاقياً، فكذا على رواية الطهارة. وإذا كان كذلك فليكن التعويل عليه
Or with stagnant water that has impurity in it—if it is not ten by ten, [it is not permissible]; otherwise it is like flowing water. That is, one should not perform wudu with still water due to the difference between the two issues. Some of our shaykhs said: this is indicated by the fact that it is also the narration of impurity, because impurity contaminates something else, whether it is thrown or contacted. Similarly, on the narration of purity. And if it is so, then let it be relied upon.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a brief commentary on a matn statement from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The original matn states that the ruling on stagnant (dā'im) water containing impurity is that it cannot be used for wudu unless it is ten cubits by ten cubits (i.e., 10x10 dhiraʻ) in size; if it meets this dimension, it is considered like flowing water (kāl-jārī) and therefore unaffected by the impurity. The commentator explains that the reason is the difference between a small body of water (which becomes contaminated) and a large one (which is like a flowing river). Some of our shaykhs have indicated that this ruling aligns with the narration that considers used water impure (najis), because impurity contaminates whatever it contacts, whether it is a submerged object or a liquid. Similarly, on the narration that considers used water pure (tahir), the same principle applies—only large quantities are immune. The commentator concludes by stating that this is what should be relied upon (fatwa).

Key Terms
ماء دائم (mā' dā'im): Stagnant or still water that does not flow; also called 'standing water'.
عشر في عشر (ʻashr fī ʻashr): Ten cubits by ten cubits (approx. 5.6 m x 5.6 m, assuming a cubit of about 56 cm). This is the minimum size for stagnant water to be considered like flowing water.
جاري (jārī): Flowing water, which does not become impure by contact with impurity unless the impurity changes its color, taste, or smell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum size for stagnant water to be considered like flowing water in the Hanafi school?
A) Two qullahs (approximately 192 liters)
B) Ten cubits by ten cubits
C) Five cubits by five cubits
D) It must be actively flowing

Key Takeaway
Stagnant water containing impurity is permissible for wudu only if it measures at least 10x10 cubits; otherwise, wudu is invalid.

Wudu from Small Tanks with Used Water
Discussion of wudu from small tanks where used water accumulates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of ghalabat al-zann (predominant opinion) to determine whether wudu is permissible from water mixed with used water in small tanks.

Core Idea
Wudu from small tanks is permissible unless predominant opinion indicates used water is more or equal.

When wudu is performed repeatedly in a small tank, used water accumulates with fresh water. Is wudu still valid? The Hanafi school answers by shifting the criterion from fixed measurements to the individual's predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann). This lesson unpacks that reasoning, showing how the school balances practicality and legal certainty in purity matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act in question is wudu from a small tank (fisqiyyah) where used water falls and mixes with fresh water. The ruling is that wudu is permissible (mubah) as long as a condition is met.
The default ruling is permissibility because used water is considered pure (taahir).
2
Understand the Criterion: Ghalabat al-Zann
The condition for permissibility is that the person does not have a predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) that the water he is using is predominantly used water or equal parts used and fresh. If he does have such an opinion, wudu is not allowed from that water.
This is the Hanafi alternative to fixed measurements like the Shafi'i 'qullatayn'.
3
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Distinction
The passage clarifies that some Hanafis (e.g., al-Haddad) base rulings on the impurity of used water, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that used water is pure. The author follows the majority view of purity.
The difference affects the baseline: on the impurity view, even a little used water would prohibit wudu.
4
Apply the Criterion to the Small Tank Scenario
In a small tank, repeated use may cause used water to accumulate. The Hanafi position is that as long as the person does not predominantly think the used water is more or equal, wudu is valid. The author cites fatwas to reinforce this.
This applies even if used water visibly accumulates, as long as there is no predominant suspicion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه غيره أجزأ أو بماء دائم فيه نجس إن لم يكن عشراً في عشر وإلا فهو كالجاري الصورتين من جهة الحكم، فالحاصل أنه يجوز الوضوء من الفساقي الصغار ما لم يغلب على ظنه أن الماء المستعمل أكثر أو مساءٍ ولم يغلب على ظنه وقوع نجاسة قال العلامة قاسم في رسالته : فإن قلت إذا تكرر الاستعمال قد يجمع ويمنع قلت : الظاهر عدم اعتبار هذا المعنى في النجس فكيف بالطاهر. قال في المبتغى يعني بالغين المعجمة . قوم يتوضؤون صفاً على شط النهر جاز فكذا في الحوض لأن حكم ماء الحوض في حكم ماء جار ا هـ بلفظه . قال العبد الضعيف : الظاهر أنه يجمع ويمنع ، وأما ما استشهد به من عبارة المبتغى فلا يمس محل النزاع لأن كلاً منافي الحوض الصغير الذي لا يكون في حكم الجاري، وما في المبتغى مصوّر في الحوض الكبير بدليل قوله لأن حكم ماء الحوض في حكم ماء جار. وقد نقل المحقق العلامة كمال الدين بن الهمام عبارة المبتغى ثم قال : وإنما أراد الحوض الكبير بالضرورة، وأيضاً ما في المبتغى مفرع على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل لا على القول بطهارته بدليل أن الحدادي في شرح القدوري ذكر ما في المبتغى تفريعاً على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل وكلامنا هنا على القول بطهارته . ثم رأيت العلامة ابن أمير حاج في شرحه على منية المصلي قال في قول صاحب المنية وعن الفقيه أبي جعفر لو توضأ في أجمة القصب فإن كان لا يخلص بعضه إلى بعض جاز» ما نصه : وإنما قيد الجواز بالشرط المذكور لأنه لو كان يخلص بعضه إلى بعض لا يجوز كما هو المفهوم المخالف لجواب المسألة لكن على القول بنجاسة الماء المستعمل، أما على طهارته فلا، بل يجوز ما لم يغلب على ظنه أن القدر الذي يغترفه منه لإسقاط فرض من مسح أو غسل ماء مستعمل أو ماء اختلط بماء مستعمل مساو له أو غالب عليه ا هـ . والأجمة محرك ركة الشجر الكثير الملتف . ثم قال أيضاً : واتصال الزرع بالزرع لا يمنع اتصال الماء بالماء وإن كان مما يخلص فيجوز على الرواية المختارة في طهارة المستعمل بالشرط الذي سلف ولا يجوز على القول بنجاسته ا هـ . ثم ذكر أيضاً مسائل على هذا المنوال وهو صريح فيما قدمناه من جواز الوضوء بالماء الذي به ماء مستعمل قليل، ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره الشيخ سراج الدين قارىء الهداية في فتاويه التي جمعها تلميذه ختام المحققين الكمال بن الهمام بما لفظه : سئل عن فسقية صغيرة يتوضأ فيها الناس وينزل فيه الماء المستعمل وفي كل يوم ينزل فيها ماء جديد، هل يجوز الوضوء فيها؟ أجاب : إذا لم يقع فيها غير الماء المذكور لا يضر ا هـ . يعني إذا وقعت فيها نجاسة تنجست لصغرها ا هـ .
If other than it suffices, or with standing water containing impurity, if it is not ten by ten, otherwise it is like running water in both respects of ruling. The conclusion: it is permissible to perform wudu from small tanks as long as it is not predominant in his opinion that the used water is more or equal, and it is not predominant in his opinion that impurity has fallen. Al-Allamah Qasim said in his treatise: If you say that with repeated use it may accumulate and prevent, I say: Apparently this meaning is not considered in impurity, so how in pure. He said in al-Mubtagha: People performing wudu in a row on the bank of a river is permissible, likewise in a tank because the ruling of the tank water is like the ruling of running water. The weak servant said: Apparently it accumulates and prevents. As for what he cited from the expression of al-Mubtagha, it does not touch the place of dispute because each is contrary to the small tank that is not in the ruling of running water, and what is in al-Mubtagha is depicted in a large tank as evidenced by his saying 'because the ruling of water in a tank is like the ruling of running water.' The investigator Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam transmitted the expression of al-Mubtagha and said: He intended the large tank necessarily. Also, what is in al-Mubtagha is based on the position of impurity of used water, not on its purity, as evidenced by al-Haddad in his commentary on al-Quduri mentioning what is in al-Mubtagha as a branch on the position of impurity of used water, and our discussion here is on the position of its purity. Then I saw al-Allamah Ibn Amir Haj in his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli, regarding the saying of the author of al-Munya: 'From al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: If he performs wudu in a thicket of reeds, if some of it does not reach others, it is permissible.' He said: He only conditioned permissibility with the mentioned condition because if some reached others, it would not be permissible, as understood contrary to the answer of the issue, but on the position of impurity of used water. As for its purity, no, rather it is permissible as long as it is not predominant in his opinion that the amount he scoops for discharging an obligatory act of wiping or washing is used water or water mixed with used water equal to it or prevailing over it. Al-Ajamah is a place with many dense trees. Then he also said: Connection of crops with crops does not prevent connection of water with water, even if it intermingles. So it is permissible on the chosen narration regarding purity of used water under the condition mentioned earlier, and not permissible on the position of its impurity. Then he also mentioned issues along this line, and it is explicit in what we presented of the permissibility of wudu with water in which there is a little used water. It is also indicated by what Shaykh Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidayah mentioned in his fatwas collected by his student, the seal of the verifiers al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, with his wording: He was asked about a small tank in which people perform wudu and used water falls into it, and every day new water falls into it. Is wudu permissible in it? He answered: If nothing other than the mentioned water falls into it, it does not harm. That is, if impurity falls into it, it becomes impure due to its smallness.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling regarding the permissibility of wudu from small tanks (فساقي) where used water (ماء مستعمل) accumulates. The author, after clarifying that the original ruling applies to both cases (using water that has been used and standing water with impurity), concludes that wudu is permissible from small tanks unless the person has a predominant opinion (غلبة الظن) that the used water is more than or equal to the pure water, or that impurity has fallen. He cites various Hanafi authorities to support this position. Al-Allamah Qasim argues that even if used water accumulates, it does not prevent purity, analogously to how a small amount of impurity is not considered. Then the author refutes an argument from al-Mubtagha, explaining that the permission for wudu in a large basin (like a river) does not apply to a small tank because the large basin is in the ruling of running water. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam clarifies that al-Mubtagha's statement referred to a large tank. Furthermore, the author notes that al-Mubtagha's permission is based on the view that used water is impure, while the discussion here assumes used water is pure. Finally, he cites Ibn Amir Haj's commentary, which similarly conditions permissibility on the absence of a predominant opinion that the scooped water is used or mixed with used water. The author concludes by citing a fatwa from Qari' al-Hidayah that explicitly permits wudu in a small tank where used water falls, as long as no impurity enters. This demonstrates that the Hanafi school relies on the principle of غلبة الظن in determining the purity of water mixed with used water, not on fixed measurements.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a ritual purification (wudu or ghusl) and has separated from the limb.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or strong presumption, used as the criterion for determining impurity in water.
فسقية (fisqiyyah): A small tank or cistern used for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the criterion for determining the permissibility of wudu from water that contains used water?
A) A fixed measurement (e.g., 10x10 cubits)
B) The predominant opinion (غلبة الظن) of the person
C) Whether the water has changed in color, taste, or smell
D) The number of people who have used the water

Key Takeaway
Wudu from a small tank containing used water is permissible unless a predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) indicates that the used water is more or equal to the fresh water.

Taharah — Purification
