كتاب الطهارة

فقد علمت أنه ليس مذهب أصحابنا، وأن محمداً وإن كان قدر به رجع الأئمة الثقات الذين هم أعلم بمذهب أصحابنا. فإن قلت: إن في الهداية وكثير من الكتب أن الفتوى على اعتبار العشر في العشر واختاره أصحاب المتون فكيف ساغ لهم ترجيح غير المذهب؟ قلت: لما كان مذهب أبي حنيفة التفويض إلى رأي المبتلى به وكان الرأي يختلف بل من الناس من لا رأي له اعتبر المشايخ العشر في العشر توسعة وتيسيراً على الناس. فإن قلت: هل يعمل بما صح من المذهب أو بفتوى المشايخ؟ قلت: يعمل بما صح من المذهب فقد قال الإمام أبو الليث في نوازله: سئل أبو نصر عن مسألة وردت عليه ما تقول رحمك الله وقعت عندك كتب أربعة: كتاب ابراهيم بن رستم وأدب القاضي عن وكتاب المجرد وكتاب النوادر من جهة هشام فهل يجوز لنا أن نفتي منها أو لا وهذه الكتب محمودة عندك؟ فقال: ما صح عن أصحابنا فذلك علم محبوب مرغوب فيه مرضى به، وأما الفتيا فإني لا أرى لأحد أن يفتي بشيء لا يفهمه ولا يتحمل أثقال الناس، فإن كانت مسائل قد اشتهرت وظهرت وانجلت عن أصحابنا رجوت أ أن يسع الاعتماد عليها في النوازل انتهى. وعلى تقدير عدم رجوع محمد عن هذا التقدير فما قدر به لا يستلزم تقديره به إلا في نظره وهو لا يلزم غيره وهذا لأنه لما وجب كونه ما استكثره المبتلى فاستكثار واحد لا يلزم غيره بل يختلف باختلاف ما يقع في قلب كل إنسان، وليس هذا من قبيل الأمور التي يجب فيها على العامي تقليد المجتهد إليه أشار في فتح القدير ويؤيده ما في شرح الزاهدي عن الحسن وأصح حده ما لا يخلص بعض الماء إلى بعض بظنّ المبتلى به واجتهاده ولا يناظر المجتهد فيه ا هـ . فعلم من هذا أن التقدير بعشر في عشر لا يرجع إلى أصل شرعي يعتمد السنة. فإن قلت: قال في شرح الوقاية وإنما قدر به بناء على قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من حفر بئراً فله حولها أربعون ذراعاً فيكون لها حريمها من كل جانب عشرة ففهم من هذا أنه إذا أراد آخر أن يحفر في حريمها بئر يمنع لأنه ينجذب الماء إليها وينقص الماء في البئر الأولى، وإذا أراد أن يحفر بئر بالوعة يمنع أيضاً لسراية النجاسة إلى البئر الأولى وينجس ماؤها ولا يمنع فيما وراء الحريم وهو عشر في عشر، فعلم أن الشرع اعتبر العشر في العشر في عدم سراية النجاسة حتى لو كانت النجاسة تسري يحكم بالمنع. قلت: هو مردود من أوجه: الأوّل إن كون حريم البئر عشرة أذرع من كل جانب قول البعض والصحيح أربعون من كل جانب كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. الثاني أن قوام الأرض أضعاف قوام الماء فقياسه عليها في مقدار عدم السراية غير مستقيم. الثالث أن المختار المعتمد في البعد بين البالوعة والبئر نفوذ الرائحة إن تغير لونه أو ريحه أو طعمه تنجس وإلا فلا. وهكذا في الخلاصة وفتاوى قاضيخان وغيرهما. وصرح في التتارخانية: أن اعتبار العشر في العشر على اعتبار حال أراضيهم والجواب يختلف باختلاف صلابة الأرض ورخاوتها، وحيث اختار في المتن اعتبار العشر لا بأس بإيراد تفاريعه والتكلم عليها فنقول: اختلف المشايخ في الذراع على ثلاثة أقوال؛ ففي التجنيس المختار ذراع الكرباس، واختلف فيه ففي كثير من الكتب أنه ست قبضات ليس فوق كل قبضة أصبع قائمة فوق أربعة وعشرون أصبعاً بعد حروف «لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله والمراد بالأصبع القائمة ارتفاع الإبهام كما في غاية البيان. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي أن ذراع الكرباس سبع قبضات ليس فوق كل قبضة أصبع قائمة. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان وغيرها الأصح ذراع المساحة وهو سبع قبضات فوق كل قبضة أصبع قائمة. وفي المحيط والكافي: الأصح أنه يعتبر في كل زمان ومكان ذراعهم من غير تعرض للمساحة والكرباس والأقوال الكل في المربع، فإن كان الحوض مدوراً ففي الظهيرية يعتبر ستة وثلاثون وهو الصحيح وهو مبرهن عند الحساب وفي غيرها المختار المفتى به وأربعون كيلاً لعسر رعاية الكسر وفي المحيط الأحوط اعتبار ثمانية وأربعين. وفي فتح القدير: والكل تحكمات غير لازمة إنما الصحيح ما قدمناه من عدم التحكم بتقدير معين. وفي الخلاصة: وصورة الحوض الكبير المقدر بعشرة في عشرة أن يكون من كل جانب من جوانب الحوض عشرة وحول الماء أربعون ذراعاً ووجه الماء مائة ذراع هذا مقدار الطول والعرض ا هـ. وأما العمق ففي الهداية والمعتبر في العمق أن يكون بحال لا ينحسر الصحيح أي لا ينكشف حتى لو انكشف ثم اتصل بعد ذلك لا يتوضأ منه
So you have known that it is not the madhhab of our companions, and that Muhammad, although he estimated it, the trustworthy imams who are more knowledgeable about the madhhab of our companions retracted from it. If you say: In al-Hidayah and many books, the fatwa is on considering ten by ten, and the authors of the matn chose it, so how did they deem it permissible to prefer other than the madhhab? I say: Because the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is to delegate to the opinion of the one afflicted (with impurity), and opinion varies, and among people there is one who has no opinion, so the mashayikh considered ten by ten as an expansion and facilitation for the people. If you say: Should one act upon what is authentic from the madhhab or upon the fatwa of the mashayikh? I say: One should act upon what is authentic from the madhhab, for Imam Abu al-Layth said in his Nawazil: Abu Nasr was asked about a matter that came to him: 'What do you say, may Allah have mercy on you, when four books come to you: the book of Ibrahim ibn Rustam, Adab al-Qadi, al-Mujarrad, and al-Nawadir from Hisham, is it permissible for us to give fatwa from them or not, and these books are praised by you?' He said: 'What is authentic from our companions is beloved, desired, and approved knowledge. As for giving fatwa, I do not think anyone should give a fatwa on something he does not understand, nor bear the burdens of people. If the issues have become well-known, apparent, and clear from our companions, I hope that reliance upon them in incidents is permissible.' End quote. And assuming Muhammad did not retract from this estimation, what he estimated does not necessitate that others estimate the same, but only in his view, and others are not bound by it. This is because when it became necessary to be what the afflicted person considers abundant, the abundance of one does not bind another, but rather it varies according to what falls in the heart of each person. This is not from the matters in which a layman must imitate a mujtahid. This is indicated in Fath al-Qadir, and it is supported by what is in Sharh al-Zahidi from al-Hasan: 'The most correct definition is what does not let some water reach other water according to the assumption and ijtihad of the afflicted person, and the mujtahid is not to be argued with regarding it.' So it is known from this that the estimation of ten by ten does not revert to a textual basis that can be relied upon from the Sunnah. If you say: It is said in Sharh al-Wiqayah that he estimated it based on his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever digs a well has around it forty cubits.' So its precinct becomes ten from each side. From this it is understood that if someone else wants to dig a well in its precinct, he is prevented because the water is attracted to it and the water in the first well decreases. And if he wants to dig a cesspool, he is also prevented because of the transmission of impurity to the first well, and its water becomes impure. And no prevention exists beyond the precinct, which is ten by ten. So it is known that the Law considered ten by ten in the non-transmission of impurity, such that if the impurity would transmit, prevention is ruled. I say: This is rebutted from several aspects: First, that the precinct of the well being ten cubits from each side is the saying of some, and the correct is forty from each side as will come if Allah wills. Second, the consistency of earth is many times that of water, so analogizing it to it in the amount of non-transmission is incorrect. Third, the chosen and relied-upon view regarding the distance between a cesspool and a well is that (if) the odor penetrates and changes its color, smell, or taste, it becomes impure, otherwise not. And this is what is in al-Khulasah, Fatawa Qadikhan, and others. And it is stated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah that considering ten by ten is based on the condition of their lands, and the answer differs according to the hardness and softness of the earth. Since the matn chose to consider ten, there is no harm in presenting its branches and discussing them. So we say: The mashayikh differed concerning the cubit on three opinions. In al-Tajnis, the chosen is the cubit of the cloth (dhirāʿ al-karbās). There is difference: in many books it is six fistfuls with no upright finger above each fistful, making twenty-four fingers after the letters of 'La ilaha illa Allah Muhammad Rasul Allah', and by the upright finger is meant the height of the thumb as in Ghayat al-Bayan. In Fatawa al-Walwaliji, the cubit of cloth is seven fistfuls with no upright finger above each fistful. In Fatawa Qadikhan and others, the most authentic is the surveying cubit (dhirāʿ al-misāḥah), which is seven fistfuls with an upright finger above each fistful. In al-Muhit and al-Kafi, the most authentic is that in every time and place their cubit is considered without specifying surveying or cloth. All these opinions are regarding a square (pool). If the pool is round, in al-Zahiriyyah, thirty-six is considered, and this is correct and proven by calculation; in other books, the chosen and fatwa is forty due to the difficulty of observing fractions; in al-Muhit, the precaution is to consider forty-eight. In Fath al-Qadir, all are arbitrary and not binding; rather the correct is what we have presented of not arbitrating with a specific estimation. In al-Khulasah, the description of a large pool estimated as ten by ten is that each side of the pool is ten, the water's circumference is forty cubits, and the water's face is one hundred cubits—this is the length and width. End quote. As for depth, in al-Hidayah, the considered depth is such that it does not recede, i.e., it does not become exposed, so that if it becomes exposed and then connected after that, one does not perform wudu from it.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the measurement of a well's perimeter (حريم البئر) for preventing impurity transmission. The author first clarifies that the opinion attributing a fixed measurement of 10x10 to the Hanafi madhhab is incorrect; the true madhhab of Abu Hanifa is to leave it to the discretion of the person affected (المبتلى), as their judgment may differ. However, later mashayikh adopted the 10x10 measurement as an easing (توسعة) to help those who have no opinion or are prone to waswasa. The author then addresses an objection citing the hadith 'Whoever digs a well has forty cubits around it' and refutes it with three points: (1) the correct ruling is forty cubits, not ten; (2) earth and water differ in consistency, so analogy is flawed; (3) the correct criterion is the transmission of impurity through smell, color, or taste, not a fixed distance. After establishing that the 10x10 is merely a practical concession, the author moves to its applications: the definition of the cubit (ذراع), different opinions on its length, and the required depth of a pool. The discussion emphasizes that fixed measurements are not part of the original madhhab but were introduced for facilitation.

Key Terms
العشر في العشر (al-‘ashr fī al-‘ashr): A measurement of ten cubits by ten cubits, used as an estimated area for a well's precinct to prevent impurity transmission.
حريم البئر (ḥarīm al-bi’r): The protected area around a well where digging another well or cesspool is prohibited to avoid water depletion or contamination.
ذراع (dhirā‘): A cubit, a unit of length; here discussed as either the cloth cubit (ذراع الكرباس) or surveying cubit (ذراع المساحة), with varying spans of fistfuls and fingers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the author's refutations of the hadith-based argument for 10x10?
A) The correct precinct is forty cubits per side.
B) Earth and water have different consistencies, so analogy fails.
C) The hadith is weak and cannot be used as evidence.
D) The actual criterion is sensory changes, not a fixed distance.

Key Takeaway
The 10x10 measurement for a well's perimeter is a permissive fatwa, but the authoritative Hanafi position delegates the determination to the individual's judgment based on actual impurity transmission.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Principle of Abundance: Ten-by-Ten Cubits and Its Proof
Refutation of a hadith-based argument for the 10x10 measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for water to be considered 'much' (كثير) and explain why the hadith about the well perimeter is not a direct proof for the ten-by-ten basin measure.

Core Idea
The ten-by-ten cubit measure is a legal convention, not derived from the well perimeter hadith.

In Hanafi taharah, water that reaches a certain size is considered 'much' (كثير) and is immune to impurity unless its properties change. The standard measure for a basin is ten cubits by ten cubits. This lesson examines the key proof cited for this measure and its refutation, along with the depth condition required for the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal condition
What is the surface area required for a water basin to be considered 'much'? Find the text that states 'ten by ten' (عشر في عشر).
This measure appears in the Kanz al-Daqa'iq and is the basis of the discussion.
2
Examine the hadith
The author cites a hadith about the perimeter of a well (40 cubits total, 10 from each side). How is this hadith used to argue for the ten-by-ten condition?
The hadith is about the protected area around a well, not directly about water basins.
3
Analyze the refutation
The author refutes the analogy on three grounds. List these grounds and understand why the hadith is not a valid proof for the basin measure.
Main points: (1) The correct perimeter is 40 cubits, not 10; (2) Earth and water have different properties; (3) The relied-upon rule for cesspools is odor penetration, not a fixed distance.
4
Understand the depth condition
Al-Hidayah adds a depth condition: the bottom must not become exposed when water is taken. Al-Bada'i disagrees, stating surface water suffices. Which position is mufta bihi?
The passage indicates that the depth condition from al-Hidayah is relied upon, though al-Bada'i's view is also noted.
5
Recognize the final principle
Despite the refutation, the text accepts the ten-by-ten measure as chosen in the matn. The final ruling: a basin of 10x10 (local cubit) with sufficient depth is 'much' water.
This is the operative rule for fatwa, even though the proof is not the hadith.

كتاب الطهارة
ثلاثة
أنه من حفر بئراً فله حولها أربعون ذراعاً فيكون له حريمها من كل جانب عشرة»(۱) ففهم من هذا أنه إذا أراد آخر أن يحفر في حريمها بئر يمنع لأنه ينجذب الماء إليها وينقص الماء في البئر الأولى، وإذا أراد أن يحفر بئر بالوعة يمنع أيضاً لسراية النجاسة إلى البئر الأولى وينجس ماؤها ولا يمنع فيما وراء الحريم وهو عشر في عشر، فعلم أن الشرع اعتبر العشر في العشر في عدم سراية النجاسة حتى لو كانت النجاسة تسري يحكم بالمنع . قلت: هو مردود من أوجه : الأوّل إن كون حريم البئر عشرة أذرع من كل جانب قول البعض والصحيح أربعون من كل جانب كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. الثاني أن قوام الأرض أضعاف قوام الماء فقياسه عليها في مقدار عدم السراية غير مستقيم. الثالث أن المختار المعتمد في البعد بين البالوعة والبئر نفوذ الرائحة إن تغير لونه أو ريحه أو طعمه تنجس وإلا فلا. وهكذا في الخلاصة وفتاوى قاضيخان وغيرهما. وصرح في التتارخانية : أن اعتبار العشر في العشر على اعتبار حال أراضيهم والجواب يختلف باختلاف صلابة الأرض ورخاوتها، وحيث اختار في المتن اعتبار العشر لا بأس بإيراد تفاريعه والتكلم عليها فنقول : اختلف المشايخ في الذراع على ثلاثة أقوال؛ ففي التجنيس المختار ذراع الكرباس، واختلف فيه ففي كثير من الكتب أنه ست قبضات ليس فوق كل قبضة أصبع قائمة فوق أربعة وعشرون أصبعاً بعد حروف «لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله والمراد بالأصبع القائمة ارتفاع الإبهام كما في غاية البيان .
وفي فتاوى الولوالجي أن ذراع الكرباس سبع قبضات ليس فوق كل قبضة أصبع قائمة. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان وغيرها الأصح ذراع المساحة وهو سبع قبضات فوق كل قبضة أصبع قائمة. وفي المحيط والكافي : الأصح أنه يعتبر في كل زمان ومكان ذراعهم من غير تعرض للمساحة والكرباس والأقوال الكل في المربع، فإن كان الحوض مدوراً ففي الظهيرية ستة يعتبر ستة وثلاثون وهو الصحيح وهو مبرهن عند الحساب وفي غيرها المختار المفتى به وأربعون كيلاً لعسر رعاية الكسر وفي المحيط الأحوط اعتبار ثمانية وأربعين. وفي فتح القدير : والكل تحكمات غير لازمة إنما الصحيح ما قدمناه من عدم التحكم بتقدير معين . وفي الخلاصة : وصورة الحوض الكبير المقدر بعشرة في عشرة أن يكون من كل جانب من جوانب الحوض عشرة وحول الماء أربعون ذراعاً ووجه الماء مائة ذراع هذا مقدار الطول والعرض ا هـ. وأما العمق ففي الهداية والمعتبر في العمق أن يكون بحال لا ينحسر الصحيح أي لا ينكشف حتى لو انكشف ثم اتصل بعد ذلك لا يتوضأ منه بالاغتراف هو ساغ لهم الخروج عن ذلك المقال، كيف وقد اعترف بأن أكثر تفاريعهم على اعتبار العشر في العشر 
(۱) رواه ابن ماجه في كتاب الرهون باب ۲۲ البخاري في كتاب المساقات باب ٣.
وعليه الفتوى، كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي البدائع : إذا أخذا الماء وجه الأرض يكفي ولا تقدير فيه في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح ا هـ . وهو الأوجه لما عرف من أصل أبي حنيفة . وفي الفتاوى : غدير كبير لا يكون فيه الماء في الصيف وتروث فيه الدواب والناس ثم يملأ ورفع منه الجمد إن كان الماء الذي يدخله يدخل على مكان نجس فالماء والجمد في الشتاء نجس وإن كان كثيراً بعد ذلك، وإن كان دخل في مكان طاهر واستقر فيه حتى صار عشراً في عشر ثم انتهى إلى النجاسة فالماء والجمد طاهران ا هـ . وهذا بناء على ما ذكروا من أن الماء النجس إذا دخل على ماء الحوض الكبير لا ينجسه وإن كان الماء النجس غالباً على الحوض لأن كل ما يتصل بالحوض الكبير يصير منه فيحكم بطهارته، وعلى هذا فماء بركة الفيل بالقاهرة طاهر إذا كان ممره طاهراً أو أكثر ممره على ما عرف في ماء السطح لأنها لا تجف كلها بل لا يزال بها غدير عظيم، فلو أن الداخل اجتمع قبل أن يصل إلى ذلك الماء الكثير بها في مكان نجس حتى صار عشراً في عشر ثم اتصل بذلك الماء الكثير كان الكل طاهراً. هذا إذا كان الغدير الباقي محكوماً بطهارته، كذا في فتح القدير. وفي التنجيس : وإذا كان الماء له طول وعمق وليس له عرض ولو قدر يصير عشراً في عشر فلا بأس بالوضوء فيه تيسيراً على المسلمين، ثم العبرة لحالة الوقوع فإن نقص بعده لا ينجس وعلى العكس لا يطهر، ولذا صحح في الاختيار وغيره ما في التنجيس. قال في فتح القدير : وهذا تفريع على التقدير بعشر ولو فرعنا على الأصح ينبغي أن يعتبر أكبر الرأي لو ضم ومثله لو كان له عمق بلا سعة ولو بسط بلغ عشراً في عشر اختلف فيه ومنهم من صحح جعله كثيراً والأوجه خلافه لأن مدار الكثرة عند أبي حنيفة على تحكيم الرأي في عدم خلوص النجاسة إلى الجانب الآخر، وعند تقارب الجوانب لا شك في غلبة الخلوص إليه والاستعمال إنما هو من السطح لا من العمق، وبهذا يظهر ضعف ما اختاره في الاختيار لأنه إذا لم يكن له عرض فأقرب الأمور الحكم بوصول النجاسة إلى الجانب الآخر من عرضه وبه خالف حكم الكثير إذ ليس حكم الكثير تنجس الجانب الآخر بسقوطها في مقابله بدون تغير وأنت إذا حققت الأصل الذي بيناه قبلت ما وافقه وتركت ما خالفه ا هـ. وقد يقال إن هذا وإن كان الأوجه إلا أن المشايخ وسعوا الأمر على الناس وقالوا بالضم كما أشار إليه في التنجيس بقوله تيسيراً على المسلمين.
وفي التنجيس : الحوض إذا كان أعلاه عشراً في عشر وأسفله أقل من ذلك وهو ممتلىء

Book of Purification. Three. That whoever digs a well, around it he has forty cubits, so its perimeter is ten from each side. So it is understood from this that if another wants to dig a well in its perimeter, he is prevented because the water is attracted to it and the water in the first well decreases, and if he wants to dig a cesspool well, he is also prevented due to the transmission of impurity to the first well and its water becomes impure. And he is not prevented beyond the perimeter, which is ten by ten. So it is known that the Law considered ten by ten in the non-transmission of impurity, so that if the impurity were to transmit, the ruling of prevention is given. I say: it is refutable from aspects: First, that the perimeter of the well being ten cubits from each side is the saying of some, and the correct is forty from each side as will come. Second, that the substance of earth is many times the substance of water, so analogizing it to it in the measure of non-transmission is not correct. Third, that the chosen and relied-upon in the distance between the cesspool and the well is the penetration of odor; if its color, smell, or taste changes, it becomes impure, otherwise no. Thus in al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadikhan and others. And it is explicitly stated in al-TatarKhaniyya: that considering ten by ten is based on the condition of their lands, and the answer differs according to the hardness or softness of the earth. And since the text chose considering ten, there is no harm in presenting its branches and discussing them. So we say: The mashayikh differed regarding the cubit into three sayings: In al-Tajnis, the chosen is the cubit of cloth, and they differed in it: in many books it is six fists with no erect finger above each fist, and it is twenty-four fingers after the letters 'La ilaha illa Allah Muhammad Rasul Allah', and the meaning of 'erect finger' is the height of the thumb as in Ghayat al-Bayan. In Fatawa al-Walwalji: the cubit of cloth is seven fists with no erect finger above each fist. In Fatawa Qadikhan and others: the most correct is the surveyor's cubit, which is seven fists with an erect finger above each fist. In al-Muhit and al-Kafi: the most correct is that in every time and place their cubit is considered without specifying surveyor or cloth. All sayings are regarding the square. If the basin is round, then in al-Zahiriyya six, thirty-six is considered, which is the correct and is proven in calculation; in others the chosen and mufta bihi is forty cubits due to the difficulty of observing fractions; in al-Muhit the most precautionary is considering forty-eight. In Fath al-Qadir: all are arbitrary and not binding; rather the correct is what we previously mentioned of not being arbitrary with a specific estimation. In al-Khulasa: The description of the large basin estimated as ten by ten is that from each side of the basin there is ten, and around the water forty cubits, and the face of the water is one hundred cubits; this is the measure of length and width. As for depth: in al-Hidaya, what is considered in depth is that it be such that it does not recede, i.e., it does not become uncovered, so that if it becomes uncovered and then connects afterwards, one does not perform wudu from it by scooping. They allowed themselves to depart from that saying, indeed he admitted that most of their branches are on considering ten by ten. (1) Narrated by Ibn Majah in the Book of Ruhun, chapter 22; al-Bukhari in the Book of Musaqat, chapter 3. And upon it is the fatwa, thus in Mi'raj al-Diraya. In al-Bada'i: If water is taken from the surface of the earth, it suffices and there is no estimation in the apparent narration, and it is the correct. And it is the most appropriate due to what is known from the principle of Abu Hanifa. In al-Fatawa: A large ghadir that has no water in summer and animals and people defecate in it, then it fills and ice is taken from it: if the water that enters it enters upon a impure place, the water and ice are impure even if it is many after that; and if it entered upon a pure place and settled in it until it became ten by ten and then reached the impurity, the water and ice are pure. This is based on their statement that impure water entering the large basin does not make it impure even if the impure water is dominant over the basin, because everything connected to the large basin becomes part of it and is ruled pure. Based on this, the water of Baraka al-Fil in Cairo is pure if its path is pure or most of its path is as known in roof water because it does not all dry up; indeed there always remains a great ghadir. So if the entering water collects before reaching that abundant water in an impure place until it becomes ten by ten, then connects to that abundant water, all is pure. This is if the remaining ghadir is ruled pure, thus in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Tanqih: If water has length and depth and no width, and if it were valued it would become ten by ten, there is no harm in performing wudu in it as a facilitation for Muslims. Then the consideration is for the state of occurrence: if it decreases afterwards it does not become impure, and conversely it does not become pure. Therefore al-Ikhtiyar and others corrected what is in al-Tanqih. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This is a branch on estimation by ten. If we branch on the most correct, it should be considered: the greater opinion if combined; similarly if it has depth without width, and if spread would reach ten by ten, there is disagreement. Some corrected making it much, but the more appropriate is contrary to that because the basis of abundance according to Abu Hanifa is judgment of opinion in non-penetration of impurity to the other side. When sides are close, there is no doubt of the preponderance of penetration to it. Use is only from the surface, not from depth. By this the weakness of what al-Ikhtiyar chose is apparent. Because if there is no width, the nearest thing is ruling that impurity reaches the other side of its width, and by this it differs from the ruling of much water, because the ruling of much water is not that the other side becomes impure by its fall opposite it without change. And if you verify the principle we have explained, you accept what agrees with it and leave what opposes it. It may be said that although this is the more appropriate, the mashayikh made it easy for the people and said with combination, as indicated in al-Tanqih by his saying 'as a facilitation for Muslims.' In al-Tanqih: The basin, if its top is ten by ten and its bottom is less than that, and it is full. His saying: (and therefore corrected etc.) Look at the meaning of this statement. His saying: (and this) i.e., what is in al-Tanqih. His saying: 'and use is only from the surface, not from depth' this looks to his saying 'and similarly if it has depth without width.' His saying: (and by this the weakness of what al-Ikhtiyar chose appears) i.e., by his saying 'and use is only from the surface, not from depth', the weakness appears of what al-Ikhtiyar chose in correcting what is in al-Tanqih regarding considering depth and length.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the condition for a water basin to be considered 'plentiful' (كثير) in Hanafi fiqh, specifically addressing the ten-by-ten cubit measure. The discussion begins by citing a hadith about digging a well with a forty-cubit perimeter, from which the author draws an analogy that the Law considers ten-by-ten as a measure below which impurity can spread. However, the author immediately refutes this analogy on three grounds: first, the correct perimeter is forty cubits, not ten; second, earth and water have different properties; third, the relied-upon position is that the distance between a well and a cesspool is determined by odor penetration, not by a fixed measure. Hence, the ten-by-ten measure for a water basin is not firmly established by this hadith, but the author accepts it as the chosen view in the base text (al-Kanz) and proceeds to discuss its branches. The core legal principle is that water in a basin measuring ten by ten cubits (however the cubit is defined) is considered 'much' (كثير) such that it cannot be made impure by the mere addition of impurity unless one of its three properties (color, taste, smell) changes. The passage then details the differing definitions of the cubit among Hanafi scholars: some prefer the cloth cubit (6 or 7 fists), others the surveyor's cubit (7 fists with a thumb), and still others say the local cubit should be used. For a round basin, the area is recalculated into square cubits. The depth requirement is that the bottom must not become exposed when water is taken; if it does, the water loses its immunity. Later, the passage discusses the ruling on a large pool (ghadir) that dries and is later refilled, emphasizing that if the incoming water passes through a pure place and becomes ten-by-ten before reaching the impurity, the whole is pure. It also addresses water with length and depth but no width, where later scholars (mutakhkhirin) permitted wudu as a facilitation, though Ibn al-Humann in Fath al-Qadir argues this is weak. The overall approach is to derive a clear, practical rule while acknowledging differing opinions among Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms
عشر في عشر (ashr fi ashr): A measure of ten cubits by ten cubits, meaning the surface area of a water basin that makes it considered 'much' (كثير) in Hanafi fiqh.
حريم البئر (harim al-bi'r): The protected area around a well, typically 40 cubits (or 10 from each side) that cannot be dug or used for cesspools.
ذراع الكرباس (dhira' al-karbas): The cubit of cloth, varying in definition (6 or 7 fists, with or without an erect finger).
ذراع المساحة (dhira' al-misaha): The surveyor's cubit, typically 7 fists with an erect finger (thumb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the hadith about digging a well (with 40-cubit perimeter) does not directly prove the ten-by-ten basin measure?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot be used as proof.
B) The hadith is about the well's protected area, not about water immunity.
C) The hadith says forty cubits, not ten.
D) The hadith was abrogated by later revelation.

Key Takeaway
The measure of ten by ten cubits for a 'large' water basin is a legal convention accepted in the Hanafi school, but its proof is not the hadith about the well perimeter.

Purity of Water from a Replenishing Pond
Ruling with proof on water and ice purity from a pond that dries and refills

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which water and ice from a pond that has dried and refilled are considered pure according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Pure path + sufficient quantity = pure water, even after contamination.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common scenario: a large pond dries up in summer, becomes fouled by animals, then refills in winter. The ruling distinguishes between two cases based on how the incoming water meets the impurity. Understanding this requires careful application of the Hanafi principle that a large body of water (kathir) does not become impure by mere contact unless it changes. Let us unpack the conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: one where the incoming water passes over an impure place before settling, and another where it settles in a pure place and reaches a specific quantity before encountering impurity. Identify each.
The key differentiator is the state of the path and whether the water reaches 10x10 cubits before contact with impurity.
2
Apply the quantity condition
In the second case, the water must become 'ten by ten' (10x10 cubits) in a pure place before it reaches the impurity. Once it attains that quantity, it is considered kathir and ruling changes.
This is the Hanafi threshold for 'much water' (kathir).
3
Understand the principle of connection
The commentator explains that when water connects to a large basin, it becomes part of it and is ruled pure. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle that a large body of water neutralises small amounts of impurity.
This principle is applied to the water of the famous Pond of the Elephant in Cairo.
4
Apply to the Cairo pond
The passage concludes that the water of the pond of the elephant is pure if its incoming water travels a pure path, because the pond never dries completely and always has a large residual body of water.
The condition is that the remaining pond water itself is ruled pure.

وفي الفتاوى : غدير كبير لا يكون فيه الماء في الصيف وتروث فيه الدواب والناس ثم يملأ ورفع منه الجمد إن كان الماء الذي يدخله يدخل على مكان نجس فالماء والجمد في الشتاء نجس وإن كان كثيراً بعد ذلك، وإن كان دخل في مكان طاهر واستقر فيه حتى صار عشراً في عشر ثم انتهى إلى النجاسة فالماء والجمد طاهران ا هـ . وهذا بناء على ما ذكروا من أن الماء النجس إذا دخل على ماء الحوض الكبير لا ينجسه وإن كان الماء النجس غالباً على الحوض لأن كل ما يتصل بالحوض الكبير يصير منه فيحكم بطهارته، وعلى هذا فماء بركة الفيل بالقاهرة طاهر إذا كان ممره طاهراً أو أكثر ممره على ما عرف في ماء السطح لأنها لا تجف كلها بل لا يزال بها غدير عظيم، فلو أن الداخل اجتمع قبل أن يصل إلى ذلك الماء الكثير بها في مكان نجس حتى صار عشراً في عشر ثم اتصل بذلك الماء الكثير كان الكل طاهراً. هذا إذا كان الغدير الباقي محكوماً بطهارته، كذا في فتح القدير.
And in al-Fatawa: A large pond that has no water in summer and animals and people dung in it, then it fills and ice is taken from it. If the water that enters passes over a impure place, then the water and ice in winter are impure, even if [the water] becomes much after that. And if it entered a pure place and settled there until it became ten by ten, then reached the impurity, then the water and ice are pure. End quote. This is based on what they mentioned: that impure water entering the water of a large basin does not make it impure, even if the impure water is dominant over the basin, because everything connected to the large basin becomes part of it and is ruled pure. And on this basis, the water of the pond of the elephant in Cairo is pure if its path is pure or most of its path, as known in roof water, because it does not completely dry but always has a great pond. So if the entering water gathered before reaching that abundant water in an impure place until it became ten by ten, then connected to that abundant water, it is all pure. This is if the remaining pond is ruled pure, as in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a large pond that dries up in summer, becomes fouled by animals, then refills. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios for the incoming water: if it passes over an impure place before settling, then both the water and the ice formed from it are impure even if the water later becomes abundant. But if the incoming water settles in a pure place and reaches the quantity of 10x10 cubits before encountering the impurity, then both water and ice are pure. The commentator explains that this ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that impure water entering a large basin does not render it impure because everything connected to a large body of water becomes part of it and is ruled pure. He then applies this to the famous Pond of the Elephant in Cairo, stating its water is pure if the path of the water is pure, as it never completely dries. The condition is that the residual pond water is itself ruled pure.

Key Terms
غدير كبير (ghadir kabir): A large pond or body of water that does not completely dry up, considered kathir (abundant water) in Hanafi fiqh
الجمد (al-jamad): Ice that forms from water; its ruling follows that of the water it came from
عشراً في عشر (asharan fi ashar): The Hanafi threshold for abundant (kathir) water: an area of 10 by 10 cubits

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on water and ice if the incoming water first passes over an impure place, even if the pond later contains abundant water?
A) The water and ice are pure because the pond becomes large.
B) The water and ice are impure because the initial contact determines the ruling.
C) The water is pure but the ice is impure.
D) The ruling depends on whether the ice is removed.

Key Takeaway
The purity of water from a refilling pond depends on the path and quantity of the incoming water before it contacts the impurity, not on the final volume.

Does Length and Depth Make Water Kathir? The Hanafi Dispute on Surface Area Criterion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on water's abundance criterion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for kathir water (tahkim al-ra'y) and explain why water with only length and depth is not considered kathir in the more correct view.

Core Idea
In Hanafi purity law, the key to abundant water is the surface area, not volume: if impurity can cross to the opposite side, the water is not kathir.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about a narrow channel of water that has length and depth but negligible width. While some later scholars allowed wudu from it as a concession (taysir), the more analytically rigorous position, rooted in Imam Abu Hanifa's original criterion, holds that such water is not kathir because impurity will inevitably reach the other side. We will trace the argument and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptional water case
This water has length and depth but no observable width, like a narrow channel or a deep well with a tiny opening. The question is whether its total volume (if spread out to 10x10 cubits) qualifies it as kathir.
2
Locate the dispute: two Hanafi positions
Al-Tanjis and al-Ikhtiyar permit wudu from such water as a concession (taysiran ala al-muslimin). Fath al-Qadir argues this is incorrect; the more correct (al-awjah) is that it is not kathir.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf resolved by later scholars (mashayikh) in favor of concession.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's criterion: Tahkim al-Ra'y
Imam Abu Hanifa defined kathir water as water that, by reasonable estimation (tahkim al-ra'y), does not allow impurity to reach the opposite side when it falls on one side. This is a context-sensitive test, not a fixed volume.
This criterion is unique to Abu Hanifa; later Hanafis adopted a fixed 10x10 cubit measurement.
4
Apply the criterion to the narrow channel
In a water body with no width, the sides are close together. Impurity falling on one side will undoubtedly reach the other side because of the narrow width. Depth does not prevent lateral spread, and use (isti'mal) is only from the surface.
Thus, such water fails the tahkim al-ra'y test and should be considered qalil (small), not kathir.
5
Explain the concession (taysir) and its status
Despite the more correct view, later mashayikh adopted the lenient position (considering it kathir by combining dimensions) to avoid hardship. This became the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) for ease of the community.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle of taysir and the hierarchy of fatwa (zahir al-riwayah vs. fatawa mutakhkhirin).

وفي التنجيس : وإذا كان الماء له طول وعمق وليس له عرض ولو قدر يصير عشراً في عشر فلا بأس بالوضوء فيه تيسيراً على المسلمين، ثم العبرة لحالة الوقوع فإن نقص بعده لا ينجس وعلى العكس لا يطهر، ولذا صحح في الاختيار وغيره ما في التنجيس. قال في فتح القدير : وهذا تفريع على التقدير بعشر ولو فرعنا على الأصح ينبغي أن يعتبر أكبر الرأي لو ضم ومثله لو كان له عمق بلا سعة ولو بسط بلغ عشراً في عشر اختلف فيه ومنهم من صحح جعله كثيراً والأوجه خلافه لأن مدار الكثرة عند أبي حنيفة على تحكيم الرأي في عدم خلوص النجاسة إلى الجانب الآخر، وعند تقارب الجوانب لا شك في غلبة الخلوص إليه والاستعمال إنما هو من السطح لا من العمق، وبهذا يظهر ضعف ما اختاره في الاختيار لأنه إذا لم يكن له عرض فأقرب الأمور الحكم بوصول النجاسة إلى الجانب الآخر من عرضه وبه خالف حكم الكثير إذ ليس حكم الكثير تنجس الجانب الآخر بسقوطها في مقابله بدون تغير وأنت إذا حققت الأصل الذي بيناه قبلت ما وافقه وتركت ما خالفه ا هـ. وقد يقال إن هذا وإن كان الأوجه إلا أن المشايخ وسعوا الأمر على الناس وقالوا بالضم كما أشار إليه في التنجيس بقوله تيسيراً على المسلمين.
And in al-Tanjis: If water has length and depth but no width, even if measured it would become ten by ten, there is no harm in performing wudu with it, as a concession to Muslims. Then the consideration is at the moment of occurrence: if it decreases afterwards it does not become impure, and conversely it does not become pure. Therefore, in al-Ikhtiyar and others, they declared as correct what is in al-Tanjis. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This is a branch of the estimation of ten. And if we base it on the more correct, one should consider the greater opinion if combined. Similarly, if it has depth without width, even if spread out it would reach ten by ten, there is disagreement. Some declared it as much (kathir), but the more correct is otherwise, because the criterion for muchness according to Abu Hanifa is the judgment of the opinion that the impurity does not reach the other side. And when the sides are close, there is no doubt of the prevalence of reaching. And use (of water) is only from the surface, not from the depth. By this, the weakness of what was chosen in al-Ikhtiyar becomes apparent, because if it has no width, the nearest thing is to rule that the impurity reaches the other side in its width, and thereby it differs from the ruling of much water, for the ruling of much water is not that the other side becomes impure by its falling opposite without change. And if you realize the principle we have explained, you accept what agrees and leave what contradicts. End quote. And it may be said that this, although more correct, the mashayikh made it easy for the people and said to combine (consider it as), as indicated in al-Tanjis by his statement 'as a concession to Muslims.'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about water that has length and depth but no significant width (e.g., a narrow channel). If its total volume, if spread out, would be 10x10 cubits, can it be considered kathir (abundant water) that does not become impure by mere contact? The author of al-Tanjis allows wudu from it as a concession (taysir). The author of al-Ikhtiyar concurred. However, the author of Fath al-Qadir critiques this, arguing that the true criterion for kathir according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that impurity does not reach the opposite side of the body of water. In a narrow channel with no width, impurity will inevitably reach across its width. Moreover, use (isti'mal) is only from the surface, not the depth, so even if there is depth, it does not help. Thus, the correct view is that such water is not kathir. Nevertheless, later scholars (mashayikh) made a concession for people and allowed considering it as kathir by 'combining' (al-damm) dimensions, as mentioned in al-Tanjis with the phrase 'taysiran ala al-muslimin'.

Key Terms
تحكيم الرأي (tahkim al-ra'y): The criterion for abundant water (kathir) at Abu Hanifa: a judgment based on reasonable assessment that impurity cannot reach the opposite side of the water body
تيسيراً على المسلمين (taysiran ala al-muslimin): A concession for the ease of Muslims, indicating that a ruling may be relaxed despite the more correct view

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Fath al-Qadir argue that water with length and depth but no width is NOT kathir?
A) Because its volume is less than 10x10 cubits.
B) Because impurity will reach the other side due to narrow width, and use is from the surface.
C) Because depth does not count in Hanafi fiqh.
D) Because the water is not flowing.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the criterion for kathir water is not volume but the reasonable assessment that impurity cannot cross to the opposite side; depth and length do not compensate for narrow width.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Hawd with Top 10x10 and Narrower Bottom
Ruling on direct wudu in a basin with large top but narrow bottom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a basin with a narrow bottom is considered abundant water (kathir) and determine when direct wudu in it is valid.

Core Idea
A basin is considered abundant based on its surface area, not depth; the top must be at least 10x10 cubits.

Imagine a large basin that is wide at the top but tapers to a narrow base. At first glance, it seems to hold a lot of water, but the Hanafi fiqh ruling on its water status depends on a specific dimension: the surface area. This lesson examines the classical ruling from al-Tanjis and the commentary that clarifies the critical factor: the surface, not the depth, determines whether the water is abundant (kathir) or little (qalil). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly performing wudu in such basins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object and its dimensions
The passage describes a basin (hawd) whose top is ten by ten cubits and whose bottom is less than that. Also, the basin is full, meaning the water reaches the top surface.
The top measurement is the criterion.
2
State the ruling for the full basin
When the basin is full, it is permissible to perform wudu and ghusl directly in it, even though the bottom is narrower.
This is because the surface area is at least 10x10, making the water kathir.
3
Identify the condition that changes the ruling
If the water level drops so that the surface becomes less than ten by ten (even if there is still depth below), then direct wudu in the basin is invalid.
The water is now qalil, like small quantity that is easily polluted.
4
Derive the alternative method
When the surface is less than 10x10, one must scoop water from the basin (scoop with the hand or a vessel) and perform wudu outside the basin.
Scooping is permissible as long as the water is still pure.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the principle that a body of water is considered abundant (kathir) only by its surface expanse, not by its depth. Depth without surface width does not change the water's status.
This principle is confirmed by the commentator's refutation of the view in al-Ikhtiyar that considered depth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التنجيس : الحوض إذا كان أعلاه عشراً في عشر وأسفله أقل من ذلك وهو ممتلىء اهـ. قوله : (ولذا صحح الخ) انظر ما معنى هذا الكلام قوله : ( وهذا) أي ما في التنجيس. قوله : والاستعمال إنما هو من السطح لا من العمق هذا ناظر إلى قوله ومثله لو كان له عمق بلا سعة. قوله : ( وبهذا يظهر ضعف ما اختاره في الاختيار أي بقوله والاستعمال إنما هو من السطح لا من العمق يظهر ضعف ما اختاره في الاختيار من تصحيح ما في التنجيس من اعتبار العمق والطول. يجوز التوضؤ فيه والاغتسال فيه، وإن نقص الماء حتى صار أقل من عشرة في عشرة لا يتوضأ فيه ولكن يغترف منه ويتوضأ
And in al-Tanjis: A basin whose top is ten by ten and whose bottom is less than that, and it is full. End quote. His statement: (And therefore they declared as correct...) Look at the meaning of this speech. His statement: (And this) meaning what is in al-Tanjis. His statement: And use is only from the surface, not from the depth – this looks to his statement: 'And similarly if it has depth without width.' His statement: (And by this appears the weakness of what was chosen in al-Ikhtiyar) meaning by his statement 'And use is only from the surface, not from the depth' appears the weakness of what was chosen in al-Ikhtiyar of declaring as correct what is in al-Tanjis regarding considering depth and length. It is permissible to perform wudu in it and to bathe in it. And if the water decreases until it becomes less than ten by ten, one does not perform wudu in it, but one scoops from it and performs wudu.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Tanjis about a basin (hawd) that is 10x10 cubits at the top but narrower at the bottom, and it is full. The commentator inserts an explanation (قوله) clarifying the earlier discussion about depth and width, but the main ruling is: it is permissible to make wudu and ghusl in such a basin. However, if the water level drops so that the surface area becomes less than 10x10, then one cannot perform wudu directly in it, but may scoop water from it and perform wudu elsewhere. This distinguishes between the water being considered kathir at the surface and being qalil (little) when the surface decreases. The interjected commentary is a refutation of the view in al-Ikhtiyar that considered depth and length without surface width.

Key Terms
يوضأ فيه (yuwadda' fihi): To perform wudu by taking water directly from the basin in the normal manner

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can one perform wudu directly in a basin that is 10x10 at the top but narrower at the bottom?
A) Only when the basin is completely full
B) When the surface area is 10x10, even if the bottom is narrower
C) Only when the water level is above the narrower part
D) Never, because the bottom is narrower

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines water abundance (kathir) by the surface expanse, not depth; a basin with a 10x10 top allows direct wudu even if the bottom narrows, but once the surface shrinks below 10x10, scooping is required.
